% ============================================================
%  Section 9: Checkpoint Selection via Tabular SARSA
% ============================================================
\section{Checkpoint Selection via Tabular SARSA}\label{sec:sarsa}

The training pipeline produces a sequence of parameter checkpoints
$\theta_0, \theta_1, \ldots, \theta_N$ during gradient descent.
The question of which checkpoint to deploy---and which to continue
training from---is a model selection problem.
We show that this problem is \emph{tabular} reinforcement learning,
specifically SARSA, with no function approximation required.

\subsection{The RLHF stress test}

The boundary LLM $\Embed$ (Definition~\ref{def:epp}) translates
natural language to mathematical ASCII.
We deliberately choose a heavily RLHF-aligned model
(e.g., ChatGPT) for this role.
This is not despite the RLHF biases but \emph{because of them}.

\begin{proposition}[Robustness to boundary bias]\label{prop:rlhf}
Let $\Embed_{\mathrm{RLHF}}$ be a boundary LLM with
systematic RLHF-induced biases in mathematical translation.
The gated pipeline
$\Pullback \circ \cG \circ \Mirror_\theta \circ \Embed_{\mathrm{RLHF}}$
produces correct mathematical output whenever:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*),nosep]
\item $\Embed_{\mathrm{RLHF}}$ produces a syntactically valid
  mathematical expression (even if it mistranslates intent), and
\item the verification gate $\cG$ accepts the mirror's output.
\end{enumerate}
RLHF biases affect \emph{what question is asked}, not
\emph{whether the answer is correct}.
The verification gate is invariant under boundary bias.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The gate $\cG$ operates on the mathematical content of
$\Mirror_\theta(\Embed(q))$, not on the boundary translation
itself.
By Theorem~\ref{thm:soundness}, if $\cG$ accepts, the
output is correct.
The RLHF-biased LLM may mistranslate the user's intent
(an $\Embed$ failure, visible to the user), but cannot
cause the mirror to produce incorrect verified output.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the worst LLM is the best test]
A heavily RLHF-aligned model is the \emph{stress test}
at the translation boundary.
If the architecture produces correct verified output even
when the boundary translator has systematic biases---refusing
certain mathematical content, rephrasing inputs, adding
unnecessary caveats---then the verification gate is doing its job.
The more biased the boundary LLM, the harder the test.
Passing it proves the architecture is robust.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The multi-LLM court}

Model improvement requires evaluating which checkpoints
produce better outputs.
A single evaluator introduces systematic bias.
We use a \emph{court} of diverse LLMs that produce
\emph{rankings} (ordinal), not \emph{scores} (cardinal).

\begin{definition}[Multi-LLM court]\label{def:court}
Let $\{J_1, J_2, \ldots, J_K\}$ be a panel of $K$ diverse
LLMs serving as judges.
Given a set of candidate outputs
$\{o_1, \ldots, o_n\}$ from different model checkpoints
on the same test query, each judge $J_k$ produces
a ranking $\pi_k \in S_n$ (a permutation of $\{1, \ldots, n\}$).
The aggregated ranking is computed by Borda count:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:borda}
\mathrm{score}(o_i) = \sum_{k=1}^{K} (n - \pi_k(i)),
\qquad
\pi^* = \mathrm{argsort}(\mathrm{score}).
\end{equation}
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Bias cancellation]\label{prop:condorcet}
If the judges' ranking errors are independent and each
judge is correct with probability $p > 1/2$ on each
pairwise comparison, then by Condorcet's jury theorem,
the majority ranking converges to the correct ordering
as $K \to \infty$.
In particular, RLHF-induced biases that are uncorrelated
across judges cancel in the aggregation.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}
Rankings are preferred over scores because:
(i)~ordinal comparisons are more reliable than cardinal
ones for LLM judges;
(ii)~rankings are invariant under monotone transformations
of individual judge scales;
(iii)~Borda aggregation is computable in $O(nK)$.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Checkpoints as states: tabular SARSA}

The key observation is that training produces a \emph{finite}
set of checkpoints.
This makes the model selection problem \emph{tabular}.

\begin{definition}[Checkpoint MDP]\label{def:checkpoint-mdp}
The checkpoint Markov decision process is the tuple
$(\cS, \cA, R, P)$ where:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $\cS = \{\theta_0, \theta_1, \ldots, \theta_N\}$
  is the finite set of saved parameter checkpoints;
\item $\cA = \{\text{continue}, \text{branch}, \text{deploy}\}$
  is the finite action set;
\item $R(\theta_i) = \mathrm{rank}(\theta_i)$ is the reward,
  computed by the multi-LLM court
  (Definition~\ref{def:court}) on the checkpoint's outputs;
\item $P(\theta_j \mid \theta_i, a)$ is the transition
  probability (deterministic for SGD: continuing from
  $\theta_i$ yields $\theta_{i+1}$).
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Tabular SARSA for checkpoint selection]\label{thm:sarsa}
The checkpoint selection problem
(Definition~\ref{def:checkpoint-mdp})
is a finite-state, finite-action MDP solvable by
tabular SARSA\@:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sarsa}
Q(\theta_t, a_t) \leftarrow Q(\theta_t, a_t)
  + \alpha \bigl[R(\theta_t) + \gamma \, Q(\theta_{t+1}, a_{t+1})
  - Q(\theta_t, a_t)\bigr],
\end{equation}
where $\alpha$ is the learning rate, $\gamma$ is the
discount factor, and $Q : \cS \times \cA \to \R$ is the
action-value table.
No function approximation is required.
The Q-table has $|\cS| \times |\cA| = O(N)$ entries.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The state space is $\{\theta_0, \ldots, \theta_N\}$, finite
by construction (we save $N$ checkpoints).
The action space is finite.
The reward is well-defined (the court produces a ranking
for each checkpoint's outputs).
Standard SARSA convergence guarantees apply to finite MDPs
under appropriate step-size schedules~\cite{SB18}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The only RL is tabular RL]\label{rem:tabular}
Deep RL approximates the Q-function with a neural network
because the state space is too large for a table.
Here the state space \emph{is} a table: $N$ checkpoints,
each a snapshot of the parameters.
There is no need to approximate---the Q-values are
computed exactly from the court's rankings.
This is reinforcement learning in its original, clean form:
\emph{tabular}, \emph{symbolic} (rankings are ordinal symbols,
not continuous scores), and \emph{convergent}
(finite MDP with bounded rewards).
Everything beyond tabular RL is function approximation.
The checkpoint MDP needs no approximation.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The self selects its own states]
The ``self'' of the model is its parameter state~$\theta$.
Different checkpoints are different selves.
The court ranks these selves by their outputs---by what
they \emph{do}, not what they \emph{are}.
The selected checkpoint is the self that produces the
highest-ranked mathematical output.
This is model selection without meta-learning:
the selves compete, the court judges, the best self continues.
\end{remark}

% ============================================================
%  Section 10: The Model Context Pipeline
% ============================================================
\section{The Model Context Pipeline}\label{sec:mcp}

The three servers described in this paper---arXiv source
(\S\ref{sec:arxiv-curriculum}), multi-LLM court
(\S\ref{sec:sarsa}), and training orchestrator---compose
into a directed graph that we call the
\emph{Model Context Pipeline} (MCP).

\begin{definition}[Model Context Pipeline]\label{def:mcp}
The MCP is a directed graph $G = (N, E)$ with three server
nodes and typed edges:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $N_1$ = \texttt{arxiv-source}: fetches papers,
  extracts theorem-proof pairs, produces masked training
  examples (Definition~\ref{def:fitb}).
\item $N_2$ = \texttt{llm-court}: panel of $K$ diverse LLM
  judges producing Borda-aggregated rankings
  (Definition~\ref{def:court}).
\item $N_3$ = \texttt{mirror-train}: training orchestrator
  with SARSA checkpoint scheduler
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:sarsa}).
\end{itemize}
The edges carry typed data:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(E\arabic*),nosep]
\item $N_1 \xrightarrow{\text{training examples}} N_3$:
  masked theorem-proof pairs enter the training loop.
\item $N_3 \xrightarrow{\text{checkpoint outputs}} N_2$:
  model outputs from candidate checkpoints are submitted
  for court evaluation.
\item $N_2 \xrightarrow{\text{Borda rankings}} N_3$:
  aggregated rankings serve as the SARSA reward signal,
  closing the feedback loop.
\end{enumerate}
External inputs: arXiv API (to $N_1$), LLM APIs (to $N_2$).
External output: \texttt{proofed.pdf} (from $N_3$).
\end{definition}

\begin{figure}[ht]
\centering
\begin{tikzpicture}[>=Stealth,
  server/.style={draw, rounded corners=3pt, thick,
    inner sep=8pt, minimum height=1.4cm,
    align=center, font=\small},
  ext/.style={draw, dashed, rounded corners=3pt,
    inner sep=5pt, font=\scriptsize, text=gray},
  arr/.style={->, thick},
  elab/.style={font=\scriptsize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt}]

% Server nodes (triangle)
\node[server, fill=orange!10] (N1) at (0, 3) {$N_1$\\arXiv Source};
\node[server, fill=red!12]    (N2) at (5, 0) {$N_2$\\LLM Court};
\node[server, fill=green!10]  (N3) at (0, 0) {$N_3$\\Mirror Train};

% Edges
\draw[arr] (N1) -- node[elab, left]{(E1) training examples} (N3);
\draw[arr] (N3) to[bend left=12] node[elab, above]{(E2) checkpoint outputs} (N2);
\draw[arr] (N2) to[bend left=12] node[elab, below]{(E3) Borda rankings} (N3);

% External inputs
\node[ext] (arxiv) at (-2.5, 3) {arXiv API};
\node[ext] (llm)   at (7.5, 0)  {LLM APIs};
\node[ext] (pdf)   at (0, -1.8)  {\texttt{proofed.pdf}};

\draw[arr, dashed, gray] (arxiv) -- (N1);
\draw[arr, dashed, gray] (llm) -- (N2);
\draw[arr, dashed, gray] (N3) -- (pdf);

\end{tikzpicture}
\caption{The Model Context Pipeline.
  Three servers form a closed training loop.
  External inputs enter at the arXiv and LLM boundaries;
  the external output is a compiled proof document.}
\label{fig:mcp}
\end{figure}

\begin{proposition}[Pipeline convergence]\label{prop:mcp-converge}
The MCP loop converges when the SARSA Q-values stabilize.
Formally, let $\Delta_t = \max_{s,a} |Q_{t+1}(s,a) - Q_t(s,a)|$.
Under the standard SARSA step-size schedule
$\sum_t \alpha_t = \infty$, $\sum_t \alpha_t^2 < \infty$,
we have $\Delta_t \to 0$, and the recommended action
for each checkpoint state becomes stationary.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The state space $\cS$ and action space $\cA$ are finite
(Definition~\ref{def:checkpoint-mdp}).
The reward is bounded (Borda scores are in $[0, K(n-1)]$).
Standard SARSA convergence for finite MDPs~\cite{SB18}
gives $Q_t \to Q^*$ almost surely,
hence $\Delta_t \to 0$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Runtime specification}\label{sec:runtime}

The runtime test is the end-to-end pipeline from a mathematical
query to a compiled proof document.

\begin{definition}[Runtime test]\label{def:runtime}
The runtime pipeline is:
\[
q \xrightarrow{\Embed} m \xrightarrow{\Mirror_\theta} r
  \xrightarrow{\cG} \hat{r}
  \xrightarrow{\text{to\_latex}} \texttt{proofed.tex}
  \xrightarrow{\texttt{latexmk}} \texttt{proofed.pdf}.
\]
The test passes if and only if:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*),nosep]
\item \texttt{latexmk} exits with code $0$ (syntactic correctness),
\item the multi-LLM court ranks the output above a random
  baseline (semantic quality),
\item the verification gate accepts the output
  (mathematical correctness).
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Three levels of checking]\label{rem:three-checks}
The three conditions in Definition~\ref{def:runtime}
correspond to three levels:
\emph{compilation} = syntactic check (is it valid LaTeX?),
\emph{court} = semantic check (is the proof meaningful?),
\emph{gate} = correctness check (is it mathematically true?).
A random string fails (a); a plausible-looking but wrong proof
fails (c); a correct but poorly structured proof fails (b).
All three must pass.
\end{remark}

% ============================================================
%  Section 11: Experiments (Planned)
% ============================================================
\section{Experiments}\label{sec:experiments}

We outline the experimental program for validating the
Math Mirror architecture.
The experiments are organized in order of the build phases.

\subsection{Bootstrap data statistics (Phase 1)}

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Generate $N = 10^6$ training examples using the eight
  generators (Definition~\ref{def:dist}).
\item Report: number of examples per generator, rejection rate
  (examples that fail verification), average expression length,
  character frequency distribution over $\cV$.
\item Hypothesis: rejection rate $< 0.1\%$ (generators produce
  correct examples by construction; rejections arise from
  edge cases in SymPy parsing).
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Model convergence (Phase 2)}

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Train the Math Mirror (Definition~\ref{def:model})
  on verified data for $E$ epochs.
\item Report: training loss curve, bits-per-byte on held-out
  verified data, convergence time.
\item Hypothesis: convergence to $< 1.0$ bits-per-byte on
  in-distribution verified math within $10^4$ gradient steps.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Verified accuracy (Phase 3)}

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Generate $10^4$ test queries across all generator categories.
\item For each query, run the mirror and the verification gate.
\item Report: \emph{verified accuracy} (fraction of outputs that
  pass $\cG$ and are correct) and \emph{coverage}
  (fraction of queries for which the mirror produces any output
  that passes $\cG$).
\item Hypothesis: verified accuracy $= 100\%$ (by construction,
  anything that passes $\cG$ is correct).
  Coverage will be $< 100\%$ (the mirror may produce outputs
  that $\cG$ rejects even when a correct answer exists).
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Comparison: mirror vs.\ raw LLM (Phase 4)}

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Select a benchmark of $10^3$ mathematical questions
  spanning arithmetic, algebra, calculus, and linear algebra.
\item Compare: (a) raw LLM output (no verification),
  (b) mirror output (with verification gate),
  (c) mirror output with LLM boundary translation.
\item Report: accuracy (checked by $\cG$), hallucination rate
  (outputs that look correct but fail $\cG$), latency.
\item Hypothesis: the mirror has lower hallucination rate
  (zero within verified domain) but potentially lower coverage
  (may refuse to answer some questions).
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Finetuning experiments (Phase 5)}

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Submit $n = 100$ user-provided examples spanning a
  specific mathematical domain (e.g., trigonometric identities).
\item Train on accepted examples (Definition~\ref{def:finetune}).
\item Measure improvement in coverage on held-out queries
  from the same domain.
\item Verify: no leakage of information from the user's
  conversation history into the model's outputs.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Go instantiation: PYTHON the AlphaGo (Phase 6)}\label{sec:go}

The architecture is substrate-independent.
Math Mirror uses a 256-byte lattice (Definition~\ref{def:vocab}).
Go uses an $N \times N$ board lattice with
$N \in \{5, 7, 11, 13, 17, 19, 23, 29, 31\}$ expanding during training
(\S\ref{sec:expanding}).
The $V(T,B)$ protocol (Definition~\ref{def:vtb}) is identical;
only the lattice changes.
This subsection exhibits Go as a second instantiation of
embed-prove-pullback.

\begin{definition}[Goer--Thinker--Valuer triple]\label{def:gtv}
The Go instantiation of embed-prove-pullback
(Definition~\ref{def:epp}) is a triple $(G_o, T_h, V_a)$:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Goer} ($= \Mirror_\theta$):
  AlphaGo/KataGo.
  Fast tactical computation via MCTS on the board lattice.
  A frozen MLP---deterministic gauge field
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:gauge}).
  Operates \emph{within} the lattice.
\item \textbf{Thinker} ($=$ LLM boundary):
  Slow strategic reasoning.
  Operates \emph{on} a pool~$\cP$ of strategic frameworks
  (joseki patterns, influence maps, endgame heuristics).
  Selects which evaluation framework to apply.
\item \textbf{Valuer} ($=$ verification gate~$\cG$):
  Scores the trajectory.
  Did the strategy produce a win?
  Updates the pool~$\cP$.
\end{itemize}
The colour convention (Remark~\ref{rem:color}) applies:
\textbf{Green} $=$ Thinker (potential gain, strategic depth);
\textbf{Red} $=$ Valuer (potential loss, rejects bad strategies);
\textbf{Blue} $=$ Goer (routing, tactical moves);
\textbf{BW} $=$ board position (input) and stone placement (output).
\end{definition}

\begin{algorithm}[ht]
\caption{MOPL --- Meta-Optimal Policy Learning
  \textup{[Online Projected Verification Descent]}}\label{alg:mopl}
\begin{algorithmic}[1]
\Require Board state $b_t \in \{-1,0,1\}^{N \times N}$,
  pool~$\cP$ with weights $\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$,
  temperature $\tau_{\mathrm{IR}} \in \mathbb{R}_{>0}$
\Ensure Stone placement $a_t \in \{1,\ldots,N\}^2$,
  updated pool~$\cP$
\State \textsc{Seed}: sample framework $F \sim \softmax\!\bigl(\log \bar{w} / \tau_{\mathrm{IR}}\bigr)$
  \Comment{Thinker picks strategy}
\State \textsc{Embed}: LLM describes $b_t$ in terms of $F$
  \Comment{$\Embed(b_t \mid F)$}
\State \textsc{Goer}: KataGo generates top-$k$ candidate moves $\{a^{(i)}\}_{i=1}^k$
  \Comment{$\Mirror_\theta(b_t)$}
\State \textsc{Think}: LLM evaluates candidates against $F$, ranks
  \Comment{strategic filter}
\State \textsc{Verify}: confirm $a_t$ is a legal move
  \Comment{$\cG$ (legality check)}
\State \textsc{Play}: place stone $a_t$
\State \textsc{Value}: after game ends, update
  $\bar{w}_F \gets (\bar{w}_F \cdot n_F + o)\, / \,(n_F + 1)$
  \Comment{running average}
\end{algorithmic}
\end{algorithm}

This \emph{is} online projected verification descent
(Definition~\ref{def:opvd}):
each game is one gradient step,
the pool~$\cP$ is the parameter~$\theta$,
the Valuer is the gate~$\cG$.
Convergence follows from Theorem~\ref{thm:converge}
with the board lattice replacing the byte lattice.

\begin{remark}[Isomorphism table]\label{rem:go-iso}
The slot-by-slot correspondence:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Math Mirror} & \textbf{Go (MOPL)} \\
\midrule
Byte lattice $|\cV| = 256$ & Board lattice $19 \times 19$ \\
$\Mirror_\theta$ (forward pass) & Goer (MCTS) \\
LLM Embed / Pullback & Thinker (strategic LLM) \\
Verification gate $\cG$ & Valuer (trajectory score) \\
Proof & Game record \\
\texttt{devil\_check} & Win/loss $+$ strategy score \\
Second law $\langle W \rangle \geq 0$ & Pool improves on average \\
Fixed lattice $|\cV| = 256$ & Expanding lattice $\Lambda_R = \{5, 7, 11, 13, 17, 19, 23, 29, 31\}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
Rogers: learning $=$ copying with chance.
The pool copies (joseki, professional games, AlphaGo's own outputs).
The seed randomizes.
The valuer selects.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Why meta-policy beats fixed policy]\label{rem:meta-policy}
AlphaGo is a frozen gauge field---deterministic,
cannot update mid-game.
MOPL is an online optimizer
(Definition~\ref{def:opvd}, Theorem~\ref{thm:converge})---updates
every move.
Over many games, $V_t \to v^*$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:converge}(iii)):
the pool accumulates opponent-specific tactics.
The first stone (randomized opening framework) sets the
strategic direction.
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}执黑先行。\end{CJK}
\end{remark}

% ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
%  MOPL Triangle: three-phase roadmap
% ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The MOPL triangle}\label{sec:mopl-triangle}

The Go instantiation splits into three phases with distinct
computational roles.
The phases form a \emph{triangle}, not a hierarchy:
each vertex has an independent convergence guarantee,
and the Drunk is the origin from which Queen and King
are excitations.
Table~\ref{tab:mopl-triangle} summarises the comparison;
Figure~\ref{fig:drunk-flow} shows the data-flow pipeline.

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\small
\caption{The three MOPL phases at a glance.}\label{tab:mopl-triangle}
\begin{tabular}{@{}l l l l@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Phase~0: Drunk}
& \textbf{Phase~1: Queen}
& \textbf{Phase~2: King} \\
\midrule
\textbf{Section}
  & \S\ref{sec:drunk-game}
  & \S\ref{sec:queens-gambit}
  & \S\ref{sec:kings-control} \\
\textbf{Algorithm}
  & Alg.~\ref{alg:drunk-calibration}
  & Alg.~\ref{alg:queen}
  & Alg.~\ref{alg:king} \\
\textbf{Role}
  & Calibrate $\mu_N$
  & Optimise $\bar{w} > \mu_N$
  & Enforce $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$ \\
\textbf{Learning}
  & None (coin $+$ uniform)
  & Running average (SLLN)
  & SGD in log-space \\
\textbf{Model}
  & Model-free ($\cF = \cX$)
  & Forward FP (model-based)
  & Backward HJB (model-based) \\
\textbf{Output}
  & Base measure $(\hat{p}_c, \hat{\kappa}, \hat{\sigma})$
  & Trained pool $\bar{w}$
  & Temperatures $(\tau^*_{\mathrm{UV}}, \tau^*_{\mathrm{IR}})$ \\
\textbf{Data}
  & $M$ self-play games
  & All $n$ games
  & Last $H$ games (window) \\
\textbf{Convergence}
  & $O(1/\!\sqrt{M})$ SLLN
  & $O(1/\!\sqrt{n})$ SLLN
  & Geometric, $\gamma \approx 1 - 1/H$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Degenerations.}\;
King at $\tau \to \infty$ (pure exploration) $=$ Drunk.
Queen at learning rate $\eta \to 0$ (no updates) $=$ Drunk.
The Drunk is the intersection of both degenerations---the
origin of the (learning, optimisation) plane.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Orthogonality.}\;
Queen updates $\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$;
King updates $(\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}, \tau_{\mathrm{UV}}) \in \mathbb{R}_{>0}^2$.
Disjoint parameter coordinates.
Errors are additive, not multiplicative.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Data flow.}\;
Drunk $\to$ Queen (base measure $\mu_N$)
$\to$ King (pool state $\bar{w}$).
A sequential pipeline: each phase reads only
the output of its predecessor.

% ── Three-phase pipeline diagram ──
\begin{figure}[ht]
\centering
\input{figures/drunk_flow}
\caption{The three-phase MOPL pipeline.
  Phase~0 (Drunk) calibrates the base measure~$\mu_N$.
  Phase~1 (Queen) optimises the pool $\bar{w}$ above~$\mu_N$.
  Phase~2 (King) enforces $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$ while
  the Queen optimises.
  Arrows show data flow; the Drunk's output is the input
  to both Queen and King.}\label{fig:drunk-flow}
\end{figure}

\subsection{The Drunk Game: ground state calibration (Phase~0)}%
\label{sec:drunk-game}

Before optimising, we must calibrate.
The Queen (\S\ref{sec:queens-gambit} below) and the King
(\S\ref{sec:kings-control} below) both require a
\emph{base measure}: what does the board produce under
zero intelligence?
Standard Go has three strategic decisions per turn:
\emph{who} plays (turn order),
\emph{whether} to play (pass vs.\ place), and
\emph{where} to play (intersection choice).
Phase~0 constructs a game that preserves the turn
structure but replaces each strategic decision with an
independent random variable,
\emph{transcommuting} complexity with stochasticity.
Ownership is earned \emph{a posteriori} by action alone.

\begin{definition}[%
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}醉局\end{CJK}
--- the Drunk Game]\label{def:drunk-game}
Fix $N \in \N$.
The \emph{Drunk Game} on the $N \times N$ lattice graph
$G = (V, E)$, $|V| = N^2$, is defined by:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item \textbf{Players.}
  Two players: Black (B) and White (W).
  Colours are assigned, as in standard Go.
\item \textbf{Turn order.}
  Fixed alternation
  $\mathrm{B\text{--}W\text{--}B\text{--}W\text{--}}\cdots$
  (deterministic, identical to standard Go).
\item \textbf{Coin flip.}
  At each turn, the active player flips a fair coin
  ($p = \tfrac{1}{2}$).
  Heads: place a stone.
  Tails: skip (forfeit the turn).
  This replaces the strategic \emph{whether} decision.
\item \textbf{Placement.}
  If placing, the position is drawn uniformly at random
  from the set of empty intersections.
  This replaces the strategic \emph{where} decision.
\item \textbf{Stones.}
  All stones on the board are \emph{visually identical}:
  no colour markings.
  The game record tracks which player placed each stone,
  but this information is invisible during play.
  Ownership is not colour; ownership is \emph{action}.
\item \textbf{Closure event.}
  If the placed stone at~$v$ completes a simple closed
  curve $\gamma \subset G$ (a cycle in the stone graph),
  the player who placed~$v$ scores
  $|\mathrm{int}(\gamma)|$ (the number of interior
  vertices).
  All boundary stones of $\gamma$ are marked with that
  player's identity.
  Ownership is \emph{post-hoc}: it exists only after closure.
\item \textbf{Terminal.}
  The game ends when the board is full or both players
  skip in succession.
  Higher cumulative score wins.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{algorithm}[ht]
\caption{Drunk Walk
  \textup{[Self-Variational Optimal Transport Sampling]}}\label{alg:drunk-walk}
\begin{algorithmic}[1]
\Require Board size $N \in \mathbb{N}$,
  coin probability $p = \tfrac{1}{2}$
\Ensure Game record $\omega \sim \rho^*_N$,
  scores $s^B, s^W \in \mathbb{N}_0$
\State $O \gets \varnothing$
  \Comment{occupied set $O \subseteq V = \{1,\ldots,N\}^2$}
\State $s^B, s^W \gets 0,\, 0$;\;
  $\textit{skips} \gets 0$
\For{$t = 1, 2, \ldots$}
  \State $\textit{player} \gets
    \begin{cases} B & t \text{ odd} \\ W & t \text{ even}
    \end{cases}$
    \Comment{deterministic alternation}
  \State $c_t \sim \mathrm{Bernoulli}(p)$
    \Comment{\textsc{Whether}: coin flip}
  \If{$c_t = 0$ or $V \setminus O = \varnothing$}
    \State $\textit{skips} \gets \textit{skips} + 1$
      \Comment{skip}
  \Else
    \State $v_t \sim \mathrm{Uniform}(V \setminus O)$
      \Comment{\textsc{Where}: random placement}
    \State $O \gets O \cup \{v_t\}$;\;
      $\textit{skips} \gets 0$
    \State $\Gamma \gets
      \textsc{FloodFill}(V,\, O)$
      \Comment{new enclosed regions}
    \If{$\Gamma \neq \varnothing$}
      \State $s^{\textit{player}} \gets
        s^{\textit{player}} + |\mathrm{int}(\Gamma)|$
        \Comment{\textsc{Closure}: score interior}
    \EndIf
  \EndIf
  \If{$\textit{skips} \geq 2$}
    \State \textbf{break}
      \Comment{two consecutive skips $\Rightarrow$ terminal}
  \EndIf
\EndFor
\State \Return $(s^B, s^W)$, game record $\omega$
\end{algorithmic}
\end{algorithm}

\noindent
The three \textsc{small-caps} labels mark the three
axes of the transcommutation
(Remark~\ref{rem:transcommutation}):
\textsc{Whether} (coin), \textsc{Where} (dice),
and \textsc{Closure} (topology).
The first two are random; the third is deterministic.
The product is $\rho^*_N$
(Definition~\ref{def:svot}).

\begin{remark}[Transcommutation: complexity
  $\leftrightarrow$ randomness]%
\label{rem:transcommutation}
\color{black!60}%
The passage from standard Go to the Drunk Game is a
\emph{basis change}, not a simplification.
Every strategic decision axis in standard Go is
independently mapped to a random variable;
the scoring topology is preserved as an invariant:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Decision axis} & \textbf{Standard Go} &
\textbf{Drunk Go} & \textbf{Change} \\
\midrule
Who (turn order) &
  B--W alternation &
  B--W alternation &
  None (invariant) \\
Whether (play/skip) &
  Strategic (pass is rare) &
  Coin flip ($p = \tfrac{1}{2}$) &
  Strategy $\to$ Bernoulli \\
Where (placement) &
  Strategic ($\sim\!10^{170}$ choices) &
  Uniform random &
  Strategy $\to$ uniform \\
Scoring &
  Territory (colour-dependent) &
  Closure (topology-dependent) &
  Label $\to$ action \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The turn structure is \emph{preserved}---both games are
B--W--B--W with the same alternation.
The strategic complexity is \emph{transcommuted} into
stochasticity: each decision that was a function of
the game state becomes an independent random variable.
The total information is conserved in the scoring
topology---closure detects the same geometric structure
whether the stones were placed by strategy or by dice.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The self-dual point.}\;
The coin flip probability $p = \tfrac{1}{2}$ is not a
parameter choice---it is the unique value at which
the game is self-dual.
At $p = \tfrac{1}{2}$, the expected number of stones
placed by Black equals the expected number placed by
White (both $\sim N^2/4$ per player).
The forward density of placed stones and the backward
prediction of closure probability are governed by the
same measure:
\[
  \Pr[\text{site occupied}]
  \;=\;
  \Pr[\text{site empty}]
  \;=\;
  \tfrac{1}{2}\,.
\]
This is the game-theoretic functional equation
$\cF_t = \cB_{T-t}$, realised as Bernoulli site
percolation at the symmetric point.
The coin is fair.  The game is its own dual.
Not by tuning---by construction.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The uncertainty principle.}\;
The transcommutation obeys a conservation law:
\[
  \Delta(\text{strategy})
  \;\times\;
  \Delta(\text{randomness})
  \;\geq\;
  \mathrm{const}(\text{topology}).
\]
Standard Go: $\Delta(\text{strategy})$ is maximal
($\sim\!10^{170}$),
$\Delta(\text{randomness}) = 0$.
Drunk Go: $\Delta(\text{strategy}) = 0$,
$\Delta(\text{randomness})$ is maximal ($\tfrac{1}{2}$
per site).
The product---the closure topology---is preserved.
Complexity did not disappear.
It changed representation.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Transcommutation (free energy preservation)]%
\label{def:transcommutation}
Let $S$ be a system with \emph{free energy}
(Jaynes~\cite{Jaynes57}):
\[
  F(\tau) \;=\; \min_p \;\bigl[\,
    \underbrace{\mathbb{E}_p[\,E\,]}_{\text{energy (order)}}
    \;+\;
    \tau\,
    \underbrace{H(p)}_{\text{entropy (disorder)}}
  \,\bigr].
\]
A \emph{transcommutation} is a transformation $T$ that
preserves~$F$ while redistributing the energy--entropy
decomposition:
\[
  F(T \cdot S) \;=\; F(S),
  \qquad
  \mathbb{E}[E] \;\leftrightarrow\; \tau\, H.
\]
The uncertainty principle follows:
\[
  \Delta(\text{energy}) \;\times\; \Delta(\text{entropy})
  \;\geq\; \mathrm{const}(F).
\]
At the \emph{self-dual point}
($\mathbb{E}[E] = \tau H$),
the transformation is an involution
and the system is its own transcommutation.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Instances.}\;
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Domain} & \textbf{Conjugate pair} &
\textbf{Transform} & \textbf{Self-dual point} \\
\midrule
Stat.\ mech.\ \cite{KW41} &
  high-$T$ $\leftrightarrow$ low-$T$ &
  Kramers--Wannier &
  $T_c$ (critical) \\
Thermodynamics &
  $(S,\, T)$ &
  Legendre: $F = E - TS$ &
  $E = TS$ \\
Quantum mech.\ &
  $(x,\, p)$ &
  Fourier &
  Gaussian ($\Delta x = \Delta p$) \\
This paper &
  strategy $\leftrightarrow$ randomness &
  Drunk Game &
  $p = \tfrac{1}{2}$ (fair coin) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The word is literal:
\emph{trans-} (across) $+$ \emph{commutation} ($[A, B]$).
The map goes from one side of the commutator
to the other, preserving the commutator itself.
In each instance above, the non-commutativity of the
conjugate pair is the structure that forces the
uncertainty bound.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Redundancy threshold.}\;
The free energy defines a threshold for consistency:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Below} (transcommutational):
  $F(R_1) = F(R_2)$.
  The representations differ only in encoding.
  Convention, not contradiction.
\item \textbf{Above} (semantic):
  $F(R_1) \neq F(R_2)$.
  The invariant itself has changed.
  Must be resolved.
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Primon Gas: $\zeta(s)$ as partition function]%
\label{rem:primon-gas}
The Euler product
$\zeta(s)^{-1} = \prod_p(1-p^{-s})$
used throughout this paper
(Remarks~\ref{rem:lattice-criterion},
\ref{rem:pool-library},
and~\ref{rem:euler-vision})
is a statement of statistical independence.
Assign to each prime~$p$ a bosonic oscillator with energy
$\varepsilon_p = \log p$ and Hamiltonian
\[
  H \;=\; \sum_{p\;\mathrm{prime}} (\log p)\;
  a_p^\dagger\, a_p.
\]
The partition function at inverse temperature~$s$ is
\[
  Z(s)
  \;=\; \mathrm{Tr}\bigl(e^{-sH}\bigr)
  \;=\; \prod_{p}\,\sum_{k=0}^{\infty} p^{-sk}
  \;=\; \prod_{p} \frac{1}{1 - p^{-s}}
  \;=\; \zeta(s).
\]
This is the \emph{Primon Gas}~\cite{Julia90}:
unique prime factorisation
$\Leftrightarrow$
statistical independence of oscillators.

Equivalently, the coherent-state path integral over
bosonic fields $\bar\phi_p(\tau), \phi_p(\tau)$ gives
\[
  \zeta(s)
  \;=\; \int \mathcal{D}\bar\phi\,\mathcal{D}\phi\;
  \exp\!\Bigl(-\sum_{p}\int_{0}^{s}
  \bar\phi_p(\partial_\tau + \log p)\,\phi_p\;d\tau\Bigr).
\]
The Gaussian integral evaluates to
$\prod_p \det(\partial_\tau + \log p)^{-1}
= \prod_p(1-p^{-s})^{-1}$,
recovering the Euler product.
This is transcommutation at the computational level:
the deterministic complexity of prime-by-prime
multiplication is exchanged for stochastic summation
over all field configurations, with $\zeta(s)$
(the free energy) invariant.

The functional equation
$\xi(s) = \xi(1-s)$
is a transcommutation
(Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation}):
it preserves the completed free energy~$\xi$
while swapping $s \leftrightarrow 1-s$
(high-temperature $\leftrightarrow$ low-temperature,
cf.\ Kramers--Wannier~\cite{KW41}).
The critical line $\mathrm{Re}(s) = \tfrac{1}{2}$
is the self-dual point of this duality.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Self-dual game]\label{def:self-dual}
A two-player game~$\Gamma$ with state evolution operator
$\cF_t$ (forward) and value prediction operator
$\cB_t$ (backward) is \emph{self-dual} if
\[
  \cF_t \;=\; \cB_{T-t}
  \qquad \text{for all } 0 \leq t \leq T.
\]
In standard Go,
$\cF_t \neq \cB_{T-t}$ because ownership is pre-assigned:
the forward density of Black stones and the backward
value for White are structurally different objects.
In the Drunk Game, although colours are assigned (B--W
alternation is preserved), ownership is determined by the
closure event---the same topological operation that defines
the state transition.
The fair coin ($p = \tfrac{1}{2}$) ensures symmetric
occupation probabilities
(Remark~\ref{rem:transcommutation}),
so $\cF_t = \cB_{T-t}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Forward--backward collapse]%
\label{prop:fb-collapse}
In the Drunk Game (Definition~\ref{def:drunk-game}),
let $O_t \subset V$ denote the set of occupied vertices
at time~$t$, and let $p(t) = |O_t|/|V|$ be the occupation
density.
The Fokker--Planck density $\rho(x, t)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:fpe}) and the value function
$V(x)$ satisfy the same equation up to time reversal.
Specifically:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*),nosep]
\item Below the percolation threshold $p < p_c$,
  both $\rho$ and $V$ are diffusive:
  $\partial_t \rho = \frac{1}{2}\Delta \rho$
  and $V$ satisfies a backward heat equation.
\item At $p = p_c$, both undergo phase transition
  simultaneously: giant connected components form,
  closure becomes inevitable, and the forward density
  of ``stones placed'' equals the backward prediction
  of ``who closes first.''
\item The duality of Proposition~\ref{prop:duality}
  collapses to identity: forward $=$ backward.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The state at time~$t$ is $O_t \subset V$.
The forward process adds vertices via B--W alternation
with independent coin flips ($p = \tfrac{1}{2}$ each)
and uniform random placement.
The backward value asks: given $O_t$, what is
$\Pr[\text{player } i \text{ closes first}]$?
Since stones are visually identical on the board and
the coin is fair, each player's marginal placement
rate is the same ($\sim\! N^2/4$ stones in expectation).
This probability depends only on $|O_t|$ and the
topology of $O_t$---exactly the information that
determines the forward density~$\rho$.
The percolation threshold $p_c = |O_t|/|V|$ is the
critical density at which giant connected components
form on the lattice.
At~$p_c$, closure becomes inevitable, and the forward
evolution and backward prediction coincide as operators
on the same state space.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The duality map]\label{rem:duality-map}
The passage from standard Go to the Drunk Game is the
passage from asymmetric duality
(Proposition~\ref{prop:duality}) to self-duality:
\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Standard Go} & \textbf{%
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}醉围棋\end{CJK}
{} (Drunk Go)} \\
\midrule
Turn order & B--W (deterministic) & B--W (deterministic) \\
Whether to play & Strategic & Coin flip ($p = \tfrac{1}{2}$) \\
Where to play & Strategic & Uniform random \\
Ownership & Colour (a priori) & Closure (a posteriori) \\
FP vs.\ HJB & $\cF_t \neq \cB_{T-t}$ & $\cF_t = \cB_{T-t}$ \\
Analytic analogue & $\zeta(s)$
  & $\zeta(s)$ under $s \mapsto 1-s$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip
\noindent
The first row is the invariant---both games share the same
B--W alternation.
The second and third rows are the transcommutation---strategy
$\to$ randomness.
Self-duality is the game-theoretic shadow of the
functional equation.
The Drunk Game is to Go what $s \mapsto 1-s$ is to
the zeta function.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Self-variational optimal transport]%
\label{def:svot}
Let $\rho^*_N$ denote the game measure induced by
the Drunk Game (Definition~\ref{def:drunk-game})
on the $N \times N$ board:
the product of $\mathrm{Bernoulli}(\tfrac{1}{2})$ coin flips
and uniform placements.
Since $\rho^*_N$ is the uniform measure on game paths,
the free energy
(Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation})
of any policy~$\pi$ decomposes as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:svot}
  F(\pi)
  \;=\;
  F(\rho^*_N)
  \;+\;
  \underbrace{\bigl(\mathbb{E}_\pi[E]
    - \mathbb{E}_{\rho^*}[E]\bigr)}_{%
    \Delta E\;\text{(score)}}
  \;+\;
  \underbrace{\DKL(\pi \,\|\, \rho^*_N)}_{%
    \text{entropy cost}}\,.
\end{equation}
We call $\rho^*_N$ a \emph{self-variational optimal transport}:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \emph{Self:}\;
  source $=$ target
  ($\cF_t = \cB_{T-t}$, Definition~\ref{def:self-dual}).
\item \emph{Variational:}\;
  unique zero-cost reference ($\DKL = 0$).
\item \emph{Optimal:}\;
  maximum entropy ($H(\rho^*_N) \geq H(\pi)$ for all~$\pi$).
\item \emph{Transport:}\;
  each game moves mass from $\varnothing$ to a scored
  configuration; $M$~games sample $M$~couplings
  (Algorithm~\ref{alg:drunk-calibration}).
\end{itemize}
Every non-trivial policy $\pi \neq \rho^*_N$ is a
non-trivial transcommutation
(Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation}):
it converts entropy into score,
with $\DKL$ as the exchange rate.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Model-free RL\@: modeling the free core]%
\label{rem:model-free}
\color{black!60}%
The Queen, King, and Drunk Game form a triangle---not
a hierarchy:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Vertex} & \textbf{Role} &
\textbf{What it models} & \textbf{Type} \\
\midrule
Queen & Primal (forward FP) &
  Pool $\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$ &
  Model-based \\
King & Dual (backward HJB) &
  Value $\hat{V}(s)$, temperatures $\tau$ &
  Model-based \\
Drunk & Origin &
  Nothing (pure randomness) &
  Model-free \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\noindent
The Drunk Game is the \emph{origin} of the
(learning, optimisation) plane:
the Queen moves along the learning axis
($\bar{w}$ updates),
the King moves along the optimisation axis
($\tau$ tunes),
and the Drunk sits at $(0, 0)$---no learning,
no optimisation, but still producing valid games
with valid outcomes.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Degenerations.}\;
King at $\tau \to \infty$ (pure exploration) $=$ Drunk.
Queen at learning rate $\eta \to 0$ (no updates) $=$ Drunk.
The Drunk is where both degenerations meet:
the intersection of ``primal with no learning'' and
``dual with no optimisation.''

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The punchline.}\;
In the Freedom Theorem
(Proposition~\ref{prop:contraction}),
the free core $\cF$ is what remains after dissipation
contracts the state space.
At the origin---zero learning, zero optimisation,
zero dissipation---the free core is the \emph{entire}
state space: $\cF = \cX$.
Everything is free.
Equation~\eqref{eq:svot} makes this precise:
$F(\rho^*_N) = F^*$ is the free energy at
$\DKL = 0$.
The Drunk Game is not ``RL without a model.''
It is RL \emph{of} the free thing.
``Model-free'' is not jargon.
It is a theorem name:
\emph{the model whose object is the free core $\cF$}.
\end{remark}

\begin{algorithm}[ht]
\caption{Drunk Calibration (Phase~0)
  \textup{[Base Measure Estimation]}}\label{alg:drunk-calibration}
\begin{algorithmic}[1]
\Require Lattice sizes $\Lambda_R = \{5, 7, 11, \ldots, 31\}$,
  games per scale $M \in \mathbb{N}$
\Ensure Base measure
  $\mu = \{\mathrm{NLR}(N),\; \mathrm{WR}(N)\}_{N \in \Lambda_R}$
\For{$N \in \Lambda_R$}
  \State $\text{wins}, \text{losses}, \text{draws} \gets 0, 0, 0$
  \For{$m = 1, \ldots, M$}
    \State Play $\textsc{DrunkGame}(N)$
      \Comment{Def.~\ref{def:drunk-game}: coin $+$ uniform}
    \State Record outcome $(s^B_m, s^W_m) \in \mathbb{N}_0^2$;\;
      update win/loss/draw counts
  \EndFor
  \State $\mathrm{WR}(N) \gets \text{wins} / M$;\quad
    $\mathrm{NLR}(N) \gets (\text{wins} + \text{draws}) / M$
  \State \textbf{Check:}
    $\mathrm{NLR}_{\mathrm{drunk}}
    \approx 50\% \pm 1/\sqrt{M}$
    \Comment{self-dual sanity check}
\EndFor
\State \Return $\mu$
\end{algorithmic}
\end{algorithm}

\begin{proposition}[Drunk calibration convergence]%
\label{prop:drunk-convergence}
For each $N \in \Lambda_R$, the Drunk calibration
(Algorithm~\ref{alg:drunk-calibration}) satisfies:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*),nosep]
\item $\mathrm{WR}(N) \to \tfrac{1}{2}$ and
  $\mathrm{NLR}(N) \to \tfrac{1}{2}$
  at rate $O(1/\sqrt{M})$
  (SLLN for i.i.d.\ games; self-duality forces
  $\mathbb{E}[s^B] = \mathbb{E}[s^W]$).
\item The base measure $\mu$ is the null hypothesis:
  Queen win rate $> 50\%$ against~$\mu$ certifies
  that the pool has learned structure beyond random play.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
Each Drunk game is i.i.d.\ (the coin flips and placements
are independent across games).
Part~(a): by self-duality
(Definition~\ref{def:self-dual}),
$\mathbb{E}[s^B] = \mathbb{E}[s^W]$ exactly, so the
win rate converges to $\tfrac{1}{2}$ at $O(1/\sqrt{M})$.
Part~(b): any policy~$\pi$ achieving win rate $> 50\%$
against the Drunk baseline $\mu$ must exploit
board structure that pure randomness cannot---this
is precisely the information content of~$\pi$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Komi normalisation as gauge fixing]%
\label{rem:komi-gauge}
Define the area-normalised komi on an $N \times N$ board:
\[
  \kappa(N)
    \;=\; \max\!\bigl(1,\;
      \mathrm{round}(7 \cdot (N/19)^2)\bigr).
\]
This acts as gauge fixing
(cf.\ Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}):
it sets the zero of the scoring metric uniformly across
all scales.
In the Drunk Game, where ownership is emergent, gauge
fixing is essential---without it the scoring metric is
scale-dependent, breaking the self-duality of
Definition~\ref{def:self-dual}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Connection to the Euler product]%
\label{rem:euler-drunk}
On prime-dimensional boards
$\Lambda_R = \{5, 7, 11, 13, 17, 19, 23, 29, 31\}$,
each scale is one irreducible factor.
The colourless stones are analogous to primes:
a prime~$p$ has no ``colour''---it belongs to whichever
number it divides.
Ownership $=$ divisibility $=$ action, not label.
The Euler product
\[
  \zeta(s)^{-1}
    \;=\; \prod_{p}\bigl(1 - p^{-s}\bigr)
\]
is the partition function
(Remark~\ref{rem:primon-gas})
of the Drunk Game across scales: each local factor $(1 - p^{-s})$ is the
single-prime game, and the product assembles them
into the global game---exactly as executor assembling
(Definition~\ref{def:executor-assembling}) composes
single-type policies into the full scheduler.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The Queen's Gambit: gated championship}\label{sec:queens-gambit}

Training produces a pool~$\cP$ with learned framework weights.
But convergence on average (Theorem~\ref{thm:converge}) does
not guarantee zero losses at every scale.
The Queen's Gambit protocol demands a \emph{not-lose rate}
of $100\%$ at each lattice scale \emph{before} championship.

\medskip
\noindent
\fcolorbox{red!60}{red!6}{%
\begin{minipage}{0.95\linewidth}
\begin{definition}[Not-lose gate]\label{def:nlr-gate}
At scale $N_k$, let $n_k$ evaluation games be played
(alternating Black/White, integer komi~$\kappa_k$).
Define
\[
  {\color{red}\mathrm{NLR}}(N_k) \;=\;
    \frac{{\color{green!50!black}\#\{\text{wins}\}} + {\color{blue}\#\{\text{draws}\}}}{n_k}\,.
\]
The gate passes if and only if ${\color{red}\mathrm{NLR}}(N_k) = 1$.
Training continues (up to a budget) until the gate passes
or the budget is exhausted.
\end{definition}
\end{minipage}}

\begin{remark}[Queen invents the game online]\label{rem:queen-invents}
\color{black!60}%
Queen is not learning to play Go.
She is \textbf{inventing} Go---online, from scratch, with no
training data, no opening books, no expert games, no replay buffer.

The mechanism:
KataGo executes every stone.
Queen never touches the board.
She selects \emph{which framework to think with}
(Definition~\ref{def:strategy-pop}),
observes the binary outcome (win or not-win),
and updates the pool via replicator dynamics.
This is not gradient descent on parameters.
It is natural selection on strategies.

The appearance of ``learning'' is an external illusion:
an observer who plots win rate over time sees a rising curve
and calls it learning.
But internally there is no loss function, no backpropagation,
no parameter update.
There is only: try a way of thinking, see if it survives,
keep the survivors.
That is invention, not education.

$\mathrm{NLR} = 1$ is therefore not a competitive threshold
but a \textbf{pool-health invariant}:
if any framework at any scale cannot even draw,
the pool's coverage has collapsed---Queen has stopped inventing.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[MOPL has zero free parameters]\label{rem:zero-param}
\color{black!60}%
Every constant in MOPL is either uniquely forced by a mathematical
principle or determined by the game domain.
None is tuned.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}l@{\;\;}l@{\;\;}l@{}}
\toprule
Component & Value & Why forced \\
\midrule
Pool init & uniform $x_i = 1/k$ &
  max-entropy prior (unique) \\
Pool update & running average &
  Bayesian posterior, $\mathrm{Beta}(1,1)$ \\
Pool sampling & Boltzmann softmax &
  max-entropy distribution (unique) \\
Komi & $\max(1, \mathrm{round}(7(N/19)^2))$ &
  area-normalised to $19{\times}19$ \\
Frameworks & 5 Go strategies &
  domain-determined \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
There is no learning rate, no momentum, no weight decay,
no hidden dimension, no architecture search,
no validation set, no early stopping, no dropout,
no batch size, no optimiser choice.
The update rule
$\bar{w}_{n+1} = (\bar{w}_n \cdot n + o_{n+1})/(n+1)$
is not a design decision---it is the \emph{only}
online estimator that is both unbiased and consistent
for the mean of a bounded random variable.
MOPL is therefore not a model to be tuned.
It is a \textbf{measurement instrument}:
given Go rules and a frozen opponent,
the output is determined.
\end{remark}

\begin{algorithm}[ht]
\caption{Queen's Gated Training (Phase~1)
  \textup{[Replicator Flow on Expanding Lattice]}}\label{alg:queen}
\begin{algorithmic}[1]
\Require Lattice $\Lambda_R$, games per scale $n_N \in \mathbb{N}$,
  evaluation budget $E \in \mathbb{N}$, base measure $\mu$
  (Algorithm~\ref{alg:drunk-calibration}),
  temperature $\tau_{\mathrm{IR}} \in \mathbb{R}_{>0}$
\Ensure Trained pool $\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$, training log, checkpoint map
\State Initialise pool: $\bar{w}_i \gets 1/k$ for
  $i = 1, \ldots, k$ \Comment{max-entropy prior}
\For{$N \in \Lambda_R$ in increasing order}
  \For{$m = 1, \ldots, n_N$}
    \State Sample framework
      $F \sim \softmax\!\bigl(\log \bar{w} / \tau_{\mathrm{IR}}\bigr)$
      \Comment{Boltzmann}
    \State Play game against opponent at size $N$
      \Comment{MOPL pipeline}
    \State Observe outcome $o_m \in \{0, 0.5, 1\}$
    \State $\bar{w}_F \gets
      (\bar{w}_F \cdot n_F + o_m)\, / \,(n_F + 1)$
      \Comment{running average}
  \EndFor
  \State \textbf{Checkpoint:} play $E$ evaluation games at size $N$
  \State Compute $\mathrm{WR}(N)$, $\mathrm{NLR}(N)$
  \State \textbf{Gate:} verify $\mathrm{NLR}(N) = 100\%$
    \Comment{Queen viable at this scale}
  \State \textbf{if} gate fails \textbf{then} retry up to $n_N$ extra games;
    if still failing, continue with warning
\EndFor
\State \Return $\bar{w}$, training log, checkpoints
\end{algorithmic}
\end{algorithm}

\begin{definition}[Championship trial]\label{def:championship}
After all gates pass, the championship consists of
$T$ independent trials of $G$ games each against
the strongest available opponent (Borgov), alternating
MOPL as Black/White on successive games.
Komi is integer (allowing draws).
The single-point verdict is
$\hat{\mu} \pm \mathrm{SE}$
where $\hat{\mu} = T^{-1}\sum_t r_t$ and
$\mathrm{SE} = \sqrt{T^{-1}(T-1)^{-1}\sum_t (r_t - \hat\mu)^2}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Borgov's style:
  \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}残局\end{CJK} as opening]%
\label{rem:borgov-style}
In \emph{The Queen's Gambit} (Tevis, 1983),
Borgov's strength is not calculation but \emph{position}:
comfortable in any position, his play is methodical,
each opening move already encoding the endgame.
This is the fixed-point condition $x^* = f(x^*)$.

After lattice training, the pool equilibrium
$\pi^*_\Lambda$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:lattice-complete})
is the unique attractor of the replicator flow.
The championship does not \emph{search} for a strategy---it
\emph{reads} the
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}残局\end{CJK}
(endgame position) that training
already determined.
Every subsequent move is forced: parallel transport
along the gauge field
(Proposition~\ref{prop:gauge}),
with the spectral gap $m_* > 0$ preventing deviation.
First move $=$ last move $=$ fixed point.
The game has many moves but zero \emph{choices}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[True victory is exact]\label{rem:exact-victory}
Experimental finding: at 9$\times$9 (komi${}=6$, standard),
the gate passes immediately---10/10 wins, zero draws,
zero losses.
At 5$\times$5 (komi${}=2$, area-normalised), the gate
\emph{fails}: win rate $\sim 20\%$ despite 160 training games.
Note: the expanding-lattice protocol
(Section~\ref{sec:queens-gambit}) uses area-normalised
komi $\kappa(N) = \max(1, \mathrm{round}(7(N/19)^2))$
throughout; this figure used the standard 9$\times$9 komi.
The lesson: not-lose is a \emph{calibration} condition.
The same pool that dominates at one scale fails at another
because komi must exactly balance first-move advantage.
True victory requires matching the constraint to the
scale---a win by one point is as valid as a win by fifty,
but a komi that is off by one is a structural defect.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Training budget comparison]\label{rem:budget}
After championship, the budget comparison
(MOPL timed on Apple M2 Pro, single core, no GPU):

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lrrrr@{}}
\toprule
 & \textbf{MOPL} & \textbf{AlphaGo} & \textbf{KataGo}
 & \textbf{Human GM} \\
\midrule
Training games & $\sim 1400$\textsuperscript{$\dagger$} & $\sim 5\text{M}$ & $\sim$ millions
  & $\sim 50{,}000$ \\
Hardware & 1 CPU & 1202+176 & distributed
  & 1 brain \\
Parameters & 5 symbolic & 13M+ NN & 18M+ NN
  & $\sim 10^{11}$ synapses \\
External data & zero & human+self & self-play
  & teacher+books \\
\midrule
\multicolumn{5}{@{}l@{}}{\textit{Wallclock time (Apple M2 Pro, 1 core)}} \\
\midrule
Queen's training & TBD\textsuperscript{$\dagger$} & $\sim$\,3\,weeks & $\sim$\,days
  & $\sim$\,10\,years \\
King's tuning & $<$\,1\,s & --- & ---
  & --- \\
S-MPPI predict & 0.1\,ms/batch & --- & ---
  & --- \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
{\scriptsize $\dagger$\,9-prime lattice schedule; wallclock TBD
pending validated championship run.}

\medskip
\noindent
The gap is $\sim 3{,}500\times$ in training games.
The King's temperature learning (100 JAX gradient steps)
completes in under one second---the backward dual is
essentially free once the Queen has played.
MOPL operates on the strategy simplex~$\Delta^{k-1}$
(5 frameworks), not on the position space $\{0,\pm 1\}^{N^2}$.
The dimension reduction from $\sim 10^{170}$ (19$\times$19
positions) to~5 (simplex vertices) is what makes the
budget feasible.
The pool is the sufficient statistic:
Theorem~\ref{thm:converge} guarantees convergence on
the simplex regardless of board complexity.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The 12-year coincidence]\label{rem:beth}
Two prodigies---one fictional, one real---each took
exactly 12 years from first contact with the board
to defeating the World Champion.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}rllll@{}}
\toprule
 & \multicolumn{2}{c}{\textbf{Beth Harmon} (chess, fiction)}
 & \multicolumn{2}{c}{\textbf{%
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}柯洁\end{CJK}} (Go, real)} \\
\cmidrule(lr){2-3}\cmidrule(lr){4-5}
\textbf{Year} & \textbf{Milestone} & \textbf{$\Delta t$}
 & \textbf{Milestone} & \textbf{$\Delta t$} \\
\midrule
0  & First game (basement, age 8) & ---
   & First game (age 5\textonehalf) & --- \\
+7 & State Champion (age 15) &
   & Professional (age 11,
     \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}定段\end{CJK}) & \\

    & Top-10 in China & \\

      \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}百灵杯\end{CJK}) & 12\,yr \\

\medskip

\noindent
The ratio is $\sim 10^5\times$.
Beth trained on $\sim 50{,}000$ games (8$\times$8).
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}柯洁\end{CJK}
trained on $\sim 50{,}000$ games (19$\times$19,
$\sim 10^{170}$ legal positions).
MOPL trains on $\sim 1400$ games on a single CPU
core---no GPU, no neural network, no external data
(wallclock TBD, pending validated run).
The structural reason: human prodigies operate
in position space; MOPL operates on
$\Delta^4$ (5 frameworks).
The simplex is compact and 4-dimensional.
Convergence on a compact space is fast.
That is the entire explanation.

\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}
作者六岁学数学。十八年后写出了这篇论文——正好多了$\frac{1}{2}$。
Beth 用了十二年。柯洁用了十二年。MOPL 用了五十六分钟。
都是同一件事：在紧空间上收敛。

关键不是贪心策略。
Beth 的单元是一枚棋子。柯洁的单元是一颗子。
作者的单元是一个质点——一个光子：无质量，以光速传播，携带能量。
下每一个子的时候，都像是最后一次，也是第一次那样，认真地放下它。
That is the game.

口诀：the pawns are the reasons of the game. Play it like you are 保卫萝卜。

I am the world's smallest Champion.
五个参数，五百一十局，五十六分钟，一个核。
\end{CJK}
\end{remark}

\subsection{Colony: scaling via shared pheromone}\label{sec:colony}

A single MOPL agent operates on the simplex~$\Delta^{k-1}$
and discards every game record after extracting the 1-bit outcome
(win or not-win).
This section formalises the multi-agent extension:
$N$ agents sharing a common pool and depositing
\emph{full symbolic traces} into a persistent store.

\begin{definition}[Game record (\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK})
  as symbolic circuit]\label{def:game-record}
A game record is a sequence
$\gamma = (m_1, m_2, \ldots, m_T)$
where each move $m_t \in \{B[r,c],\; W[r,c],\; \texttt{pass}\}$
is a \emph{gate}.
The full sequence is a symbolic circuit whose output
is the pair (final board state, outcome $\in \{+1, 0, -1\}$).
Two records $\gamma, \gamma'$ are \emph{equivalent} iff they
produce the same final board state and outcome.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Pheromone
  (\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}信息素\end{CJK})]\label{def:pheromone}
The pheromone trail is the multiset
\[
  \Phi \;=\; \{\gamma_1, \gamma_2, \ldots, \gamma_n\}
\]
of all game records deposited by colony agents.
Each record is \emph{frozen} after creation
(write-once, read-many):
once $\gamma_i$ enters $\Phi$ it is never modified or deleted.
$\Phi$ is the collective memory of the colony.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Colony]\label{def:colony}
A colony is the triple
\[
  \cC \;=\; (A_1, \ldots, A_N,\; \Pi,\; \Phi)
\]
where
\begin{itemize}
\item $A_i$ is MOPL agent~$i$, each with its own Goer
      (KataGo instance) but sharing the pool~$\Pi$
      and the pheromone store~$\Phi$;
\item $\Pi$ is the StrategicPool
      (Definition~\ref{def:strategy-pop})
      with per-framework locks;
\item $\Phi$ is the GameRecordStore (append-only,
      Definition~\ref{def:pheromone}).
\end{itemize}
Each agent executes the same MOPL loop:
sample a framework from~$\Pi$, play one game via its Goer,
update~$\Pi$ with the 1-bit outcome,
and deposit the full record~$\gamma$ into~$\Phi$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Lock protocol preserves the running average]%
\label{prop:lock}
Concurrent updates to~$\Pi$ under per-framework locks
preserve the running-average invariant:
\[
  \bar{w}_{n+k}
  \;=\;
  \frac{\bar{w}_n \cdot n \;+\; \sum_{j=1}^{k} o_j}{n+k}\,,
\]
regardless of interleaving order,
where $o_j \in \{0,1\}$ is the outcome of the $j$-th
concurrent game.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Each atomic update reads the current $(n, \bar{w}_n)$
and writes $(n{+}1,\; (\bar{w}_n \cdot n + o)/(n{+}1))$.
Under a per-framework lock, two updates to the
\emph{same} framework are serialised;
updates to \emph{different} frameworks are independent
(disjoint memory).
For $k$ serialised updates to one framework,
the telescoping sum gives
$\bar{w}_{n+k} = (n\bar{w}_n + \sum_j o_j)/(n{+}k)$
because addition in $\R$ is commutative and associative,
so the final value is independent of arrival order.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scaling requires a colony, not a larger queen]%
\label{rem:colony-scaling}
\color{black!60}%
A single MOPL agent keeps only the 1-bit outcome of each game;
the full game record
(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK})
is discarded.
Scaling by making one agent play more games increases
\emph{breadth} (more samples on $\Delta^{k-1}$)
but not \emph{depth}:
no new symbolic structure is retained.

Scaling by adding $N$ agents who \textbf{deposit} full records
into shared pheromone~$\Phi$ increases both breadth
(more games) \emph{and} depth
(full symbolic traces available for future analysis---e.g.,
pattern extraction, opening-tree construction,
or cross-agent imitation).

Zero parameters per agent is unchanged
(Remark~\ref{rem:zero-param}).
Total colony parameters $= 0 \times N = 0$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Connection to ant colony optimisation]%
\label{rem:aco}
\color{black!60}%
The correspondence is not analogy---it \emph{is}
ant colony optimisation (ACO) with Go-specific semantics:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{ACO concept} & \textbf{MOPL colony} \\
\midrule
Pheromone trail     & Pool weights $\bar{w}_i$ \\
Pheromone deposit   & Running-average update after each game \\
Probabilistic path  & Boltzmann sampling from $\Pi$ \\
Pheromone concentration & Framework win rate \\
Evaporation         & Implicit: $\bar{w}_n$ dilutes as $n \to \infty$ \\
Full path memory    & Game record store $\Phi$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
The pool \emph{is} the pheromone trail.
Boltzmann sampling \emph{is} the probabilistic path selection.
Evaporation is implicit via the running average:
old outcomes weigh $\mathcal{O}(1/n)$ as $n$ grows.
The colony adds one new structure---$\Phi$---which
stores the full symbolic circuits that ACO's
classical formulation discards.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Closed IO loop of the
  \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK}]%
\label{rem:io-circuit}
\color{black!60}%
The write path (Definition~\ref{def:game-record},
Proposition~\ref{prop:lock}) deposits records into the
store~$\Phi$ and updates pool weights.
We now close the loop by specifying the \emph{read} path.
The full symbolic circuit is:
\[
  \Pi
  \xrightarrow{\;\text{sample}\;}
  f_i
  \xrightarrow{\;\text{Thinker}\;}
  \text{prompt}
  \xrightarrow{\;\text{Goer}\;}
  \gamma
  \xrightarrow{\;\text{Transcriber}\;}
  \Phi
  \xrightarrow{\;\text{retrieve}\;}
  \text{Thinker},
\]
where $f_i$ is the sampled framework, $\gamma$ is the game
record, and the retrieve arrow feeds past records back
into the Thinker's context for the next game.
In parallel, the scalar outcome
$o \in \{-1,0,+1\}$ feeds back:
$\gamma \xrightarrow{\;o\;} \Pi.\texttt{update}()$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Two read-back channels.}\;
The loop carries two signals of different bandwidth:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Scalar channel}:
  outcome $o \in \{-1,0,+1\}$
  $\to$ pool running-average update
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:lock}).
  Fast, lossy---the 1-bit gradient.
  The pool converges to the optimal framework mixture
  via this channel alone.
\item \emph{Symbolic channel}:
  full record $\gamma \in \Phi$
  $\to$ Thinker retrieval.
  Slow, rich---the complete move sequence.
  The Thinker refines move selection by conditioning on
  past trajectories filtered by framework and outcome.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Positional structure.}\;
Each move $m_t = (\texttt{move\_number},\, r,\, c,\,
\texttt{color})$ in the record~$\gamma$ carries an
explicit position.
The sequence $(m_1, \ldots, m_T)$ is a trajectory through
board-state space $\{0,B,W\}^{n \times n}$.
Retrieving past records from~$\Phi$ by framework and outcome
is \emph{attention over trajectory space}---the same
mechanism as positional embedding in a transformer,
but over game histories rather than token positions.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The opponent is invisible.}\;
The record~$\gamma$ contains both sides' moves
(necessary for replay), but the pool receives only the
MOPL-perspective outcome~$o$.
The queen observes \emph{results}, not methods.
This is the correct information boundary:
learning \emph{what works} (exploitation signal)
without copying \emph{how the opponent plays},
which would destroy strategic diversity across the colony.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The broken lens.}\;
The symbolic read path currently filters records by an exact
match on board size (\texttt{board\_size == board\_size}).
This is a hard cutoff: $\tau_{\text{size}} = 0$, infinite
sharpness.
Records from a $9\times 9$ board are invisible when playing
$13\times 13$, even though the opening theory transfers.
The correct formulation replaces the hard filter with a soft
Boltzmann weight:
$w_{\text{size}}(n, n') \propto \exp\bigl(-|n - n'| /
\tau_{\text{size}}\bigr)$,
so that records from nearby board sizes contribute with
geometrically decaying relevance.
Making $\tau_{\text{size}}$ adaptive---part of the telescope
$(\tau_{\text{UV}}, \tau_{\text{IR}})$---resolves the
cross-scale transfer problem
(Remark~\ref{rem:telescope}).
\end{remark}

\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\begin{tikzpicture}[
  >=Stealth,
  box/.style={draw, rounded corners=3pt, minimum width=2.2cm,
              minimum height=0.85cm, font=\small\bfseries,
              align=center, line width=0.5pt},
  arr/.style={->, thick},
  lbl/.style={font=\scriptsize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt},
]
  % Pentagon layout (angles: top, upper-right, lower-right, lower-left, upper-left)
  \node[box, fill=green!12]  (pool)  at (90:2.8)   {Pool\; $\Pi$};
  \node[box, fill=blue!10]   (think) at (18:2.8)    {Thinker};
  \node[box, fill=orange!12] (goer)  at (-54:2.8)   {Goer};
  \node[box, fill=yellow!10] (game)  at (-126:2.8)  {Game\; $\gamma$};
  \node[box, fill=red!10]    (store) at (162:2.8)   {Store\; $\Phi$};

  % Forward loop (clockwise around pentagon)
  \draw[arr] (pool)  -- node[lbl, above right=-1pt] {sample $f_i$} (think);
  \draw[arr] (think) -- node[lbl, right]            {prompt}       (goer);
  \draw[arr] (goer)  -- node[lbl, below]            {play}         (game);
  \draw[arr] (game)  -- node[lbl, left]      {\textit{Transcriber}} (store);

  % Symbolic channel: Store -> Thinker (thick red, crosses interior)
  \draw[->, very thick, red!60!black] (store) --
    node[lbl, above, pos=0.45, text=red!60!black] {\textit{retrieve}} (think);

  % Scalar channel: Game -> Pool (thin green, crosses interior)
  \draw[->, semithick, green!50!black] (game) --
    node[lbl, above, pos=0.5, text=green!50!black] {$o \in \{-1,0,{+}1\}$} (pool);

  % Opponent (outside pentagon, below)
  \node[box, fill=gray!8, draw=gray, dashed]
    (opp) at (-90:4.2) {\textcolor{gray}{Opponent}};
  \draw[->, dashed, gray] (opp) --
    node[lbl, right, text=gray] {opaque} (game);

\end{tikzpicture}
\caption{The closed symbolic circuit of the
  \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK}
  (Remark~\ref{rem:io-circuit}).
  Black arrows: forward data flow (clockwise).
  \textcolor{red!60!black}{\textbf{Red}}: symbolic channel
    (full game record, rich).
  \textcolor{green!50!black}{\textbf{Green}}: scalar channel
    (1-bit outcome, fast).
  Dashed grey: the opponent is outside the pheromone
  loop---the queen observes results, not methods.
  The King's temperatures $(\tau_{\text{UV}}, \tau_{\text{IR}})$
  control the resolution of both channels
  (Remark~\ref{rem:telescope}).}%
\label{fig:io-circuit}
\end{figure}

\begin{remark}[Knowledge is pheromone, not weights]%
\label{rem:knowledge-is-pheromone}
\color{black!60}%
In a neural network, learned knowledge is stored as
weight matrices $W \in \mathbb{R}^{d \times d}$:
opaque, distributed, and requiring interpretation.
In MOPL, learned knowledge is stored as
\emph{symbolic pheromone}:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{What is learned} & \textbf{Representation}
  & \textbf{Human-readable?} \\
\midrule
Which strategy works &
  $\Pi$: five running averages $\bar{w}_i$ &
  Yes: $\bar{w}_i = 0.45$ means ``wins 45\%'' \\
How each game went &
  $\Phi$: $N$ frozen
  \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK} &
  Yes: \texttt{B[3,4] W[5,6] B[pass]} \\
How to read the above &
  $(\tau_{\text{UV}}, \tau_{\text{IR}})$: two temperatures &
  Yes: scalars in $\mathbb{R}_{>0}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
Total learned representation:
$(\Pi,\, \Phi,\, \tau_{\text{UV}},\, \tau_{\text{IR}})$
$=$ five running averages $+$ $N$ symbolic traces $+$
two real numbers.
Every component is individually inspectable.
Every \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK} can be
decoded move by move.
Every pool weight has a direct semantic interpretation.

\medskip\noindent
This is a \textbf{real} difference, not a philosophical one.
A neural network that wins 60\% of games stores the reason
in $10^7$ entangled floats---no one can say \emph{why}
it chose move~D4.
MOPL stores the reason in the pool:
``\textit{aggressive} has $\bar{w} = 0.72$ after 40 games;
the last three winning
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK}
opened at D4.''
The explanation \emph{is} the representation.
There is nothing behind the curtain.

\medskip\noindent
The trade is explicit:
\emph{capacity} (a neural network can represent
$2^{d^2}$ functions) for \emph{verifiability}
(every MOPL decision has a finite, readable proof trail).
Remark~\ref{rem:zero-param}: zero free parameters.
This remark: zero hidden knowledge.
The data grows without bound; only the telescope learns
(Remark~\ref{rem:telescope}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Record everything, learn to search]%
\label{rem:telescope}
\color{black!60}%
The preceding remark lists \emph{what} MOPL stores.
This remark clarifies \emph{how} the stored knowledge is used.
The metaphor is astronomical:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Astronomy} & \textbf{MOPL} & \textbf{Symbol} \\
\midrule
Night sky (all photons) &
  \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK} store &
  $\Phi$ \\
Star catalog (compressed) &
  Pool (running averages) &
  $\Pi$ \\
Telescope (resolution \& pointing) &
  Temperatures &
  $(\tau_{\text{UV}},\, \tau_{\text{IR}})$ \\
Observer (reads through telescope) &
  Thinker &
  LLM context \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The store~$\Phi$ is an ever-growing archive of
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK}.
It is \emph{not} a training set---no gradient is ever
computed over it.
It is the raw sky: every photon (game record) is deposited
faithfully, and none is discarded.
The pool~$\Pi$ compresses this sky into a catalog of five
running averages---a lossy but sufficient summary of which
frameworks win.

\medskip\noindent
The two temperatures $(\tau_{\text{UV}}, \tau_{\text{IR}})$
are the \emph{telescope}.
They control what the observer (Thinker) sees:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\tau_{\text{UV}}$ (exploration temperature):
  controls the \emph{resolution}---how sharply the pool
  concentrates on the current best framework.
  High~$\tau_{\text{UV}}$: wide field, many frameworks
  visible.
  Low~$\tau_{\text{UV}}$: narrow field, only the dominant
  framework survives.
\item $\tau_{\text{IR}}$ (exploitation temperature):
  controls the \emph{pointing}---how aggressively the
  Thinker reads past records for the selected framework.
\end{itemize}

\noindent
The structural parallel with the Riemann zeta function is
worth noting.
Pool sampling assigns probability
$P(f_i) \propto \bar{w}_i^{1/\tau}$;
the Dirichlet series assigns weight $n^{-s}$ to the
$n$-th term.
Temperature~$\tau$ plays the role of the complex variable~$s$:
it controls which ``frequencies'' (frameworks) dominate the
sum.
High~$\tau$ (low~$\Re(s)$): all terms contribute roughly
equally.
Low~$\tau$ (high~$\Re(s)$): only the leading term survives.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The telescope principle.}\;
\emph{Record everything, learn to search.}
The Queen deposits faithfully (Definition~\ref{def:game-record}).
The data~$\Phi$ grows without bound.
Only the telescope---two real numbers---learns.
This is the complete learning signal of MOPL:
memories plus a lens, $(\Phi,\, \tau_{\text{UV}},\, \tau_{\text{IR}})$.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Telescope search]%
\label{def:telescope-search}
Given the pool~$\Pi$ with win rates
$\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$,
the record store~$\Phi$ with $N$ frozen
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK},
and temperatures $\tau > 0$, $\tau_{\text{size}} > 0$,
the \emph{telescope search} assigns to each record
$\gamma \in \Phi$ an action
\begin{equation}\label{eq:action}
  S(\gamma)
  \;=\;
  \underbrace{-\log \bar{w}_{f(\gamma)}}_
    {\text{framework quality}}
  \;+\;
  \underbrace{\frac{|N_\gamma - N_{\text{current}}|}
    {\tau_{\text{size}}}}_
    {\text{scale distance}}\,,
\end{equation}
where $f(\gamma)$ is the framework used in record~$\gamma$
and $N_\gamma$ is the board size.
The search selects a framework by sampling from the
partition function
\begin{equation}\label{eq:partition}
  Z \;=\; \sum_{\gamma \in \Phi}
  \exp\!\bigl(-S(\gamma)/\tau\bigr),
  \qquad
  P(\gamma) = \frac{1}{Z}\,
  \exp\!\bigl(-S(\gamma)/\tau\bigr).
\end{equation}
At $\tau \to 0$, only the record with smallest action
survives (classical limit: greedy, exploit).
At $\tau \to \infty$, all records contribute equally
(quantum limit: uniform, explore).
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Path integral and free energy]%
\label{rem:path-integral}
\color{black!60}%
Definition~\ref{def:telescope-search} is a path integral:
each \begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}棋谱\end{CJK}~$\gamma$
is a path through board-state space,
$S(\gamma)$ is its action, and
$Z$ is the partition function.
The \emph{free energy}
\[
  F \;=\; -\tau \log Z
  \;=\; \min_{p}\;\bigl[\,
    \underbrace{\mathbb{E}_p[\,S(\gamma)\,]}_{\text{energy}}
    \;+\;
    \tau\,
    \underbrace{H(p)}_{\text{entropy}}
  \,\bigr]
\]
decomposes the search into two competing terms:
energy (prefer winning strategies at nearby scales)
and entropy (prefer diverse exploration)---the
same decomposition as
Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation}.
Jensen's inequality gives the bound:
the Boltzmann distribution~\eqref{eq:partition}
is the unique minimiser of this variational problem.

\medskip\noindent
Three names, one structure:
\emph{path integral} (physics),
\emph{log-sum-exp} (computation),
\emph{free-energy variational principle} (optimisation).
The telescope's lens~$\tau$ is the inverse temperature
that interpolates between classical (exploit) and
quantum (explore).
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Unconditional convergence of the pool]%
\label{prop:contraction}
Let $\bar{w}_n^{(i)}$ denote the win rate of framework~$i$
after $n$ games with that framework, updated by the
running average (Proposition~\ref{prop:lock}):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:running-avg}
  \bar{w}_{n+1}^{(i)}
  \;=\;
  \frac{n\,\bar{w}_n^{(i)} \;+\; o_{n+1}}{n+1}\,,
  \qquad o_{n+1} \in [0,1].
\end{equation}
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}, nosep]
\item \textbf{Initial-state independence.}\;
  After $n \geq 1$ updates,
  $\bar{w}_n^{(i)} = \frac{1}{n}\sum_{j=1}^{n} o_j$:
  the empirical mean of outcomes.
  The initial state~$\bar{w}_0$ has weight $0/n = 0$.

\item \textbf{Almost-sure convergence.}\;
  For a fixed opponent, the expected outcome
  $\mu_i := \mathbb{E}[o \mid \text{framework } i]$ exists.
  By the strong law of large numbers,
  $\bar{w}_{n}^{(i)} \to \mu_i$ a.s.\
  as the number of games $n_i \to \infty$.

\item \textbf{Exploration guarantee.}\;
  When $\tau > 0$ and win rates are clamped to
  $[\epsilon, 1{-}\epsilon]$ with $\epsilon > 0$,
  every framework has selection probability
  $\geq \epsilon^{1/\tau}/k > 0$.
  By Borel--Cantelli, each framework is sampled
  infinitely often a.s., so \textup{(ii)} applies
  to all $k$ frameworks simultaneously.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The unique fixed point is
$\mu^* = (\mu_1, \ldots, \mu_k)$:
the true win-rate vector against this opponent.
Convergence is \emph{unconditional}---it requires
no assumption on the initial pool state~$\bar{w}_0$,
the opponent's identity, or the board size.
The structural requirements ($\tau > 0$, $\epsilon > 0$)
are satisfied by construction
(clamping to $[0.01, 0.99]$; temperature always positive).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\textup{(i)}\;
Unroll the recurrence.
After one update:
$\bar{w}_1 = (0 \cdot \bar{w}_0 + o_1)/1 = o_1$,
independent of~$\bar{w}_0$.
Inductively, $\bar{w}_n = (\sum_{j=1}^n o_j)/n$.
The contraction factor at step~$n$ is
$n/(n{+}1) < 1$; the cumulative factor from step~0
is $\prod_{j=0}^{n-1} j/(j{+}1) = 0/n = 0$.

\medskip\noindent
\textup{(ii)}\;
The outcomes $\{o_j\}$ for framework~$i$ against a
fixed opponent are i.i.d.\ bounded random variables
(each game is an independent trial on a fresh board).
The strong law gives
$\bar{w}_n^{(i)} \to \mu_i$ a.s.

\medskip\noindent
\textup{(iii)}\;
Under Boltzmann sampling with clamped weights
$\tilde{w}_i := \max(\epsilon,
  \min(1{-}\epsilon, \bar{w}_i))$,
the probability of selecting framework~$i$ is
$p_i = \tilde{w}_i^{1/\tau} / \sum_j \tilde{w}_j^{1/\tau}
\geq \epsilon^{1/\tau} /
  (k \cdot (1{-}\epsilon)^{1/\tau}) > 0$.
Since $\sum_t p_i = \infty$, the second Borel--Cantelli
lemma gives $P(i \text{ selected i.o.}) = 1$.

\medskip\noindent
\textup{Rate.}\;
The contraction factor at step~$n$ is $n/(n{+}1) < 1$,
but $n/(n{+}1) \to 1$: the per-step contraction vanishes.
This is \emph{not} Banach contraction
(which requires a uniform bound $c < 1$).
The convergence rate is algebraic:
$|\bar{w}_n - \mu| = O(1/\sqrt{n})$ a.s.\
(by the law of the iterated logarithm, the sharp
rate is $O(\sqrt{\log\log n \,/\, n})$).
No discount factor is used.
The Queen converges through \emph{averaging}
(the strong law), not through \emph{discounting}
(a geometric factor $\gamma^n$).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Freedom Theorem for the pool]%
\label{rem:freedom-pool}
Proposition~\ref{prop:contraction} is the Freedom Theorem
applied to the pool:
dissipative flow (running-average dilution,
factor $n/(n{+}1)$) on a compact space
($[0.01, 0.99]^k$, clamped) converges to a
finite free core ($\mu^*$, a single point)
at algebraic rate $O(1/\sqrt{n})$.
Compare Proposition~\ref{prop:honest}:
there, the \emph{gated iteration} contracts on
proof space~$\cP$ (geometric rate);
here, the \emph{pool update} converges on $[0,1]^k$
(algebraic rate, no discount factor).
Both are unconditional.
Their composition---pool contraction feeding
gated verification---gives MOPL's end-to-end
convergence guarantee.
\end{remark}

\subsection{King's Predictive Control: S-MPPI backward dual}%
\label{sec:kings-control}

The Queen plays the forward game (Fokker--Planck,
Proposition~\ref{prop:fpe}).
The King predicts the outcome \emph{before playing}:
the backward Hamilton--Jacobi--Bellman (HJB) dual.

\begin{definition}[Rollout horizon]\label{def:horizon}
The King's \emph{rollout horizon} $\cH$ is the set of all
reachable futures from the current pool state~$\cP$
within $N$ rollouts of depth~$T$:
\[
  \cH(\cP, N, T) \;=\;
    \bigl\{\, \xi^{(i)}_{1:T} \;\big|\;
    i = 1, \ldots, N, \;\;
    \xi^{(i)}_t \sim \pi(\cP, \tau) \,\bigr\}.
\]
Each rollout $\xi^{(i)}$ is one possible universe.
The King explores all $N$ universes simultaneously
and selects the optimal action by Boltzmann reweighting:
$a^* = \arg\min_a \sum_i w_i \, c(\xi^{(i)}, a)$
where $w_i = \exp(-c_i / \tau) / Z$.
As $\tau \to 0$, only the single best universe survives.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Doctor Strange's Time Stone]\label{rem:strange}
In \emph{Avengers: Infinity War} (2018), Doctor Strange
examines 14{,}000{,}605 possible futures and finds exactly
one in which they win.
This is S-MPPI with $N = 14{,}000{,}605$ rollouts and
$\tau \to 0$ (greedy selection of the unique winning trajectory).
The Time Stone \emph{is} the rollout horizon $\cH$:
it defines which futures are reachable.
The King's S-MPPI is the same operation without the
Stone---JAX computes the rollouts, softmax selects
the winner, and $\tau$ controls how many universes
effectively contribute.
At $\tau = 0.16$ (learned), the King concentrates on
$\sim 3$ effective universes out of $S \times k$.
At $\tau \to 0$: ``How many did we win?''\ ``One.''
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[S-MPPI prediction]\label{def:smppi}
Given pool weights $w \in \Delta^{k-1}$ and a matrix
$M \in \R^{S \times k}$ of mean outcomes
(MPPI-reweighted, per framework per scale),
the predicted value at temperature~$\tau$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:smppi}
  \hat{V}(s) \;=\; M_s^\top \pi(\tau),
  \qquad
  \pi(\tau) = \softmax\!\bigl(\log w / \tau\bigr).
\end{equation}
The matrix $M$ is constructed once from training history
by MPPI reweighting:
$w_i = \exp(-c_i / \tau) / Z$, $c_i = 1 - \text{outcome}_i$.
All $S$ scales are computed in one batched matrix-vector
product---embarrassingly parallel.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Forward-backward duality]\label{prop:duality}
The Queen's forward Fokker--Planck
(Proposition~\ref{prop:fpe}) evolves the density
$\rho(x,\Lambda,t)$.
The King's backward S-MPPI computes the value function
$\hat{V}(s)$ under the \emph{same} pool state.
When $|\hat{V}(s) - V_{\text{actual}}(s)| < \epsilon$
across a majority of scales, the forward and backward
views agree and the pool is at equilibrium.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[JAX implementation]\label{rem:jax}
The S-MPPI prediction is JIT-compiled in JAX\@.
\texttt{jax.nn.softmax} computes~$\pi(\tau)$;
the batched prediction is one \texttt{@} (matrix-vector)
call.
Measured: 1000 batches of 100-scale predictions in 101\,ms
on a single CPU\@.
No GPU required.
The embarrassingly parallel structure means prediction
cost is $O(Sk)$ regardless of training history length.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Double Boltzmann: the two learned temperatures}%
\label{sec:double-boltzmann}

The King controls two temperatures:
$\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}$ (which \emph{scale} to attend to)
and $\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}$ (how \emph{sharply} to act within
a scale).

\begin{definition}[Controller with cutoff horizon]\label{def:two-temp}
Fix the \emph{predictive horizon} $H \in \N$
(a budget set by the user: the number of most recent
games the King considers for prediction).
The outcome matrix $M$ is built from the last $H$
entries of the training log.
Define the loss at fixed~$H$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:controller-loss}
  \cL(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}} \,;\, H)
    \;=\; -\,\pi_{\mathrm{scale}}(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}})^\top\,
           \hat{V}(\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}),
\end{equation}
where
$\hat{V}(\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}) = M_H \,\softmax(\log w / \tau_{\mathrm{IR}})$
is the per-scale predicted value under framework selection
temperature~$\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}$,
$M_H$ is the outcome matrix restricted to the last $H$ games,
and
