$\pi_{\mathrm{scale}}(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}})
  = \softmax(\hat{V}(\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}) / \tau_{\mathrm{UV}})$
is the scale allocation policy.
$H$ is the user's budget: how far back to look.
$H = 60$: the King sees the last 60 games.
$H = |\Lambda_R| \cdot \bar{n}$: the King sees everything.
The two temperatures $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}})$
are learned via gradient descent at fixed~$H$;
they live in log-space ($\tau = e^\theta$) for positivity.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Gradient learning via pullback]\label{prop:pullback}
The loss~\eqref{eq:controller-loss} is differentiable in
$(\theta_{\mathrm{UV}}, \theta_{\mathrm{IR}})$ through
two nested softmax operations.
JAX auto-differentiation computes exact gradients:
\[
  \theta \;\leftarrow\; \theta - \eta\,\nabla_\theta \cL.
\]
The gradient $\nabla_\theta \cL$ pulls back through
the double Boltzmann to learn the temperatures that
maximise predicted not-lose rate.
\end{proposition}

\begin{algorithm}[ht]
\caption{King's Predictive Control (Phase~2)
  \textup{[Double Boltzmann Temperature Optimization]}}\label{alg:king}
\begin{algorithmic}[1]
\Require Pool state $\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$, training log,
  horizon $H \in \mathbb{N}$, learning rate $\eta \in \mathbb{R}_{>0}$,
  steps $J \in \mathbb{N}$,
  warm-start $\theta_0 \in \mathbb{R}^2$ (optional)
\Ensure Optimal temperatures
  $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}^*, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}}^*) \in \mathbb{R}_{>0}^2$,
  predictions $\hat{V} \in \mathbb{R}^S$
\State $M_H \gets$ outcome matrix from last $H$ games
  \Comment{$M_H \in \mathbb{R}^{S \times k}$}
\State $\theta \gets \theta_0$ if warm-start,
  else $(\log\tau_{\mathrm{UV}},\, \log\tau_{\mathrm{IR}})
  = (0, 0)$
\For{$j = 1, \ldots, J$}
  \State $\tau_{\mathrm{IR}} \gets e^{\theta_{\mathrm{IR}}}$,
    \quad $\tau_{\mathrm{UV}} \gets e^{\theta_{\mathrm{UV}}}$
  \State $\pi_f \gets
    \softmax\!\bigl(\log \bar{w} / \tau_{\mathrm{IR}}\bigr)$
    \Comment{$\in \Delta^{k-1}$}
  \State $\hat{V}(s) \gets M_H \, \pi_f$
    \quad for all scales $s$
    \Comment{Def.~\ref{def:smppi}}
  \State $\pi_s \gets
    \softmax\!\bigl(\hat{V} / \tau_{\mathrm{UV}}\bigr)$
    \Comment{$\in \Delta^{S-1}$}
  \State $\mathcal{L} \gets -\pi_s^\top \hat{V}$
    \Comment{Eq.~\ref{eq:controller-loss}}
  \State $\theta \gets \theta - \eta\,\nabla_\theta \mathcal{L}$
    \Comment{JAX auto-diff}
\EndFor
\State $\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}^* \gets e^{\theta_{\mathrm{UV}}}$,
  \quad $\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}^* \gets e^{\theta_{\mathrm{IR}}}$
\State \Return
  $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}^*, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}}^*)$,
  $\hat{V}$, $\theta$ (for warm-start)
\end{algorithmic}
\end{algorithm}

\begin{remark}[Two strings and one knob]\label{rem:two-strings}
$\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}$ controls \emph{where to look}
(scale selection)---learned.
$\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}$ controls \emph{how sharply to act}
(framework selection)---learned.
$H$ controls \emph{how far to see}
(predictive horizon)---set by the user.
Two learned strings, one free knob.
The King learns HOW to look within the horizon YOU set.
The King tunes online during championship---warm-starting
from the previous game's parameters.
Each championship game adds one data point to the
training log; the King re-optimizes in $< 1$\,s
(50 warm-start gradient steps).
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}
两根弦，调好了，宇宙就响了。
\end{CJK}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Optimal switching in linear time]\label{rem:switching}
The controller is an \emph{optimal switching random walk}.
$H$ is the hard off---the finite window of games the King sees.
Within that window, each round's framework is selected with
probability $\pi_f = \softmax(\log w / \tau_{\mathrm{IR}})$:
a learned chance $\in (0,1)$.
The walk visits scales according to
$\pi_{\mathrm{scale}} = \softmax(\hat{V} / \tau_{\mathrm{UV}})$:
another learned chance.
Two soft switches, one hard cutoff.
The entire walk runs in $O(H \cdot k)$ time---linear in
the horizon $H$ and the number of frameworks $k$.
This is the infinity-Go-universe reduced to linear time:
$H$ games, each resolved by two softmax lookups.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Two horizons, two convergence mechanisms]%
\label{rem:two-horizons}
The King's architecture separates two horizons.
Their interplay---and their contrast with the Queen's
convergence---reveals MOPL's full convergence structure.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Forward lookahead $\cH$.}\;
Definition~\ref{def:horizon} defines the \emph{rollout horizon}:
the set of $N$ simulated futures of depth~$T$
from the current pool state.
This is the \emph{planning} horizon---what \emph{could} happen.
In MPC, this corresponds to the open-loop forward simulation
(Doctor Strange's 14{,}000{,}605 futures).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Backward data window $H$.}\;
Definition~\ref{def:two-temp} fixes $H \in \N$---the number
of most recent games used to build the outcome matrix~$M_H$.
This is the \emph{memory} horizon---what \emph{did} happen.
Each past game is one realised sample from the
reachable set~$\cH$.
Using $H$ samples approximates the forward expectation
by empirical averaging.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The connection.}\;
In classical MPC, both horizons coincide: you simulate
$H$ steps forward.
In KPC, they separate because the King uses \emph{real}
past data---not simulated futures---to build the
prediction matrix.
The forward lookahead~$\cH$ defines the space;
the backward window~$H$ samples from it.
As $H \to \infty$, the empirical matrix~$M_H$
converges to the true expectation over~$\cH$
(again by the strong law).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Queen vs.\ King: two independent convergence mechanisms.}

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Queen (forward)} & \textbf{King (backward)} \\
\midrule
What converges &
  Pool $\bar{w} \to \mu^*$ &
  Temperatures $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}}) \to \tau^*$ \\
Mechanism &
  Running average (SLLN) &
  Gradient descent on $\cL$ \\
Data used &
  All $n$ games (full history) &
  Last $H$ games (sliding window) \\
Rate &
  Algebraic: $O(1/\sqrt{n})$ &
  Geometric (if $\cL$ strongly convex) \\
Discount factor &
  None (Ces\`{a}ro averaging) &
  Implicit: $\gamma \approx 1 - 1/H$ \\
Contraction source &
  Memory dilution: $n/(n{+}1) \to 1$ &
  Finite horizon: $H < \infty$ \\
Independence &
  Converges for \emph{any} $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}})$ &
  Converges for \emph{any} $\bar{w}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The two mechanisms are \emph{independent}:
the Queen's SLLN convergence does not depend on the
King's temperatures, and the King's gradient descent
does not depend on the Queen's specific win-rate trajectory.
The coupling is through \emph{data flow}
(game outcomes feed both), not through the convergence proofs.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The $H \leftrightarrow \gamma$ equivalence.}\;
The King's data window~$H$ plays the role of the
discount factor~$\gamma$ in reinforcement learning.
A sliding window of size~$H$ assigns uniform weight~$1/H$
to recent games and weight~$0$ to older games (hard cutoff).
An exponential discount $\gamma^{n-t}$ assigns geometrically
decaying weight to past games (soft cutoff).
Both achieve the same effect: bounding the \emph{effective
memory} to prevent old data from dominating.
The equivalence is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:H-gamma}
  \gamma \;\approx\; 1 - \frac{1}{H}\,,
  \qquad\text{so}\qquad
  H = 60 \;\Longleftrightarrow\;
  \gamma \approx 0.983.
\end{equation}
Both give contraction:
$\gamma < 1$ ensures geometric forgetting;
$H < \infty$ ensures bounded influence of any single game.
The Queen has neither: $\gamma = 1$ (no discount),
$H = \infty$ (all data).
She converges anyway---by averaging, not by discounting.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Two-timescale system.}\;
The Queen is slow ($1/\sqrt{n}$, all data);
the King is fast (geometric, warm-started with 50 gradient
steps per game).
By the two-timescale stochastic approximation theorem
\textup{(Borkar, 2008)}, the coupled system converges:
the fast process (King) sees a quasi-static slow process
(Queen), and the slow process sees the fast process at
equilibrium.
Their composition gives MOPL's end-to-end convergence:
the Queen finds the right strategy,
the King executes it optimally.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{No log-gas leak.}\;
A ``leak'' between the two processes would require
positive feedback: King's output amplifies Queen's
error, which amplifies King's error, ad infinitum.
This cannot happen because:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item The Queen's averaging operator and the King's
  gradient operator act on \emph{disjoint coordinates}
  ($[0,1]^k$ vs.\ $\R^2$).
\item The coupling is a \emph{sequential pipeline}:
  Queen deposits $\bar{w}$, King reads $\bar{w}$,
  King plays, outcome~$o$ feeds Queen.
  No simultaneous write; no within-step feedback.
\item The Queen's error $|\bar{w}_n - \mu^*| = O(1/\sqrt{n})$
  is \emph{unconditional}---it holds for any sequence of
  outcomes, regardless of how the King chose the move.
  The King changes the \emph{distribution} of~$o$, not the
  \emph{validity} of the strong law.
\end{enumerate}
The errors are additive, not multiplicative.
The system lives on a product space
$[0,1]^k \times \R^2$;
convergence in each factor is independent.
No energy flows between the two subsystems through the
data pipeline, because the pipeline is sequential and
the convergence operators are orthogonal.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Recursive feasibility of the King's control]%
\label{prop:viability}
\color{black!60}%
Define the \emph{viability constraint}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:viability}
  K \;=\; \bigl\{\, \cP \in [0,1]^k \;\big|\;
  \exists\, \xi \in \cH(\cP, N, T) \;\text{with}\;
  \mathrm{NLR}(\xi) \geq 1 \,\bigr\}.
\end{equation}
That is, $K$ is the set of pool states from which the King
can find at least one not-losing rollout.
The \emph{viability kernel}
\textup{(Aubin, 1991; translating Monod's
\emph{Chance and Necessity})}
is
\[
  \mathrm{Viab}(K) \;=\; \bigl\{\, \cP_0 \in K \;\big|\;
  \exists\, \text{evolution } \cP(t) \text{ with }
  \cP(t) \in K \;\;\forall\, t \geq 0 \,\bigr\}.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}, nosep]
\item \textbf{Non-emptiness.}\;
  $\mathrm{Viab}(K) \supseteq \cF$, the free core of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:contraction}.
  In particular, $\mathrm{Viab}(K) \neq \emptyset$.

\item \textbf{Recursive feasibility.}\;
  If\/ $\cP_n \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$, there exists
  a framework selection such that
  $\cP_{n+1} \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$.
  Once inside the viability kernel, the King is never stuck.

\item \textbf{Finite reach.}\;
  For any initial state $\cP_0 \in [0,1]^k$,
  there exists a finite horizon
  $H^* < \infty$
  such that within $H^*$ games
  the pool enters $\mathrm{Viab}(K)$.
  Compactness of $[0,1]^k$ guarantees $H^*$ is finite.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\textup{(i)}\;
The free core $\cF = \{\mu^*\}$ is the SLLN limit
(Proposition~\ref{prop:contraction}).
At $\mu^*$, the pool is at equilibrium: the true win rates.
Since $\tau > 0$ ensures all frameworks are sampled
(Borel--Cantelli), and at least one framework has
$\mu_i > 0$ (the not-lose assumption), there exists
a rollout with $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$.
Hence $\mu^* \in K$.
The constant evolution $\cP(t) = \mu^*$ stays in $K$
forever, so $\mu^* \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$.

\medskip\noindent
\textup{(ii)}\;
By definition: if $\cP_n \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$,
there exists an infinite evolution staying in~$K$.
The first step of that evolution gives a framework
selection~$f^*$ such that the updated pool~$\cP_{n+1}$
remains in $\mathrm{Viab}(K)$.
This is the standard recursive-feasibility argument
of viability theory.

\medskip\noindent
\textup{(iii)}\;
$[0,1]^k$ is compact and the running average is
dissipative (factor $n/(n{+}1)$).
By the Freedom Theorem, every orbit enters~$\cF$
in finite time.
Since $\cF \subseteq \mathrm{Viab}(K)$ by~\textup{(i)},
the orbit enters the viability kernel.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[King's penny --- the primal-dual lemma]%
\label{lem:kings-penny}
\color{black!60}%
Define the \emph{MOPL Lagrangian}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mopl-lagrangian}
  \cL_{\mathrm{PD}}(\bar{w},\, \lambda)
  \;=\;
  \bar{w}^\top \hat{V}
  \;-\;
  \lambda\,\bigl(1 - \mathrm{NLR}(\bar{w})\bigr),
\end{equation}
where $\lambda \geq 0$ is the Lagrange multiplier.
In Go, $\lambda$ is the \emph{komi}: the compensation points
the King must concede and still not lose.
The penny is the komi.
The King's head is on the penny.
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}, nosep]
\item \textbf{Weak duality.}\;
  The Queen's primal optimum upper-bounds the King's
  dual guarantee:
  \[
    \underbrace{\max_{\bar{w}}\;
      \bar{w}^\top \hat{V}}_
      {\text{Queen (primal)}}
    \;\;\geq\;\;
    \underbrace{\max_\lambda\;
      \min_\tau\;
      \cL_{\mathrm{PD}}
        \;\big|\;
      \mathrm{NLR} \geq 1}_
      {\text{King (dual)}}.
  \]

\item \textbf{Per-game feasibility.}\;
  If\/ $\cP_n \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$ and the King follows
  the regulation map
  $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}^*, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}}^*)$,
  then at every game~$n$ there exists a framework selection
  with $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$.
  The constraint is \emph{per-game, not on average}.
  Not ``how to win more,'' but
  ``how to not lose at all, even after paying the komi.''

\item \textbf{Strong duality.}\;
  At the free core $\bar{w} = \mu^* \in \cF$,
  the duality gap closes to zero:
  the primal optimum and the dual feasibility
  $\cP \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$ are achieved simultaneously.
  The optimal multiplier $\lambda^*$ is the maximum komi
  at which the King can still enforce $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The asymmetry.}\;
The Queen may lose individual games---her SLLN absorbs
variance, and $\bar{w}_n \to \mu^*$ regardless.
The King may not: a single game with
$\mathrm{NLR} < 1$ at every scale violates the viability
constraint, ejecting the state from $\mathrm{Viab}(K)$.
The Queen's guarantee is \emph{statistical}
(law of large numbers);
the King's guarantee is \emph{existential}
(viability kernel membership).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Uniqueness.}\;
This is the \emph{only} primal-dual lemma in MOPL\@.
There is exactly one hard constraint ($\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$),
hence one multiplier ($\lambda =$ komi),
one dual variable ($\tau$),
one primal variable ($\bar{w}$),
and one duality gap (closing at~$\cF$).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\textup{(i)}\;
Standard weak duality: for any feasible
$(\bar{w}, \lambda)$,
$\max_{\bar{w}} \cL_{\mathrm{PD}}
 \geq \max_\lambda \min_{\bar{w}} \cL_{\mathrm{PD}}$.

\medskip\noindent
\textup{(ii)}\;
From Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}\textup{(ii)}:
if $\cP_n \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$, recursive feasibility
gives a framework selection~$f^*$ with
$\cP_{n+1} \in \mathrm{Viab}(K) \subseteq K$,
hence $\mathrm{NLR}(\xi) \geq 1$ for some
$\xi \in \cH(\cP_{n+1}, N, T)$.
Per-game guarantee by induction on~$n$.

\medskip\noindent
\textup{(iii)}\;
At $\bar{w} = \mu^*$ the Queen's primal is at its
optimum (SLLN, Proposition~\ref{prop:contraction}).
By Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}\textup{(i)},
$\mu^* \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)$, so the dual constraint
$\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$ is satisfied.
Gap $= \max \cL_{\mathrm{PD}} - \max\min \cL_{\mathrm{PD}}
     = 0$ at this point.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Viability theory: chance and necessity]%
\label{rem:viability}
\color{black!60}%
Proposition~\ref{prop:viability} is an instance of
Aubin's \emph{viability theory} (1991), which studies
the evolution of dynamical systems under constraints.
The core formulation translates Jacques Monod's
\emph{Chance and Necessity} (1970) into mathematics:
\[
  \underbrace{x'(t) \in F(x(t))}_
    {\text{chance (differential inclusion)}}
  \qquad\qquad
  \underbrace{x(t) \in K}_
    {\text{necessity (viability constraint)}}
\]
The differential inclusion $x'(t) \in F(x(t))$ is an
\emph{evolutionary engine}: at each state, there is a
\emph{set} of possible evolutions (not a single
deterministic trajectory).
The constraint $x(t) \in K$ is the hard requirement
that the evolution must never leave the allowed region.
The viability kernel $\mathrm{Viab}(K)$ is the largest
subset of~$K$ from which at least one evolution stays
in~$K$ forever.
If $\mathrm{Viab}(K) = K$: the entire environment is
viable.
If $\mathrm{Viab}(K) = \emptyset$: the environment is a
\emph{repellor}---all evolutions eventually violate the
constraints.

\medskip\noindent
The mapping to MOPL is exact:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Viability theory (Aubin)} &
\textbf{MOPL (King)} &
\textbf{Symbol} \\
\midrule
State $x(t)$ &
  Pool state + board position &
  $\cP$ \\
Constraint set $K$ &
  Not-lose region &
  $\{\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1\}$ \\
Evolutionary engine $F(x)$ &
  Reachable futures &
  $\cH(\cP, N, T)$ \\
Viability kernel &
  Free core &
  $\cF$ \\
Chance: $x'(t) \in F(x)$ &
  Framework + move selection &
  Stochastic \\
Necessity: $x(t) \in K$ &
  Not-lose at every step &
  Hard constraint \\
Regulation map &
  Temperature policy &
  $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}})$ \\
Repellor &
  All paths lose at all scales &
  Game over \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Adaptive horizon.}\;
If the King's current horizon $H$ reveals only losing
rollouts ($\cP \notin K$ under~$H$), the horizon is doubled:
$H \to 2H \to 4H \to \cdots$
until a not-losing path is found.
Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}\textup{(iii)} guarantees
termination: the finite-reach bound $H^*$ ensures
that a sufficiently long horizon always reveals a path
to the viability kernel.
In practice this is triggered at most once or twice
per championship---the multi-scale lattice
($|\Lambda_R| \times k$ independent escape routes)
makes the viability kernel large.
On a $19 \times 19$ Go board
($\sim\!2 \times 10^{170}$ legal positions,
branching factor $\sim\!250$),
each horizon doubling multiplies escape paths
exponentially; the probability that \emph{all} paths
lose at \emph{all} scales vanishes unless the opponent
is strictly dominant at every dimension.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The one assumption.}\;
Everything rests on a single structural requirement:
\emph{at least one framework has positive expected outcome
against the current opponent} ($\exists\, i : \mu_i > 0$).
If the opponent is strictly stronger at every scale
under every framework, $\mathrm{Viab}(K) = \emptyset$ and
the environment is a repellor.
In this case MOPL correctly identifies the situation
as unwinnable---the NLR gate fails, and training stops.
This is not a bug; it is the honest boundary of the
system's competence.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Belief RL and the myopia principle]%
\label{rem:belief-rl}
\color{black!60}%
The pool $\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$ \emph{is} the belief state
in the sense of partially observable RL\@.
The true framework qualities $\mu^*$ are hidden;
the Queen maintains the empirical estimate
$\bar{w}_n \to \mu^*$ (SLLN)\@.
The King plans in belief space~$[0,1]^k$,
not in state space ($\sim\!10^{170}$ board positions).
The viability kernel
$\mathrm{Viab}(K) \subset [0,1]^k$
is the set of \emph{viable beliefs}.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The myopia principle}
(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}保持短视\end{CJK}).\;
Keep horizon $H$ small: operate in a low-dimensional belief
projection.  Expand $H$ only when the current belief says
``stuck'' (all rollouts lose).
This is belief RL's exploration--exploitation balance:
\emph{exploit} current belief (small~$H$, cheap);
\emph{explore} only when forced (double~$H$, expensive).

\medskip\noindent
The $10^{170}$ combinatorial guarantee ensures that
``forced'' is rare.
With branching factor $\sim\!250$ and
$|\Lambda_R| \times k$ independent
scale\,$\times$\,framework channels,
the belief must be catastrophically wrong at every
dimension simultaneously for the King to need horizon
expansion.
The one assumption ($\exists\, i : \mu_i > 0$) ensures
this cannot persist: the Queen's SLLN convergence
corrects any transient belief error in $O(1/\sqrt{n})$
games.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Amortized King (mean action scheduler)]%
\label{def:amortized-king}
\color{black!60}%
Let $f_\theta\colon [0,1]^k \to \R^2$ be a small MLP
trained to predict optimal log-temperatures
($\tau = e^\theta$, cf.\ Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}):
\[
  \hat{\theta} \;=\; f_\theta(\bar{w})
  \;\approx\; \theta^*(\bar{w})
  \;=\; \arg\min_\theta \cL(e^\theta;\, \bar{w},\, M_H).
\]
The \emph{online distillation protocol} is:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}, nosep]
\item At game $n$: warm-start GD at
  $\hat{\theta}_n = f_\theta(\bar{w}_n)$.
\item Run $J \ll 100$ gradient steps $\to \theta^*_n$.
\item Store $(\bar{w}_n, \theta^*_n)$ in a replay buffer
  of size~$B$.
\item Every $B_u$ games ($B_u \leq B$): update $\theta$
  by SGD on
  $\|f_\theta(\bar{w}) - \theta^*\|^2$.
\end{enumerate}
The NN is a \emph{learned gauge field on belief space}:
it maps each belief $\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$ to the
optimal control $\tau^*(\bar{w}) \in \R^2$.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Softmax field on belief space]%
\label{rem:softmax-field}
\color{black!60}%
Without the amortized King,
the controller~(Definition~\ref{def:two-temp})
has $\theta = (\theta_{\mathrm{UV}}, \theta_{\mathrm{IR}})
\in \R^2$---a constant vector, not a field.
The amortized King promotes it to a map
$f_\theta \colon [0,1]^k \to \R^2$---an MLP,
i.e.\ a deterministic gauge field on belief space
(Proposition~\ref{prop:gauge}).

Composing with the two nested softmaxes gives the
\emph{softmax field}:
\[
  \bar{w}
  \;\xmapsto{\;f_\theta\;}
  (\tau_{\mathrm{IR}},\, \tau_{\mathrm{UV}})
  \;\xmapsto{\;\softmax\;}
  (\pi_f,\, \pi_{\mathrm{scale}}).
\]
The field's value at each belief $\bar{w}$ is not
a number---it is a \emph{Boltzmann distribution}.
Each softmax is a partition function
(Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation}):
\[
  \pi_f
  = \frac{e^{\,\log \bar{w}\,/\,\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}}}
         {Z_{\mathrm{IR}}},
  \qquad
  \pi_{\mathrm{scale}}
  = \frac{e^{\,\hat{V}\,/\,\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}}}
         {Z_{\mathrm{UV}}},
\]
where $Z_{\mathrm{IR}}, Z_{\mathrm{UV}}$ are the
normalising constants.
The composed map
$\bar{w} \mapsto (\pi_f, \pi_{\mathrm{scale}})$
is the same structure as $z = \sigma(Wx)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:gauge}):
MLP weights determine the field,
softmax determines the distribution,
and the free energy
$\cL = -\pi_{\mathrm{scale}}^\top \hat{V}$
is the invariant under reparametrisation of~$\theta$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Distillation as RG flow]%
\label{rem:rg-distillation}
\color{black!60}%
The amortized King instantiates the RG pattern of
model distillation:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{RG scale} & \textbf{King's control} & \textbf{Cost} \\
\midrule
UV (full resolution) &
  100-step GD from scratch &
  $O(100 \cdot k)$ per game \\
IR (compressed) &
  NN forward pass + $J$-step refinement &
  $O(k^2 + J \cdot k)$ per game \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
As the NN converges, $J$ shrinks---the
residual GD becomes a perturbative correction around
the field's prediction.
The distillation is \emph{online}: the King teaches
itself while playing.
The sharp test is the \emph{warm-start gap}:
$\|\hat{\tau}_n - \tau^*_n\| \to 0$ as $n \to \infty$.
When the gap closes, the King has learned to see
without searching
(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}不搜而视\end{CJK}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The transcommutation triangle:
  Drunk--Queen--King]%
\label{rem:transcommutation-triangle}
\color{black!60}%
The three agents in MOPL---Drunk, Queen, King---look
like three separate ideas.
They are one idea evaluated at three temperatures.

\medskip\noindent
Recall the free energy
(Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation}):
\[
  F(\tau) \;=\; \min_p \;\bigl[\,
    \underbrace{\mathbb{E}_p[\,E\,]}_{\text{energy (order)}}
    \;+\;
    \tau\,
    \underbrace{H(p)}_{\text{entropy (disorder)}}
  \,\bigr].
\]
The minimiser $p^*(\tau)$ is the Boltzmann distribution
at temperature~$\tau$.
At three temperatures it yields three agents:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Temperature} &
\textbf{Agent} &
\textbf{Minimiser $p^*$} &
\textbf{Role in MOPL} \\
\midrule
$\tau \to \infty$ &
  Drunk &
  $\mathrm{Uniform}$ (max entropy) &
  Reference measure $\rho^*$ \\
$\tau \to 0$ &
  Queen &
  $\arg\max\; V$ (max order) &
  Primal: maximise expected value \\
$\tau = \lambda$ (komi) &
  King &
  Saddle point of $\cL_{\mathrm{PD}}$ &
  Dual: enforce $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The three edges of the triangle are:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Edge} &
\textbf{Relationship} &
\textbf{Mathematical content} \\
\midrule
Drunk $\leftrightarrow$ Queen &
  Transcommutation &
  $F(\rho^*) = F(\pi^*)$;\;
  energy $\leftrightarrow$ entropy swap \\
Queen $\leftrightarrow$ King &
  Primal--dual &
  Strong duality at $\cF$;\;
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kings-penny} \\
King $\leftrightarrow$ Drunk &
  Viability test &
  Drunk samples $\mathrm{Viab}(K)$;\;
  Prop.~\ref{prop:viability} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
\textbf{The triangle closes.}\;
The SVOT loss (Definition~\ref{def:svot})
encodes this triangle in a single expression:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:svot-triangle}
  \cL(\theta)
  \;=\;
  \underbrace{F(\pi_\theta)}_
    {\substack{\text{Queen's objective:}\\\text{minimise free energy}}}
  \;-\;
  \underbrace{F(\rho^*)}_
    {\substack{\text{Drunk's baseline:}\\\text{reference free energy}}}
  \;\geq\; 0,
\end{equation}
with equality if and only if $\pi_\theta = \rho^*$
(the policy \emph{is} the Drunk).
The King's constraint $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$
is the feasibility condition that keeps $\pi_\theta$
inside $\mathrm{Viab}(K)$ during the descent from
$\cL > 0$ to $\cL = 0$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Training is annealing on the triangle.}\;
At initialisation, $\pi_\theta \approx \rho^*$
(random weights $\Rightarrow$ near-uniform policy):
the agent starts at the Drunk vertex.
As training progresses:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item The King's constraint $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$
  activates---the agent crosses the
  Drunk--King edge (viability test).
  The komi $\lambda$ sets the operating temperature.
\item The Queen's primal objective drives
  $\bar{w} \to \mu^*$---the agent crosses the
  King--Queen edge (primal--dual convergence).
  The duality gap closes at $\cF$.
\item At convergence, $F(\pi^*) = F(\rho^*)$ and
  the SVOT loss reaches zero---the agent
  has traversed the Queen--Drunk edge
  (transcommutation).
  The trained policy and the Drunk reference have
  the \emph{same free energy},
  redistributed from entropy to order.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The coin.}\;
The fair coin in the Drunk Game ($p = \tfrac{1}{2}$)
is the self-dual point of the transcommutation
(Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation}).
One face is strategy (Queen).
The other face is randomness (Drunk).
The edge is the King's constraint.
The wrong-vacuum detection in
Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}
flips the coin back:
when the Queen gets stuck
($\|F\|^2 < \varepsilon_F$ and
$\mathrm{Hol} \approx \mathrm{Id}$),
fire a Drunk burst---return momentarily to
$\tau = \infty$.
The instanton is a transcommutation event.
\end{remark}

% ── §11.7: End-to-end learning via Drunk Walk ─────────────
\subsection{End-to-end learning via Drunk Walk}\label{sec:e2e}

The Drunk Walk (Algorithm~\ref{alg:drunk-walk}) is the
\emph{only} end-to-end differentiable component in MOPL\@.
The Queen evolves framework weights by running averages
(evolutionary, no gradient).
The King optimises two temperatures by gradient descent
(Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}), but this is a
$2$-parameter controller, not a policy.
The Amortized King (Definition~\ref{def:amortized-king})
distils the King into an MLP, but the MLP maps
belief to temperature, not observation to action.

Only the SVOT decomposition (Definition~\ref{def:svot})
provides a loss function for a \emph{full policy}
$\pi_\theta \colon \cS \to \Delta(\cA)$:

\begin{definition}[SVOT policy gradient]\label{def:svot-pg}
Let $\pi_\theta$ be a parametric policy (neural network)
with $\theta \in \R^d$.
The \emph{SVOT loss} is the free energy excess relative
to the Drunk reference:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:svot-loss}
  \cL(\theta)
  \;=\;
  F(\pi_\theta) - F(\rho^*_N)
  \;=\;
  \underbrace{\bigl(\mathbb{E}_{\pi_\theta}[E]
    - \mathbb{E}_{\rho^*}[E]\bigr)}_{\Delta E(\theta)}
  \;+\;
  \underbrace{\DKL(\pi_\theta \,\|\, \rho^*_N)}_{%
    \text{entropy cost}}\,.
\end{equation}
The gradient decomposes as
\[
  \nabla_\theta \cL
  \;=\;
  \nabla_\theta \mathbb{E}_{\pi_\theta}[E]
  \;+\;
  \nabla_\theta \DKL(\pi_\theta \,\|\, \rho^*_N).
\]
The first term is the policy gradient (REINFORCE or
pathwise estimator).
The second is the entropy regularisation gradient.
Both are computable by auto-differentiation
through~$\pi_\theta$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[SVOT $=$ Soft Actor-Critic]%
\label{prop:svot-sac}
The SVOT loss~\eqref{eq:svot-loss} is the
SAC objective~\cite{Haarnoja2018} with
$\rho^*_N$ as the max-entropy reference and
$\alpha = 1$ as the entropy coefficient:
\[
  J_{\mathrm{SAC}}(\pi)
  \;=\;
  \sum_t \mathbb{E}_{\pi}\bigl[r_t
    + \alpha\, H\!\bigl(\pi(\cdot \mid s_t)\bigr)\bigr]
  \;=\;
  -\cL(\theta) + \mathrm{const}.
\]
The identification is:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{SVOT (this paper)} &
\textbf{SAC} &
\textbf{Role} \\
\midrule
$\rho^*_N$ (Drunk Walk) &
  Max-entropy reference &
  Variational origin \\
$\Delta E$ &
  Expected return &
  Reward signal \\
$\DKL(\pi \| \rho^*)$ &
  $-\alpha\, H(\pi)$ &
  Entropy regularisation \\
Temperature $\tau$ &
  $\alpha$ &
  Exploration--exploitation \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The Drunk Walk
(Algorithm~\ref{alg:drunk-walk})
produces $\rho^*_N =
\mathrm{Bernoulli}(\tfrac{1}{2})
\otimes \mathrm{Uniform}(V \setminus O)$,
the maximum-entropy policy on the Go state space.
Substituting into~\eqref{eq:svot}:
$F(\pi_\theta) = F(\rho^*_N) + \Delta E + \DKL$.
Negating and adding the constant $F(\rho^*_N)$ gives
$-\cL(\theta) = -\Delta E - \DKL + \mathrm{const}
= J_{\mathrm{SAC}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Domain-agnostic extension:
  from board to body]%
\label{rem:domain-agnostic}
\color{black!60}%
The SVOT decomposition~\eqref{eq:svot} requires only:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}, nosep]
\item a state space $\cS$
  (Go: $N \times N$ grid;
   robotics: $\R^n$),
\item an action space $\cA$
  (Go: $N^2 + 1$;
   robotics: $\R^m$),
\item a reference measure $\rho^*$
  (Go: Drunk Walk;
   robotics: random actions),
\item a scalar reward
  $r : \cS \times \cA \to \R$
  (Go: territory score;
   robotics: task objective).
\end{enumerate}
Replacing the Go board with a physics simulator
(e.g.\ MuJoCo) and the rule-based Thinker--Goer
with a neural policy
$\pi_\theta : \cS \to \cA$ gives end-to-end
differentiable control:
\[
  \text{observation}
  \;\xrightarrow{\;g_\phi\;}
  \text{state}
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\pi_\theta\;}
  \text{action}
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\text{dynamics}\;}
  \text{reward},
\]
where $g_\phi$ is an optional encoder
(CNN, ViT, or 3D Gaussian splatting for visual inputs).
The gradient $\nabla_\theta \cL$ pulls back through
the entire pipeline.

\medskip\noindent
The Drunk Walk is not a Go algorithm---it is the
\emph{variational origin} for any sequential decision
process.
The board is a proof of concept.
The loss function is the contribution.
\end{remark}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
% §11.8  Locomotion instantiation
% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

\subsection{Instantiation: quadruped locomotion on the Euler--Lagrange equation}
\label{sec:locomotion}

The Euler--Lagrange equation is not an analogy for a game board.
It \emph{is} the board.
A physics simulator (MuJoCo, Brax, or a hand-written integrator)
is a numerical solver of that equation,
exactly as KataGo is a numerical player of the Go rules.
The mathematics is the constrained EL system;
everything else---time-stepping scheme, collision library,
GPU backend---is implementation.

This section instantiates every object from
\S\ref{sec:e2e}
on a concrete physical system:
the Unitree Go2 quadruped robot.
Every number below is extracted from the
MuJoCo Menagerie model (\texttt{go2\_mjx.xml})
and verified against the manufacturer's URDF.
A reader who knows nothing about Go, pools, or MOPL
should be able to read this section and
understand the state, action, constraint, pool,
reference measure, and loss---then recognise them
as the \emph{same} objects that appeared on the $19\times 19$ board.

%% ── Block 2: EL universe ──────────────────────────────────

\begin{definition}[Euler--Lagrange universe]
\label{def:el-universe}
The \emph{EL universe} is the constrained
Euler--Lagrange equation with contact:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:el-contact}
  M(q)\,\ddot{q}
  + C(q,\dot{q})\,\dot{q}
  + g(q)
  \;=\;
  B\,\tau
  + J_c(q)^{\!\top}\lambda,
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $q \in \mathcal{Q}$ --- configuration
      (generalised coordinates),
\item $M(q) \succ 0$ --- mass--inertia matrix
      (symmetric positive-definite, $\dim = n_q \times n_q$),
\item $C(q,\dot{q})$ --- Coriolis and centrifugal terms,
\item $g(q)$ --- gravitational generalised force,
\item $B \in \R^{n_q \times m}$ --- actuation matrix
      (selects which joints receive torque;
       for a fully actuated limb $B$ is a rectangular selector),
\item $\tau \in \R^{m}$ --- joint torques
      (the \emph{only} quantity the agent controls),
\item $J_c(q) \in \R^{n_c \times n_q}$ --- contact Jacobian
      (maps generalised velocities to foot-frame velocities
       at each active contact point),
\item $\lambda \in \R^{n_c}$ --- contact impulses,
      resolved by the complementarity condition below.
\end{itemize}
The contact law is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:contact-complementarity}
  0 \leq \lambda \;\perp\; J_c\,\dot{q} \geq 0
  \quad\text{(Signorini)},
  \qquad
  \norm{\lambda_t} \leq \mu\,\lambda_n
  \quad\text{(Coulomb cone)},
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_n, \lambda_t$ are the normal and tangential
components at each contact, and $\mu$ is the friction coefficient.

\medskip\noindent\textbf{Key property.}\;
Equation~\eqref{eq:el-contact} is a
\emph{differential inclusion}, not an ODE,
because the contact mode switches discretely:
when a foot lifts off, the corresponding rows of $J_c$
vanish; when a foot strikes down, new rows appear.
The contact Jacobian $J_c$ changes rank at each
mode transition.
The set of active contacts at time $t$ partitions
the dynamics into finitely many smooth ODE branches
glued along switching surfaces.
\end{definition}

%% ── Block 3: Quadruped state--action ──────────────────────

\begin{definition}[Quadruped state and action spaces]
\label{def:quadruped-state}
Instantiate Definition~\ref{def:el-universe}
for the Unitree Go2 quadruped.
All values are from the MuJoCo Menagerie model
(\texttt{go2\_mjx.xml}).

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Symbol} & \textbf{Dim} & \textbf{Description}
  & \textbf{Go2 value} \\
\midrule
$q$ & 18 & Configuration: $\mathrm{SE}(3) \times \R^{12}$
  & 6 base + 12 joints \\
$\dot{q}$ & 18 & Generalised velocity
  & base twist + joint velocities \\
$\tau$ & 12 & Joint torques
  & 4 legs $\times$ 3 joints \\
$m_{\mathrm{base}}$ & --- & Base mass
  & 6.921\,kg \\
$\ell_{\mathrm{thigh}}$ & --- & Thigh link length
  & 0.213\,m \\
$\ell_{\mathrm{calf}}$ & --- & Calf link length
  & 0.213\,m \\
$h_{\mathrm{stand}}$ & --- & Standing height (CoM)
  & 0.312\,m \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Joint limits per leg} (radians):
ab/ad $\in [-0.863,\; 0.863]$,
hip $\in [-1.047,\; 3.490]$,
knee $\in [-2.697,\; {-0.837}]$.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{Torque limits} (Nm):
$[23.7,\; 23.7,\; 35.55]$ for ab/ad, hip, knee respectively.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{Velocity limit}: $21.0$\,rad/s per joint.
\textbf{Control rate}: 50\,Hz ($\Delta t = 0.02$\,s).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Observation} (what the agent receives at each step):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:quadruped-obs}
  x \;=\;
  \bigl(\,
    R,\; p,\; \omega,\; v,\;
    \theta,\; \dot{\theta}
  \,\bigr)
  \;\in\; \R^{42},
\end{equation}
where
$R \in \mathrm{SO}(3)$ flattened to $\R^9$,\;
$p \in \R^3$ (CoM position),\;
$\omega \in \R^3$ (angular velocity),\;
$v \in \R^3$ (linear velocity),\;
$\theta \in \R^{12}$ (joint angles),\;
$\dot{\theta} \in \R^{12}$ (joint velocities).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Action} = torque:
$u = \tau \in \R^{12}$,
subject to $|\tau_i| \leq \bar{\tau}_i$
for each joint $i$.

\medskip\noindent
The state is what the robot sees.
The action is the only thing it can do.
\end{definition}

%% ── Block 4: Contact mode lattice ─────────────────────────

\begin{definition}[Contact mode lattice]
\label{def:contact-mode}
Each foot is either in contact with the ground ($1$)
or in the air ($0$).
The \emph{contact mode} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:contact-mode}
  c \;=\;
  (c_{\mathrm{FL}},\, c_{\mathrm{FR}},\,
   c_{\mathrm{RL}},\, c_{\mathrm{RR}})
  \;\in\; \{0,1\}^4,
  \qquad
  |\cC| = 2^4 = 16.
\end{equation}
These are the pool frameworks
(Definition~\ref{def:executor-assembling}).
Not gaits---contact modes.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Mode $c$} & \textbf{Binary}
  & \textbf{Active feet}
  & \textbf{Example gait phase} \\
\midrule
$(1,1,1,1)$ & 1111 & All four & Standing \\
$(1,0,0,1)$ & 1001 & FL + RR  & Trot phase A \\
$(0,1,1,0)$ & 0110 & FR + RL  & Trot phase B \\
$(1,1,0,0)$ & 1100 & Front pair & Bound phase A \\
$(0,0,0,0)$ & 0000 & None     & Flight \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
A \emph{gait} is a temporal sequence of contact modes.
Trot $= \ldots,\, c_A,\, c_B,\, c_A,\, c_B,\, \ldots$
where $c_A = (1,0,0,1)$ and $c_B = (0,1,1,0)$.
Gaits \emph{emerge} from the pool dynamics;
the pool does not prescribe them.

The agent never selects a contact mode.
It outputs torques; the EL engine resolves contact;
the mode \emph{emerges}.
The empirical distribution over modes
$\hat{p}(c) = T^{-1}\sum_{t} \mathbf{1}[c_t = c]$
is a \emph{diagnostic statistic} of the policy,
not a decision variable.
It lives on $\Delta^{15}$ ($k = 16$ vertices),
and its temporal structure---which modes follow which,
at what frequency---is what we recognise post hoc as a gait.
\end{definition}

%% ── Block 5: Command space and Drunk Command ──────────────

\begin{definition}[Command space]
\label{def:command-space}
The \emph{command} is the centre-of-mass (CoM) velocity:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:command}
  v_{\mathrm{cmd}}
  \;=\;
  (v_x,\, v_y,\, \omega_z)
  \;\in\; \R^3.
\end{equation}
This is the \emph{only} legitimate command.
Anything beyond CoM velocity
(specific foot placement, hip angle)
is either redundancy resolved by the contact mode
selection, or undefined:
the robot has 12 actuators but only 3 command
dimensions---the 9-dimensional null space is
the contact mode's job.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Drunk Command (Markov kernel form)]
\label{def:drunk-command}
Let $o \in \cS$ be the agent's observation
(proprioception, or proprioception + vision).
The \emph{Drunk Command kernel} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:drunk-command-kernel}
  \rho^*(\cdot \mid o)
  \;=\;
  \mathrm{Uniform}\!\bigl(\cR(o)\bigr),
  \qquad
  \cR(o) \subset \R^3,
\end{equation}
where $\cR(o)$ is the reachable command set
\emph{conditioned on the current observation}
(determined by the viability kernel
at the observed state).
Sample $v_{\mathrm{cmd}} \sim \rho^*(\cdot \mid o)$;
apply for a random duration
$T \sim \mathrm{Exp}(\lambda)$; then resample.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Blind case} (hard Riccati, proprioception only):\;
$\cR(o) = \cR$ is constant.
The kernel degenerates to the marginal
$\mathrm{Uniform}(\cR)$.
This is Definition~\ref{def:drunk-game}
on a different substrate.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Sighted case} (soft Riccati, with vision):\;
$\cR(o)$ contracts near obstacles
(a robot facing a wall has smaller $\cR$
than one on flat ground)
and expands on open terrain.
The kernel conditions the reference measure
on what the robot sees---the soft Riccati upgrade
costs nothing structurally
(same algorithm, same loss,
the observation $o$ simply carries more information).

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
 & \textbf{Go} & \textbf{Locomotion} \\
\midrule
Strategy
  & Where to place stone
  & Which torques to apply \\
Randomness
  & $\mathrm{Uniform}(V \setminus O)$
  & $\rho^*(\cdot \mid o)
    = \mathrm{Uniform}\!\bigl(\cR(o)\bigr)$ \\
Self-dual point
  & $p = 1/2$ (fair coin)
  & $v_{\mathrm{cmd}} = 0$ (stand still) \\
Blind $\to$ sighted
  & Text $\to$ image input
  & Proprioception $\to$ vision \\
Free energy preserved
  & Territory topology
  & Viability kernel \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{definition}

%% ── Block 6: Viability constraint ─────────────────────────

\begin{definition}[Viability constraint for locomotion]
\label{def:viability-locomotion}
The \emph{viable set} for locomotion is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:viable-loco}
  K_{\mathrm{loco}}
  \;=\;
  \bigl\{\,
    x \in \cX \;:\;
    h(x) \geq h_{\min},\;\;
    \norm{R_{\mathrm{body}} - I}_F \leq \phi_{\max},\;\;
    |\dot{\theta}_i| \leq \bar{v},\;\;
    |\tau_i| \leq \bar{\tau}_i
  \,\bigr\},
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $h(x) \geq h_{\min}$:
      CoM height above ground (not fallen),
\item $\norm{R_{\mathrm{body}} - I}_F \leq \phi_{\max}$:
      body orientation within bounds (not flipped),
\item $|\dot{\theta}_i| \leq \bar{v}$:
      joint velocity limits ($\bar{v} = 21.0$\,rad/s),
\item $|\tau_i| \leq \bar{\tau}_i$:
      torque limits ($[23.7,\; 23.7,\; 35.55]$\,Nm).
\end{itemize}
The correspondence to Go:
\[
  \underbrace{\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1}_{\text{Go: not-lose}}
  \quad\longleftrightarrow\quad
  \underbrace{x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}}_{\text{Robot: not-fall}}.
\]
The \emph{viability kernel}
$\mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})$
is the largest subset of $K_{\mathrm{loco}}$
from which there exists a control law keeping
$x(t) \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$ for all $t \geq 0$.
This is Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}
instantiated for locomotion,
with the King's Penny (Lemma~\ref{lem:kings-penny})
providing the exit certificate.
\end{definition}

%% ── Block 7: MOPL--Locomotion isomorphism ─────────────────

\begin{remark}[MOPL--Locomotion isomorphism]
\label{rem:mopl-locomotion-iso}
The following table extends
Remark~\ref{rem:chess-iso}
from bilevel optimisation to the full pipeline.
Every row except the last is mathematics;
only the last row mentions software.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.8cm}p{5.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Layer}
  & \textbf{Go (MOPL)}
  & \textbf{Quadruped (this section)} \\
\midrule
Universe
  & Go rules on $N \times N$ lattice
  & EL equation~\eqref{eq:el-contact}:
    $M\ddot{q} + C\dot{q} + g
     = B\tau + J_c^{\!\top}\lambda$ \\[3pt]
State
  & Board position $s \in \{-1,0,1\}^{N^2}$
  & $(R, p, \omega, v, \theta, \dot{\theta})
    \in \R^{42}$ \\[3pt]
Action
  & Place stone at $v \in V \setminus O$
  & Torque $\tau \in \R^{12}$,
    $|\tau_i| \leq \bar{\tau}_i$ \\[3pt]
Command
  & ``Win the game'' (scalar)
  & CoM skew
    $(v_x, v_y, \omega_z) \in \R^3$ \\[3pt]
Constraint
  & $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$ (not lose)
  & $x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$ (not fall) \\[3pt]
Pool
  & 5 strategic frameworks, $\Delta^4$
  & 16 contact modes $\{0,1\}^4$,
    $\Delta^{15}$ (emergent diagnostic) \\[3pt]
Frameworks
  & territorial, influence, \ldots
  & $(1,1,1,1)$, $(1,0,0,1)$, \ldots \\[3pt]
Gaits
  & ---
  & Emerge: temporal sequences
    of contact modes \\[3pt]
Perception
  & Board is fully observed
  & $g_\phi: o \to x \in \R^{42}$
    (blind: identity; sighted: encoder) \\[3pt]
Drunk ref.
  & $\mathrm{Bernoulli}(1/2) \otimes
    \mathrm{Uniform}(V \setminus O)$
  & $\rho^*(\cdot \mid o)
    = \mathrm{Uniform}\!\bigl(\cR(o)\bigr)$
    (kernel) \\[3pt]
Free space
  & Free core $\cF \subseteq \mathrm{Viab}(K)$
  & $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}
    \cong \mathrm{SE}(2) \times
    \cF_{\mathrm{shape}}$ (standing) \\[3pt]
Viability
  & $\mathrm{Viab}(K) = \mathrm{Push}(\cF)$
  & $\mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})
    = \bigcup_\Gamma
    \mathrm{Orbit}_\Gamma(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})$ \\[3pt]
Holonomy
  & ---
  & $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) \in \mathrm{SE}(3)$:
    net displacement per gait cycle \\[3pt]
SVOT loss
  & $\cL = \Delta E
    + \DKL(\pi \| \rho^*)$
  & Same, $\rho^* = $ Drunk Command kernel \\[3pt]
Gradient
  & $\nabla_\theta$ through policy
  & $\nabla_{(\phi,\theta)}$ through
    encoder + policy; not through
    $\mathrm{Step}$ \\[3pt]
Scale lattice
  & $\Lambda_R = \{5,7,\ldots,31\}$
    board sizes
  & Terrain difficulty / command range /
    duration \\[3pt]
\midrule
Simulator
  & KataGo
  & MuJoCo / Brax / any EL integrator \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
The simulator row is the \emph{only} row that mentions
software.
Every other row is mathematics.
\end{remark}

%% ── Flow diagram ──────────────────────────────────────────

\begin{figure}[ht]
\centering
\begin{tikzpicture}[
  >=Stealth,
  node distance=1.6cm and 1.8cm,
  layer/.style={
    draw=none, fill=#1, rounded corners=3pt,
    minimum height=1.0cm, minimum width=2.2cm,
    align=center, font=\small},
  learn/.style={
    draw=orange!70!black, fill=orange!10,
    rounded corners=3pt,
    minimum height=1.0cm, minimum width=2.4cm,
    align=center, font=\small},
  buf/.style={
    draw=yellow!70!black, fill=yellow!15,
    rounded corners=3pt,
    minimum height=0.7cm, minimum width=2.0cm,
    align=center, font=\small},
  diag/.style={
    draw=orange!50!black, fill=orange!5,
    rounded corners=2pt,
    minimum width=2.4cm,
    align=center, font=\scriptsize},
  grad/.style={->, thick, blue!70!black, dashed},
  flow/.style={->, thick, black},
  nogo/.style={->, thick, red!60!black,
    decorate, decoration={zigzag, amplitude=1pt,
    segment length=4pt}},
  burst/.style={->, thick, orange!70!red, dashed},
  lbl/.style={font=\footnotesize\bfseries},
]
% ── Column anchors ──
% col0: layer labels, col1: input, col2: NN box,
% col3: output, col4: feedback margin,
% col5: learn column (right)

% ── Layer 1: Perception ──
\node[lbl, green!50!black] (L1) {Layer 1};
\node[layer=green!12, right=1.0cm of L1] (sensor)
  {Sensor\\[-2pt]
  {\scriptsize proprioception / camera}};
\node[layer=green!12, right=of sensor] (encoder)
  {$g_\phi$\\[-2pt] {\scriptsize encoder (NN)}};
\node[right=1.0cm of encoder, font=\small] (state)
  {$x_t \in \R^{42}$};

% ── Layer 2: Policy ──
\node[lbl, blue!50!black,
  below=2.0cm of L1] (L2) {Layer 2};
\node[font=\scriptsize, text=black!60, align=center,
  right=0.3cm of L2] (drunk)
  {$\rho^*(\cdot \mid o)$\\[-1pt]Drunk kernel};
\node[font=\small, right=0.4cm of drunk] (cmd)
  {$v_{\mathrm{cmd}}$};
\node[layer=blue!12,
  right=0.6cm of cmd] (policy)
  {$\pi_\theta$\\[-2pt] {\scriptsize policy (NN)}};
\node[right=1.0cm of policy, font=\small] (torque)
  {$u_t \in \R^{12}$};

% ── Layer 3: Physics ──
\node[lbl, red!50!black,
  below=2.0cm of L2] (L3) {Layer 3};
\node[layer=red!12,
  below=2.0cm of policy] (engine)
  {$\mathrm{Step}$\\[-2pt]
  {\scriptsize EL engine (black box)}};
\node[right=1.0cm of engine, font=\small] (next)
  {$x_{t+1}$};
\node[below=0.5cm of engine, font=\scriptsize,
  text=black!60] (contact)
  {$c_t \in \{0,1\}^4$ (emergent)};

% ── Forward arrows ──
\draw[flow] (sensor) -- (encoder);
\draw[flow] (encoder) -- (state);
\draw[flow] (state.south) -- ++(0,-0.55)
  -| (policy.north);
\draw[flow] (drunk) -- (cmd);
\draw[flow] (cmd) -- (policy);
\draw[flow] (policy) -- (torque);
\draw[flow] (torque.south) -- ++(0,-0.55)
  -| (engine.north);
\draw[flow] (engine) -- (next);
\draw[flow] (engine) -- (contact);

% ── State → Step (x_t also feeds physics) ──
\coordinate (stR) at ($(state.east)+(0.3,0)$);
\coordinate (engR) at ($(engine.east)+(0.3,0)$);
\draw[flow, gray!50] (state.east) -- (stR)
  -- (stR |- engR) -- (engine.east);

% ── Feedback loop (raised + fold-down into sensor) ──
\coordinate (fbR) at ($(next.east)+(0.6,0)$);
\coordinate (fbTop) at ($(sensor.north)+(0,0.6)$);
\draw[flow, gray!50] (next.east) -- (fbR)
  -- (fbR |- fbTop) -- (fbTop) -- (sensor.north)
  node[font=\scriptsize, gray, pos=0.35, above=1pt]
  {next step};

% ── Reward + Replay buffer ──
\node[font=\small, below=0.5cm of contact] (reward)
  {$r_t$};
\node[font=\scriptsize, text=black!50,
  right=0.1cm of reward] (rewardlbl)
  {reward};
\draw[flow] (contact.south) -- (reward.north);

\node[buf, below=0.4cm of reward] (buffer)
  {$\mathcal{B}$\\[-2pt]
  {\scriptsize replay buffer}};
\draw[flow] (reward) -- (buffer);

% ── Learn block (right column) ──
\node[learn, right=3.0cm of buffer,
  minimum height=2.0cm] (learn)
  {%
  $\delta = Q_\psi - y$\\[-1pt]
  {\scriptsize \textbf{curvature} $F$}\\[4pt]
  {\scriptsize Critic: $\tfrac12\delta^2$
    (Yang--Mills)}\\[1pt]
  {\scriptsize Actor: $\alpha\,D_{\mathrm{KL}}$
    (Faddeev--Popov)}};
\node[lbl, orange!60!black,
  above=0.2cm of learn] (learnlbl) {Learn};

\draw[flow] (buffer) -- (learn)
  node[font=\scriptsize, pos=0.5, above=1pt]
  {sample};

% ── Gauge diagnostics ──
\node[diag, below=0.5cm of learn] (gauge)
  {$\alpha \gets \alpha \cdot
    \mathrm{clip}\bigl(
      \mathbb{E}[\delta^2]/\|F\|^2_{\mathrm{ref}}
    \bigr)$\\[2pt]
  wrong vacuum $\Rightarrow$ Drunk burst
    {\scriptsize (instanton)}};
\node[lbl, orange!50!black,
  above left=0.1cm and 0.0cm of gauge]
  (gaugelbl) {\scriptsize diagnostics};

\draw[flow] (learn) -- (gauge);

% ── Gradient arrows from Learn back to NN blocks ──
% ∇_φ: up from learn (+3pt right), -| to encoder
\draw[grad] ([xshift=3pt]learn.north)
  -- ++(0,0.6) -| (encoder.south east)
  node[font=\scriptsize, blue!70!black,
    pos=0.95, left=1pt] {$\nabla_\phi$};
% ∇_θ: up from learn (-3pt left), left to policy
\draw[grad] ([xshift=-3pt]learn.north)
  -- ([xshift=-3pt]learn.north |- policy.south east)
  -- (policy.south east)
  node[font=\scriptsize, blue!70!black,
    near end, below=1pt] {$\nabla_\theta$};

% ── No-gradient marker on physics ──
\draw[nogo] ([yshift=-2pt]next.south west)
  -- ([yshift=2pt]engine.north east)
  node[font=\scriptsize, red!60!black,
    pos=0.5, left=1pt] {no $\nabla$};

% ── Drunk burst: instanton — left from gauge, up to ρ* ──
\draw[burst] (gauge.west) -| (drunk.south)
  node[font=\scriptsize, orange!70!red,
    pos=0.3, below=2pt]
  {Drunk burst {\scriptsize(instanton)}};

\end{tikzpicture}

\caption{Forward--Learn pipeline of
  Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}.
  \emph{Left}: three-layer forward pass
  (perception, policy, physics).
  \emph{Right}: Learn block---critic loss
  $= \tfrac12\delta^2$ (Yang--Mills),
  actor loss $= \alpha\,D_{\mathrm{KL}}$
  (Faddeev--Popov).
  Blue dashed: gradient flows
  ($\nabla_\phi$ through encoder,
   $\nabla_\theta$ through policy).
  Red zigzag: no gradient through the EL engine.
  Orange dashed: Drunk burst (instanton from
  wrong-vacuum detection;
  Remark~\ref{rem:gauge-alg}).
  Gauge diagnostics adapt $\alpha$ to curvature
  (asymptotic freedom).
  The contact mode $c_t$ is an \emph{output}
  of Layer~3 (emergent), not an input
  to Layer~2.}
\label{fig:locomotion-pipeline}
\end{figure}

%% ── Block 8: Model-free = modelling the free ──────────────

\begin{remark}[Model-free = modelling the free]
\label{rem:model-free-locomotion}
The agent does \emph{not} know
$M(q)$, $C(q,\dot{q})$, $g(q)$,
$J_c(q)$, $\mu$, or $\lambda$.
It sees only:
\[
  x_t
  \;\xrightarrow{\;u_t\;}
  x_{t+1}.
\]
One state, one action, one next state.

What it learns:
the viability kernel
$\mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})$---the set of states
from which not-fall is achievable.
This \emph{is} the free core $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
of the Freedom Theorem
(Definition~\ref{def:free-space-locomotion}
makes this precise:
$\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ is the standing equilibrium
manifold from which all viable behaviours
are reachable).

``Model-free'' means the agent does not model
$M$, $C$, $g$ (the ``model'').
It models $\cF$ (the ``free'').
This is not a pun---it is the content of
Remark~\ref{rem:model-free}.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Why time-varying cost is forced.}\;
The reachable command set $\cR(t,x)$ depends on the
current state.
A robot about to fall has a smaller $\cR$ than one
standing upright.
The cost function must therefore be state-dependent,
hence time-varying.
This is not a design choice---it is structurally forced
by the viability constraint,
exactly as the King's Penny
(Lemma~\ref{lem:kings-penny})
forces state-dependent discounting in Go.
\end{remark}

%% ── Block 9: Concrete algorithm ───────────────────────────

\begin{algorithm}[H]
\caption{Drunk Walk on the Euler--Lagrange equation
  \textup{[Model-free locomotion via SVOT--SAC
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:svot-sac});
  cf.\ Algorithm~\ref{alg:drunk-walk} for Go]}}%
\label{alg:svot-locomotion}
\small
\begin{algorithmic}[1]
\Require EL engine $\mathrm{Step}: (x, u) \mapsto x'$
  \Comment{black box, no $\nabla$ (Remark~\ref{rem:el-engine})}
\Require Perception $g_\phi: o \mapsto x \in \R^{42}$;\;
  Go2 limits $(\bar\tau, \bar v, h_{\min}, \phi_{\max})$
  \Comment{Def.~\ref{def:quadruped-state}}
\Require Drunk kernel
  $\rho^*(\cdot \mid o)
    = \mathrm{Uniform}\!\bigl(\cR(o)\bigr)$
  \Comment{Def.~\ref{def:drunk-command}}
\Require $\alpha$ (temperature),
  $\eta$ (learning rate),
  $\gamma$ (discount),
  $\lambda$ (command rate)
\Ensure $\pi_\theta : \R^{42} \times \R^3 \to \R^{12}$,\;
  $g_\phi$,\;
  $Q_\psi : \R^{42} \times \R^{12} \to \R$
\Statex
\State Init $\pi_\theta, g_\phi,
  Q_\psi, \bar Q_{\bar\psi}
  \gets \text{random}$;\;
  $\cB \gets \emptyset$
\For{episode $= 1, 2, \ldots$}
  \State $x_0 \in \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
    \Comment{reset to free space
      (Def.~\ref{def:free-space-locomotion})}
  \State \textsc{Whether}:\;
    $T \sim \mathrm{Exp}(\lambda)$;\quad
    \textsc{Where}:\;
    $v_{\mathrm{cmd}} \sim \rho^*(\cdot \mid x_0)$
    \Comment{drunk picks direction + duration}
  \For{$t = 0, 1, \ldots$}
    \Statex
    \Comment{\textbf{Layer 1}: perception
      ($\nabla_\phi$ flows)}
    \State $o_t \gets \mathrm{sensor}()$;\quad
      $x_t \gets g_\phi(o_t) \in \R^{42}$
      \Comment{Eq.~\eqref{eq:quadruped-obs}}
    \Statex
    \Comment{\textbf{Layer 2}: policy
      ($\nabla_\theta$ flows)}
    \State $u_t \sim
      \pi_\theta(\cdot \mid x_t, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})$;\quad
      $u_t \gets \mathrm{clip}(u_t, {-\bar\tau}, \bar\tau)$
      \Comment{truncated $t_\nu$ (Def.~\ref{def:student-t-policy})}
    \Statex
    \Comment{\textbf{Layer 3}: \textsc{Closure}
      (no gradient---black box)}
    \State $x_{t+1} \gets \mathrm{Step}(x_t, u_t)$
      \Comment{EL engine: Eq.~\eqref{eq:el-contact}}
    \State $c_t \gets
      (\mathbf{1}[z_{\mathrm{foot},i} \leq 0])_{i=1}^4$
      \Comment{contact mode: emergent diagnostic}
    \Statex
    \Comment{Reward: survive $+$ track Drunk Command}
    \State $r_t \gets
        \;W_{\mathrm{alive}}
        -W_v \norm{v_{\mathrm{CoM}} - v_{\mathrm{cmd}}}^2
        -W_h (z{-}h_{\mathrm{ref}})^2
        -W_R \norm{R_{\mathrm{body}}{-}I}_F^2
        -W_u \norm{u_t}^2
        -W_{\Delta u}\norm{u_t{-}u_{t-1}}^2$
    \State $d_t \gets
      \mathbf{1}[x_{t+1} \notin K_{\mathrm{loco}}]$;\;
      \textbf{if} $d_t{=}1$:\;
      $r_t \gets r_t - W_{\mathrm{fall}}$
      \Comment{terminal penalty: violating $K_{\mathrm{loco}}$}
    \State store
      $(o_t, u_t, r_t, o_{t+1}, d_t,
        v_{\mathrm{cmd}}) \to \cB$;\;
      \textbf{if} $d_t{=}1$ \textbf{break}
      \Comment{fell $\Rightarrow$ done}
    \Statex
    \Comment{\textsc{Whether} $\times$ \textsc{Where}:
      resample?}
    \If{$t \cdot \Delta t > T$}
      \State $v_{\mathrm{cmd}}
        \sim \rho^*(\cdot \mid x_t)$;\;
        $T \sim \mathrm{Exp}(\lambda)$
        \Comment{drunk changes direction}
    \EndIf
    \Statex
    \Comment{Learn: SVOT $=$ Yang--Mills $+$ Faddeev--Popov
      (Def.~\ref{def:gauge-curvature})}
    \State Sample $(o, u, r, o', d, v) \sim \cB$;\quad
      $\tilde u' \sim \pi_\theta(\cdot \mid
        g_\phi(o'), v)$
    \State $y \gets r + \gamma(1{-}d)\bigl[
      \bar Q_{\bar\psi}(g_\phi(o'), \tilde u')
      - \alpha \log \pi_\theta(\tilde u' \mid
        g_\phi(o'), v)\bigr]$
      \Comment{TD target}
    \State $\delta \gets Q_\psi(g_\phi(o), u) - y$
      \Comment{\textbf{curvature} $F$: Eq.~\eqref{eq:td-curvature}}
    \State \textbf{Critic:}\;
      $\psi \gets \psi
        - \eta\,\nabla_\psi \tfrac12\,\delta^2$
      \Comment{$\int|F|^2$ (Yang--Mills): Eq.~\eqref{eq:critic-ym}}
    \State \textbf{Actor + Encoder:}\;
      $(\theta,\phi) \gets (\theta,\phi)
        - \eta\,\nabla_{(\theta,\phi)}\bigl[
          \alpha\log\pi_\theta(\tilde u \mid
            g_\phi(o), v)
          - Q_\psi(g_\phi(o), \tilde u)\bigr]$
      \Comment{$\alpha\DKL$ (Faddeev--Popov): Eq.~\eqref{eq:svot-ym}}
    \State $\bar\psi \gets
      (1{-}\rho)\bar\psi + \rho\psi$
      \Comment{Polyak}
    \Statex
    \Comment{Gauge diagnostics
      (Remark~\ref{rem:gauge-alg})}
    \State $\alpha \gets \alpha \cdot
      \mathrm{clip}\!\bigl(
        \mathbb{E}_{\cB}[\delta^2]\,/\,
        \norm{F}^2_{\mathrm{ref}},\;
        c^{-1},\; c\bigr)$
      \Comment{curvature-adaptive $\alpha$
        (asymptotic freedom)}
    \If{$\mathbb{E}_\cB[\delta^2] < \varepsilon_F$
      \textbf{and}\;
      $\norm{\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) - \mathrm{Id}} < \varepsilon_H$}
      \State $v_{\mathrm{cmd}}
        \sim \rho^*(\cdot \mid x_t)$;\;
        $T \sim \mathrm{Exp}(\lambda / 4)$
        \Comment{wrong vacuum $\Rightarrow$
          Drunk burst (instanton)}
    \EndIf
  \EndFor
\EndFor
\end{algorithmic}
\end{algorithm}

\begin{remark}[What the EL engine does and does not provide]
\label{rem:el-engine}
Line~7 of Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}
is the \emph{only} place the EL engine appears.
It computes
\[
  x_{t+1}
  \;=\;
  x_t
  + \Delta t \cdot f(x_t, u_t, \lambda_t),
\]
where $f$ encodes
$M(q)^{-1}\bigl[B\tau + J_c^\top\lambda - C\dot{q} - g\bigr]$
and $\lambda_t$ is resolved internally
(Delassus QP, barrier penalty, or any other contact solver).
The agent never sees $M$, $C$, $g$, $J_c$, or $\lambda$.

\medskip\noindent
Concrete engines that solve Eq.~\eqref{eq:el-contact}:

\smallskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Engine} & \textbf{Contact solver}
  & \textbf{Differentiable?}
  & \textbf{Backend} \\
\midrule
MuJoCo~2.x & Newton + PGS & No  & C \\
MJX        & Barrier + scan & Yes & JAX / XLA \\
Brax       & Spring--damper & Yes & JAX / XLA \\
DFD6 (this paper) & $\kappa$-barrier + Delassus
  & Yes & JAX \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\smallskip\noindent
All four solve the same equation.
Choosing between them is choosing a numerical method,
not changing the mathematics.
The algorithm is identical in all cases---only the
$\mathrm{Step}$ function pointer changes.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Reward structure and replay semantics]
\label{rem:reward-structure}
Three design choices in
Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}
deserve explanation.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(i) Survival bonus and terminal penalty.}\;
Every reward term except $W_{\mathrm{alive}}$
is a penalty ($\leq 0$).
Without $W_{\mathrm{alive}} > 0$,
the return-maximising policy is to terminate
immediately (dying incurs no further penalty).
The survival bonus ensures that
remaining in $K_{\mathrm{loco}}$
is strictly better than leaving it;
the terminal penalty $W_{\mathrm{fall}}$
reinforces the viability boundary as a hard wall.
Together they encode:
\emph{alive is rewarded, falling is punished}.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(ii) Command in the replay buffer.}\;
The tuple stored in $\cB$ includes
$v_{\mathrm{cmd}}$
because SAC is off-policy:
transitions collected under one command
are reused to update the critic and actor
for any command.
Omitting $v_{\mathrm{cmd}}$ would make
the $Q$-function and policy condition on a
stale command---a silent Markov violation.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(iii) Why $T \sim \mathrm{Exp}(\lambda)$.}\;
The exponential distribution is
\emph{memoryless}:
$P(T > t{+}s \mid T > t) = P(T > s)$.
At every time step, the probability of a
command switch is the same regardless of
elapsed time.
This means the remaining time
$\tau_{\mathrm{remain}} = T - t\Delta t$
carries no information beyond what is already
in the current state $x_t$---the
MDP property is preserved without
augmenting the state.
Any other switch-time distribution
(e.g.\ fixed-length episodes)
would require $\tau_{\mathrm{remain}}$ in the state,
breaking the Markov assumption.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Gauge diagnostics in
  Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}]%
\label{rem:gauge-alg}
\color{black!60}%
Lines~13--21 of Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}
are the SVOT loss
$\cL = \tfrac{1}{2}\mathbb{E}[\delta^2]
  + \alpha\,\DKL(\pi_\theta \| \rho^*)$
\eqref{eq:svot-ym},
which is the Yang--Mills action
$\int|F|^2$
plus a Faddeev--Popov gauge-fixing term
(Definition~\ref{def:gauge-curvature}).
Three additions exploit this structure.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(i)\ Curvature-adaptive $\alpha$
  (asymptotic freedom).}\;
Standard SAC tunes $\alpha$ to maintain a target
\emph{entropy}: $H(\pi) \approx H_{\mathrm{target}}$.
Line~20 replaces this with a target
\emph{curvature}:
\[
  \alpha
  \;\gets\;
  \alpha
  \cdot
  \mathrm{clip}\!\Bigl(
    \frac{\mathbb{E}[\delta^2]}
         {\norm{F}^2_{\mathrm{ref}}},\;
    c^{-1},\; c
  \Bigr),
  \qquad c \in (1, 2].
\]
The bound $c = 2 = |\{0,1\}|$ is the cardinality of the
contact alphabet
(Definition~\ref{def:contact-mode}).
A single foot touching or leaving the ground is a
$1$-bit flip in $c \in \{0,1\}^4$;
the contact Jacobian $J_c$ gains or loses one
rank-$1$ term $J_i^\top \lambda_i$,
so the curvature ratio from a single-mode transition
is bounded by~$2$.
A $k$-bit mode change (e.g.\ trot transition: $k = 2$;
jump: $k = 4$) compounds $k$ independent
single-bit changes,
giving a curvature ratio $\leq 2^k$
and an adaptation time of
$\log_c(2^k) = k$ clip steps---the
Hamming distance between the two contact modes.
Flight ($c = 0000$) is not excluded:
it is one of the $16$ modes,
and the $4$-step adaptation handles the
$(1111) \to (0000)$ transition.

When the critic is bad ($\mathbb{E}[\delta^2]$ large),
$\alpha$ increases---more exploration,
because the value function is unreliable.
When the critic is good ($\mathbb{E}[\delta^2]$ small),
$\alpha$ decreases---more exploitation,
because the value function is trustworthy.
This is the RL analogue of \emph{asymptotic freedom}
in QCD:
the coupling constant (exploration) weakens
at low energy (good critic),
strengthens at high energy (bad critic).
Standard entropy targeting is
scale-independent---it ignores the critic's
reliability entirely.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(ii)\ Wrong-vacuum detection
  (instanton trigger).}\;
Lines~21--22 monitor two gauge-invariant
quantities simultaneously:
curvature $\mathbb{E}[\delta^2]$
and holonomy
$\norm{\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) - \mathrm{Id}}$.
Four regimes:

\smallskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}ccl@{}}
\toprule
$\norm{F}^2$ & $\mathrm{Hol}$
  & \textbf{Interpretation} \\
\midrule
high & high
  & Learning, making progress. Continue. \\
low  & high
  & Converged. Good policy. \\
high & $\approx \mathrm{Id}$
  & Early training. Normal. Continue. \\
low  & $\approx \mathrm{Id}$
  & \textbf{Wrong vacuum.}
    Flat but trivial. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\smallskip\noindent
The last row is the failure mode that standard SAC
cannot detect:
the connection is flat ($\delta \approx 0$),
so the critic loss is small,
but the holonomy is trivial
($\mathrm{Hol} \approx \mathrm{Id}$)---the
robot stands still or sways without walking.
The policy has converged to a
\emph{local minimum with zero physical content}.
In gauge-theory language: the \emph{wrong vacuum}.

The fix is an \emph{instanton}---a tunnelling event
from the wrong vacuum to the correct one.
Line~22 implements this as a Drunk burst:
resample $v_{\mathrm{cmd}}$ and extend the
command duration by a factor of~4
(longer random impulse to escape the basin).
Without gauge diagnostics, this failure mode
is invisible: the loss is small,
the policy looks converged,
but the robot is not walking.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(iii)\ Gauge-invariant logging.}\;
The confinement principle
(Remark~\ref{rem:gauge-dictionary})
dictates what to log:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $\mathbb{E}[\delta^2]$ per contact mode
  $c \in \{0,1\}^4$
  (where is the curvature concentrated?);
\item $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma)$ per test gait cycle
  (is the policy producing displacement?);
\item $\mathbb{E}[\delta]$
  (Bianchi check:
   nonzero means actor--critic inconsistency).
\end{itemize}
Do \emph{not} log individual neuron activations---they
are gauge-dependent
(Remark~\ref{rem:gauge-dictionary}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Where the gradient flows]
\label{rem:gradient-flow}
Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion} has three layers.
The gradient flows through the first two and
\emph{stops} at the third:
\[
  \underbrace{o \;\xrightarrow{\;g_\phi\;}\; x}_{\text{%
    perception (NN)}}
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\pi_\theta\;}
  \underbrace{\tau}_{\text{policy (NN)}}
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\mathrm{Step}\;}
  \underbrace{x'}_{\text{physics (black box)}}.
\]
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Perception} $g_\phi$:\;
  raw sensor $\to$ state $x \in \R^{42}$
  (or richer with vision).
  Differentiable.
  Gradient $\nabla_\phi$ flows here.
\item \textbf{Policy} $\pi_\theta$:\;
  state $\to$ torque $\tau \in \R^{12}$.
  Differentiable.
  Gradient $\nabla_\theta$ flows here.
\item \textbf{Physics} $\mathrm{Step}$:\;
  torque $\to$ next state.
  Black box.
  SAC does \emph{not} differentiate through the EL engine.
  Contact modes are \emph{output} of this layer,
  not input to the policy.
\end{enumerate}
``Model-free'' (Remark~\ref{rem:model-free-locomotion})
means: no gradient through layer~3.
The pullback is through the neural network---perception
and policy---not through contact dynamics.
This is why the engine table in
Remark~\ref{rem:el-engine}
lists both differentiable (MJX, Brax, DFD6)
and non-differentiable (MuJoCo~2.x) engines:
\emph{SAC does not care},
because it never asks for $\nabla_{\mathrm{Step}}$.

\medskip\noindent
The sighted case
(Definition~\ref{def:drunk-command}, soft Riccati)
adds a vision encoder to layer~1.
The gradient $\nabla_\phi$ now also flows through
the encoder---but still not through the physics.
The upgrade from blind to sighted is purely
a change in the perception layer.
\end{remark}

%% ── Block 9b: Student-t torque policy ────────────────────

\begin{definition}[Truncated Student-$t$ torque policy]
\label{def:student-t-policy}
The policy
$\pi_\theta(\tau \mid x, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})$
in Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}
is a product of independent truncated
Student-$t$ distributions on
$[-\bar\tau, \bar\tau]^{12}$.
The network $f_\theta$ outputs three heads:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:policy-heads}
  \bigl(\mu,\; \log\sigma,\; \log\nu\bigr)
  \;=\;
  f_\theta(x, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})
  \;\in\;
  \R^{12} \times \R^{12} \times \R,
\end{equation}
giving $25$ scalars:
$12$ means, $12$ log-scales,
and $1$ shared log-degrees-of-freedom.
The density is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:student-t-policy}
  \pi_\theta(\tau \mid x, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})
  \;=\;
  \prod_{i=1}^{12}
  \frac{t_{\nu}(\tau_i;\, \mu_i, \sigma_i)}
       {Z_i(\mu_i, \sigma_i, \nu)},
  \qquad
  Z_i
  \;\coloneqq\;
  F_{\nu}\!\bigl(\bar\tau_i;\, \mu_i, \sigma_i\bigr)
  - F_{\nu}\!\bigl(-\bar\tau_i;\, \mu_i, \sigma_i\bigr),
\end{equation}
where $t_\nu$ is the univariate Student-$t$ density
with $\nu > 0$ degrees of freedom,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:student-t-density}
  t_\nu(z;\, \mu, \sigma)
  \;=\;
  \frac{\Gamma\!\bigl(\tfrac{\nu+1}{2}\bigr)}
       {\Gamma\!\bigl(\tfrac{\nu}{2}\bigr)\,
        \sigma\sqrt{\nu\pi}}
  \biggl(
    1 + \frac{(z - \mu)^2}{\nu\,\sigma^2}
  \biggr)^{\!-(\nu+1)/2}\!,
\end{equation}
$F_\nu$ is the corresponding CDF,
and $\Gamma$ is the gamma function.
The log-probability used in the SAC actor update
(Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}, line~14) is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:log-pi-student}
  \log\pi_\theta(\tau \mid x, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})
  \;=\;
  \sum_{i=1}^{12}
  \biggl[
    \log t_\nu(\tau_i;\, \mu_i, \sigma_i)
    - \log Z_i
  \biggr],
\end{equation}
which is differentiable in $(\mu, \sigma, \nu)$,
hence in $(\theta, \phi)$ through
Eq.~\eqref{eq:policy-heads}.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Why Student-$t$: contact modes force heavy tails]
\label{rem:student-t-forced}
The Student-$t$ family in
Definition~\ref{def:student-t-policy}
is not a design preference---it is forced
by the contact structure.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The argument.}\;
Each contact mode
$c \in \{0,1\}^4$
(Definition~\ref{def:contact-mode})
gives a different local dynamics,
hence a different local Hessian
$\nabla^2_\tau Q(x, \tau; c)$.
The Boltzmann optimal policy
$\pi^*(\tau \mid x)
  \propto \exp\!\bigl(Q(x,\tau)/\alpha\bigr)$
is therefore a \emph{Gaussian mixture}:
near-Gaussian within each contact mode
(locally quadratic $Q$),
with mode weights
$w_c(x) \propto
  \int \exp(Q_c / \alpha)\,d\tau$.
A scale mixture of Gaussians
has Student-$t$ marginals---this is the
classical representation theorem
($\sigma^2 \sim
  \mathrm{Inv}\text{-}\chi^2(\nu, s^2)$,\;
$\tau \mid \sigma \sim \mathcal{N}(\mu, \sigma^2)$\;
$\Rightarrow$\;
$\tau \sim t_\nu(\mu, s)$).
The Student-$t$ is therefore the
natural single-family approximation
to the true multi-modal optimum,
with $\nu$ controlling
the departure from Gaussianity.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Interpretation of $\nu_\theta(x)$.}\;
The learned degrees of freedom
$\nu_\theta(x) = \exp\!\bigl([\log\nu]\bigr)$
tracks the effective number of
active contact modes at state $x$:

\smallskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Regime} & $\boldsymbol{\nu}$
  & \textbf{Policy shape} \\
\midrule
Standing $(c = 1111)$, one mode
  & $\to \infty$ & Gaussian (peaked) \\
Trotting, two alternating modes
  & $\approx 2$--$5$ & Moderate tails \\
Bounding / flight, many transitions
  & $\approx 1$--$2$ & Heavy tails (exploratory) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\smallskip\noindent
A squashed Gaussian
($\nu = \infty$, $\tanh$ output)
is the standard SAC choice
and is correct for quasi-static tasks
where a single contact mode dominates.
For dynamic locomotion with frequent mode
transitions, the finite-$\nu$ Student-$t$
captures the structural multi-modality
in a single differentiable family.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Truncation vs.\ squashing.}\;
Standard SAC uses
$u = \bar\tau \tanh(z)$,
requiring a Jacobian correction
$\log\lvert\det(d\tanh/dz)\rvert$
in the entropy term.
The truncated Student-$t$
(Eq.~\eqref{eq:student-t-policy})
enforces $|\tau_i| \leq \bar\tau_i$
via the normaliser $Z_i$---no
Jacobian correction, exact bounds.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Non-smooth $Q$ is not a problem.}\;
The $Q$-function is locally Lipschitz
but \emph{not} $C^1$ at contact-mode
boundaries
(the Hessian $\nabla^2_\tau Q$
jumps when $J_c$ changes rank).
Classical gradients $\nabla_\tau Q$
are undefined on this zero-measure set,
so direct policy optimisation would require
Clarke subdifferentials
$\partial_C Q$.
The Student-$t$ policy resolves this
\emph{automatically}:
the expected $Q$ under the policy,
\[
  \bar Q(\theta)
  \;\coloneqq\;
  \mathbb{E}_{\pi_\theta}\!\bigl[Q(x, \tau)\bigr]
  \;=\;
  \int_{[-\bar\tau,\bar\tau]^{12}}
    \!\!Q(x, \tau)\,
    \pi_\theta(\tau \mid x, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})\,
    d\tau,
\]
is smooth in $(\theta, \phi)$
because $\pi_\theta$ has full support
on $[-\bar\tau, \bar\tau]^{12}$
and is $C^\infty$ in its parameters.
Integrating a Lipschitz function
against a smooth kernel
with full support
produces a smooth function---the
policy acts as a \emph{mollifier}.
The SAC policy gradient
$\nabla_\theta \bar Q
  = \mathbb{E}_\pi[Q\,\nabla_\theta\log\pi_\theta]$
(score function identity)
is therefore well-defined
without any appeal to subdifferential calculus.
Non-smoothness of $Q$
at mode boundaries is absorbed by the
stochastic integration,
exactly as the Drunk Walk absorbs
strategic discontinuities in Go
(Remark~\ref{rem:model-free-locomotion}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Constructive instanton]
\label{rem:constructive-instanton}
The Drunk burst
(Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}, lines~23--25)
is a \emph{constructive instanton}:
the tunnelling from wrong vacuum to correct vacuum
is specified by three computable ingredients,
not by solving a variational problem.
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Trigger.}\;
  Two gauge-invariant inequalities:
  $\mathbb{E}_\cB[\delta^2] < \varepsilon_F$
  and
  $\norm{\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) - \mathrm{Id}} < \varepsilon_H$
  (Remark~\ref{rem:gauge-alg}\,(ii)).
  Standard SAC cannot distinguish
  wrong vacuum from convergence.
\item \textbf{Mechanism.}\;
  Resample $v_{\mathrm{cmd}} \sim \rho^*$
  with extended duration
  $T \sim \mathrm{Exp}(\lambda/4)$.
  The Student-$t$ policy
  (Definition~\ref{def:student-t-policy})
  provides polynomial tunnelling probability
  $P(\text{escape at distance } d)
    \propto d^{-\nu}$,
  versus $\exp(-d^2/2\sigma^2)$ for Gaussian.
  The heavy tail is forced by
  contact structure
  (Remark~\ref{rem:student-t-forced}),
  not chosen.
\item \textbf{Verification.}\;
  After the burst, monitor holonomy.
  $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) \neq \mathrm{Id}$:
  non-trivial vacuum (walking).
  $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) \approx \mathrm{Id}$:
  burst failed---fire again.
\end{enumerate}
The instanton has finite action
(bounded reward cost during the burst),
is localised in time
($T$ is exponentially distributed),
and interpolates between
topologically distinct vacua
(trivial~$\to$ non-trivial holonomy).
In the language of constructive mathematics:
the Drunk burst is a \emph{witness}
for the tunnelling,
not an existence proof.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Structural knowledge and maneuverability]
\label{rem:structural-knowledge}
The Drunk kernel $\rho^*$
(Definition~\ref{def:student-t-policy})
carries two pieces of \emph{a priori} knowledge
that no purely data-driven policy possesses:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item the \textbf{contact alphabet}
  $\cC = \{0,1\}^4$
  (Definition~\ref{def:contact-mode}),
\item the \textbf{viability constraint}
  $K_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  (Definition~\ref{def:viability-locomotion}).
\end{enumerate}
Together these define a finite reachability problem:
$16$ contact modes connected by transitions
that the Euler--Lagrange dynamics permits.
\emph{Maneuverability} is reachability on this graph.

A diffusion policy
$\pi_\theta\colon s \mapsto p(a \mid s)$,
trained on a demonstration set~$D$,
learns the empirical distribution over actions.
It has no explicit representation of~$\cC$
and cannot certify viability:
high likelihood under~$D$ does not imply
$x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$.
When the robot encounters a state
outside $D$'s support---novel terrain,
external perturbation, actuator degradation---the
policy has no mechanism to verify
whether the contact mode it produces is viable.

The Drunk does not learn gaits.
The Student-$t$ tails
visit all $16$ modes with positive probability;
the viability kernel is a hard constraint,
not a soft reward signal.
This is the difference between
\emph{structural knowledge}
(the robot stands on its feet---known \emph{a priori}
from morphology)
and \emph{statistical knowledge}
(the robot usually stands---inferred
from finite data).
A cat dropped upside-down rights itself
in ${\sim}\,0.3$\,s.
This is not learned; it is a hardwired reflex.
The vestibular system knows which way is down;
the motor cortex knows which limbs make contact.
The cat has the contact alphabet
and the viability constraint.
A robot trained by behavioural cloning
on ``how I usually land''
has a statistical summary of landings,
not the constraint that forces them.

The maneuverability gap is exponential
in the number of feet.
The contact lattice has $2^n$ modes.
A finite demonstration set covers
at most $|D|$ state-mode pairs.
Full viability coverage requires
demonstrations from all $2^n$ modes
under all reachable states---exponential in~$n$.
The Drunk covers all modes by construction
(Student-$t$ support $= \R^{12}$;
Remark~\ref{rem:student-t-forced}).
\end{remark}

%% ── Block 10: Free space, holonomy, theorem ───────────────

% Override definition background: light blue for the free-space pair
\tcolorboxenvironment{definition}{
  enhanced, breakable, sharp corners,
  colback=blue!8!white, colframe=blue!8!white,
  borderline west={2pt}{0pt}{specOrange},
  boxsep=0pt, left=5pt, right=3pt, top=2pt, bottom=2pt,
}

\begin{definition}[Free space for locomotion --- geometric structure]
\label{def:free-space-locomotion}
The \emph{free space} is not a single object
but a four-level structure.
Each level is forced by the one below it.
This definition gives Level~0 and Level~1
(the geometry);
Definition~\ref{def:free-space-analytic} gives
Level~2 and Level~3 (the analysis).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Level~0: Configuration space.}\;
$\mathcal{Q} = \mathrm{SE}(3) \times \mathcal{Q}_{\mathrm{shape}}$,
where $\mathcal{Q}_{\mathrm{shape}} \subset \R^{12}$
is the joint-angle space (bounded by joint limits).
Write $q = (g, \theta)$ with
$g \in \mathrm{SE}(3)$ (body pose)
and $\theta \in \mathcal{Q}_{\mathrm{shape}}$ (joint angles).
The state space is the tangent bundle
$T\mathcal{Q}$, with $\dim T\mathcal{Q} = 36$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Level~1: Manifold $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$.}\;
The free space is the equilibrium submanifold
of the all-contact mode:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:free-space}
  \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}
  \;=\;
  \bigl\{\,
    x = (g,\, \theta,\, 0,\, 0)
    \;\in\; T\mathcal{Q}
    \;:\;
    c = (1,1,1,1),\;\;
    g(q) = B\tau_{\mathrm{static}}
      + J_c(q)^{\!\top}\lambda_{\mathrm{static}},\;\;
    x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}
  \,\bigr\},
\end{equation}
where $\tau_{\mathrm{static}}, \lambda_{\mathrm{static}}$
solve the static equilibrium
(zero velocity, zero acceleration,
all four feet on the ground).

\emph{Type:}\;
$\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ is a \textbf{compact smooth
manifold with boundary},
not a Hilbert space,
not an infinite-dimensional object.
It is finite-dimensional:
$\dim \cF_{\mathrm{loco}} \leq \dim \mathcal{Q} = 18$.

\emph{Symmetry:}\;
$\mathrm{SE}(2)$ acts freely on $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
(translate and rotate the robot horizontally
without changing the shape).
Given $\theta$, the foot positions fix $g$
up to $(x, y, \psi)$.
Thus
\begin{equation}\label{eq:free-space-decomp}
  \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}
  \;\cong\;
  \mathrm{SE}(2) \times \cF_{\mathrm{shape}},
\end{equation}
where
$\cF_{\mathrm{shape}} \subset \mathcal{Q}_{\mathrm{shape}}$
is the set of joint angles admitting static balance
(CoM over the support polygon,
torques within limits).

\emph{Boundary:}\;
$\partial \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ is where
constraint inequalities become active---joint limits,
torque-limit saturation,
or CoM on the edge of the support polygon.
The interior is smooth.
The boundary is piecewise smooth
(corners where two constraints meet).
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Free space for locomotion --- analytic structure]
\label{def:free-space-analytic}
Continuing the four-level structure
of Definition~\ref{def:free-space-locomotion}.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Level~2: Viable control bundle.}\;
At each state $x \in \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$,
the set of controls that keep the robot viable
is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:viable-controls}
  U(x)
  \;=\;
  \bigl\{\,
    u \in \R^{12}
    \;:\;
