    \mathrm{Step}(x, u) \in \mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})
  \,\bigr\}
  \;\subset\; \R^{12}.
\end{equation}
The \emph{viable control bundle} is
\[
  \cE
  \;=\;
  \bigl\{\,
    (x, u) \;:\;
    x \in \cF_{\mathrm{loco}},\;
    u \in U(x)
  \,\bigr\}
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\mathrm{pr}_1\;}\;
  \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}.
\]
A policy $\pi : \cF_{\mathrm{loco}} \to \R^{12}$
is a \emph{section} of this bundle:
$\pi(x) \in U(x)$ for all $x$.
Viable policies are exactly the sections of $\cE$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Level~3: Policy Hilbert space.}\;
The Drunk Command kernel
(Definition~\ref{def:drunk-command})
induces a reference measure $\rho^*$
on $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$.
The policy space is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:policy-hilbert}
  \cH_{\mathrm{loco}}
  \;=\;
  L^2\!\bigl(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}},\, \rho^*;\;
    \R^{12}\bigr),
  \qquad
  \ip{\pi}{\pi'}
  \;=\;
  \int_{\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}}
    \pi(x)^\top \pi'(x)
  \;\, d\rho^*(x).
\end{equation}
\emph{Type:}\;
$\cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$ \textbf{is} a
(separable, infinite-dimensional) Hilbert space.
The SVOT loss~\eqref{eq:svot-loss}
is a functional $\cL : \cH_{\mathrm{loco}} \to \R$,
and SAC is a stochastic gradient flow in
$\cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$.
Neural network parametrisation
$\pi_\theta \in \cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$
restricts this flow to a finite-dimensional
submanifold $\Theta \hookrightarrow \cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}clll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Level} & \textbf{Object}
  & \textbf{Type}
  & \textbf{Dim} \\
\midrule
0 & $T\mathcal{Q}$ (state space)
  & Smooth manifold
  & 36 \\
1 & $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ (free space)
  & Compact manifold with boundary
  & $\leq 18$ \\
2 & $\cE$ (viable control bundle)
  & Fiber bundle over $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  & $\leq 30$ \\
3 & $\cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$ (policy space)
  & Separable Hilbert space
  & $\infty$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{What ``free'' means at each level.}\;
Level~1 is the free core $\cF$ of the Freedom Theorem:
the minimal set from which
$\mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})
  = \mathrm{Push}(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})$.
Level~2 is the set of viable actions:
$U(x) \neq \emptyset$
for all $x \in \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
(that is what ``free'' means---freedom to act).
Level~3 is where learning happens:
the SVOT gradient flow in $\cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$
finds the optimal section of $\cE$.

Standing is to locomotion what territory is to Go.
The free space is not the standing pose---it is
the four-level structure that makes standing
\emph{generative}:
every viable behaviour is reachable from it.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Well-posedness.}\;
The four levels are well-posed:
$\cF_{\mathrm{loco}} \neq \emptyset$
(the standing pose is a witness),
$\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ is compact
(zero velocity + joint limits + closed constraints),
its interior is a smooth manifold
(implicit function theorem),
and
$\cH_{\mathrm{loco}}
  = L^2(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}, \rho^*;\, \R^{12})$
is a separable Hilbert space
(compact base, finite Borel measure).
See Proposition~\ref{prop:free-space-wp} for proof.
\end{definition}

% Restore default definition background
\tcolorboxenvironment{definition}{
  enhanced, breakable, sharp corners,
  colback=white, colframe=white,
  borderline west={2pt}{0pt}{specOrange},
  boxsep=0pt, left=5pt, right=3pt, top=2pt, bottom=2pt,
}

\begin{proposition}[Well-posedness of the free space]
\label{prop:free-space-wp}
Under the Go2 parameters
(Definition~\ref{def:quadruped-state}):
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item \emph{Non-emptiness.}\;
  $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}} \neq \emptyset$.
  The default standing state
  ($\theta_0 = (0.0,\, 0.8,\, {-}1.5)^{\otimes 4}$,
  $h = 0.312\,\mathrm{m}$)
  satisfies static equilibrium with all four feet
  on the ground.
\item \emph{Compactness.}\;
  $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ is compact:
  zero velocity forces boundedness in $T\mathcal{Q}$;
  joint limits and the viability constraint
  $K_{\mathrm{loco}}$ are closed.
\item \emph{Regularity.}\;
  The interior of $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  is a smooth manifold
  ($g(q)$ and $J_c(q)$ are smooth;
  implicit function theorem applies).
  The boundary $\partial \cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  is piecewise smooth
  (smooth on faces where one inequality
  is active, corners where two meet).
\item \emph{Separability.}\;
  $\cH_{\mathrm{loco}}
  = L^2(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}, \rho^*;\, \R^{12})$
  is a separable Hilbert space.
  $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ compact
  and $\rho^*$ induced by Drunk Command
  (Uniform on a bounded set)
  imply $\rho^*$ is a finite Borel measure;
  $L^2$ over a finite measure on a compact space
  is always separable.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
(i)~Direct verification with Go2 parameters
(Definition~\ref{def:quadruped-state}).
(ii)~$\cF_{\mathrm{loco}} \subset
  \{(q,0) \in T\mathcal{Q}\}$
  with $q$ in the joint-limit polytope;
  continuous constraint functions
  on a compact domain have closed preimage.
(iii)~At interior points all constraint inequalities
  are strict;
  the constraint map
  $q \mapsto g(q) - B\tau - J_c(q)^\top\lambda$
  has full-rank Jacobian
  when $J_c^{(g)}$ is invertible
  (four non-coplanar feet).
(iv)~Standard: $L^2$ over a compact space
  with a finite Borel measure is separable
  (countable dense set from polynomials
  on a compact manifold).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Riesz structure of the policy space]
\label{prop:riesz-policy}
Let $\cH = \cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:free-space-wp}\textup{(iv)})
and let
$Q \in L^\infty\!\bigl(
  \cF_{\mathrm{loco}} \times
  [-\bar\tau,\bar\tau]^{12}\bigr)$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item \emph{Riesz representative.}\;
  The evaluation functional
  \[
    \ell_Q(\pi)
    \;=\;
    \int_{\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}}
    \int_{[-\bar\tau,\bar\tau]^{12}}
    \!\!\pi(\tau \mid x)\,Q(x,\tau)\,
    \rho^*(dx)\,d\tau
  \]
  is a continuous linear functional on $\cH$.
  By the Riesz representation theorem,
  there exists a unique $h_Q \in \cH$
  such that
  $\ell_Q(\pi) = \langle \pi, h_Q \rangle_\cH$
  for all $\pi \in \cH$.
  On compact $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  with finite $\rho^*$,
  $L^\infty \hookrightarrow L^2$,
  so $h_Q = Q$ (natural embedding):
  the $Q$-function IS
  the Riesz representative of the critic.

\item \emph{Existence and uniqueness.}\;
  The SVOT loss
  \[
    \cL(\pi)
    \;=\;
    -\ell_Q(\pi)
    + \alpha\,\DKL(\pi \| \rho^*)
  \]
  is strictly convex on the closed convex set
  $\Delta(\cH)
    = \{\pi \in \cH :
    \pi \geq 0,\;
    \textstyle\int \pi\,d\tau = 1\}$
  (linearity of $\ell_Q$
  $+$ strict convexity of $\DKL$).
  The minimiser exists
  (weak compactness of $\Delta(\cH)$)
  and is unique.

\item \emph{Closed form.}\;
  The unique minimiser is the
  soft-Boltzmann policy:
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:boltzmann-optimal}
    \pi^*(\tau \mid x, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})
    \;=\;
    \frac{\rho^*(\tau \mid x)\,
      \exp\!\bigl(Q(x,\tau)/\alpha\bigr)}
         {Z(x)},
    \qquad
    Z(x)
    = \!\int_{[-\bar\tau,\bar\tau]^{12}}
      \!\!\rho^*\exp(Q/\alpha)\,d\tau.
  \end{equation}
  This is the exponential tilt of
  the Drunk Command $\rho^*$
  by the Riesz representative $h_Q = Q$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
(i)~Cauchy--Schwarz:
$|\ell_Q(\pi)|
  \leq \|Q\|_{L^\infty}\,\|\pi\|_\cH < \infty$.
Continuity and linearity invoke Riesz.
The embedding $h_Q = Q$ follows from
$\|Q\|_\cH \leq \|Q\|_{L^\infty}\,\rho^*(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})^{1/2} < \infty$
(compact base, finite measure).
(ii)~$\DKL$ is strictly convex
and lower semicontinuous on $\Delta(\cH)$;
$-\ell_Q$ is linear (hence convex);
the sum is strictly convex.
Coercivity: $\DKL(\pi \| \rho^*) \to \infty$
as $\|\pi\|_\cH \to \infty$.
(iii)~First variation
$\delta\cL/\delta\pi
  = -Q + \alpha(\log\pi - \log\rho^*) + \lambda = 0$
($\lambda$ the Lagrange multiplier for $\int\pi = 1$);
solving gives~\eqref{eq:boltzmann-optimal}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Free space as Embed--Prove--Pullback]
\label{rem:free-space-epp}
The four levels of the free space
(Definitions~\ref{def:free-space-locomotion}--\ref{def:free-space-analytic})
reproduce the Mirror Reflection pipeline
(Algorithm~\ref{alg:reflect}):

\smallskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Level} & \textbf{Free space}
  & \textbf{Mirror Reflection} \\
\midrule
0 & Configuration $\mathcal{Q}$
  & Raw input \\
1 & Viability $K_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  & \textbf{Embed} (formalise constraints) \\
2 & Free core $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  & \textbf{Prove} (verify viability) \\
3 & Policy Hilbert space $\cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  & \textbf{Pullback} (extract usable policy) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{Embed.}\;
The physical configuration
$q \in \mathcal{Q}$
is embedded into observation space
$x = g_\phi(o) \in \R^{42}$,
and the constraint
$x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$
is formalised
(Definition~\ref{def:viability-locomotion}).
\textbf{Prove.}\;
The viability kernel
$\mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})$
is computed---the free core
$\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ is the standing equilibrium
from which all viable behaviours are reachable
(Level~2).
\textbf{Pullback.}\;
The optimal policy
$\pi^* \in \cH_{\mathrm{loco}}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:riesz-policy})
is pulled back to a concrete torque command
$\tau = \pi^*(x, v_{\mathrm{cmd}})$.

\medskip\noindent
The Riesz representative
$h_Q = Q$
is the \emph{proof object}:
it certifies that $\pi^*$ is optimal.
The Student-$t$ parametrisation
(Definition~\ref{def:student-t-policy})
is the finite-dimensional
approximation of the pullback,
with degrees of freedom
$\nu_\theta(x)$
tracking the structural complexity
(contact-mode count) of the proof.
This is not metaphor---it is the
same functor applied to a different category
(Remark~\ref{rem:mopl-locomotion-iso}).
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Mechanical connection and holonomy]
\label{def:holonomy-locomotion}
Fix a contact mode $c \in \{0,1\}^4$
with $|c| \geq 1$ (at least one foot on the ground).
The contact constraint
$J_c(q)\,\dot{q} = 0$
(no slip at active feet)
defines a \emph{mechanical connection}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mech-connection}
  A_c \;:\; T_\theta \mathcal{Q}_{\mathrm{shape}}
  \;\longrightarrow\;
  \mathfrak{se}(3),
  \qquad
  A_c(\dot\theta)
  \;=\;
  -\bigl(J_c^{(g)}\bigr)^{-1}
   J_c^{(\theta)}\,\dot\theta,
\end{equation}
where $J_c^{(g)}$ and $J_c^{(\theta)}$ are the
body-pose and joint-angle blocks of $J_c$.
The connection $A_c$ maps a joint velocity
to the body twist it induces
via the contact constraint:
move the joints, the feet are pinned,
so the body must move.

\medskip\noindent
A \emph{gait cycle} is a closed loop
$\gamma : [0, T] \to \mathcal{Q}_{\mathrm{shape}}$,
$\gamma(0) = \gamma(T)$,
together with a piecewise-constant
contact mode function
$c : [0, T] \to \{0,1\}^4$
(the mode switches at foot-strike and foot-lift events).
The \emph{holonomy} of $\gamma$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:holonomy}
  \mathrm{Hol}(\gamma)
  \;=\;
  \overleftarrow{\prod}_{i}
  \exp\!\Bigl(
    \int_{t_i}^{t_{i+1}}
    A_{c_i}\!\bigl(\dot\gamma(t)\bigr)\,dt
  \Bigr)
  \;\in\; \mathrm{SE}(3),
\end{equation}
where the ordered product is over the segments
$[t_i, t_{i+1}]$ on which the contact mode
is constant at $c_i$.
$\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma)$ is the net body displacement
after one gait cycle:
the joints return to where they started,
the robot has moved.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Holonomy differentiability of the free space]
\label{thm:holonomy-diff}
Let $\Gamma$ be a gait pattern
(a fixed cyclic sequence of contact modes
$c_1, \ldots, c_n, c_1$
with prescribed topology:
which feet strike and lift in which order).
Let $\gamma_s : [0, T] \to \mathcal{Q}_{\mathrm{shape}}$,
$s \in S$,
be a smooth family of gait cycles
realising $\Gamma$,
parametrised by gait parameters
$s = (\text{amplitude, frequency, phase offsets})
\in S \subset \R^p$.
Assume all contact transitions are \emph{transversal}:
at each switching time $t_i(s)$,
the foot height crosses zero
with nonzero velocity.
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Smooth free space.}\;
  $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ is a compact smooth
  submanifold of $K_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  (with boundary where the static balance
  or torque-limit constraints are active).
\item \textbf{Smooth holonomy.}\;
  The holonomy map
  $\mathrm{Hol} : S \to \mathrm{SE}(3)$,\;
  $s \mapsto \mathrm{Hol}(\gamma_s)$,
  is $C^\infty$ on $S$.
\item \textbf{Orbit decomposition.}\;
  $\mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})
    = \bigcup_{\Gamma}\,
      \mathrm{Orbit}_\Gamma(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})$,
  where the union is over all viable gait patterns,
  and
  $\mathrm{Orbit}_\Gamma(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})$
  is the set of states visited by trajectories
  starting in $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
  and executing gait pattern $\Gamma$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
\emph{Part~1.}\;
In the all-contact mode $c = (1,1,1,1)$,
the EL equation~\eqref{eq:el-contact}
is a smooth ODE
(no switching---all feet are on the ground).
The equilibrium conditions
($\dot{q} = 0$, $\ddot{q} = 0$,
$g(q) = B\tau + J_c^\top\lambda$,
$x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$)
define $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$
as a sublevel set of smooth functions.
The implicit function theorem gives the manifold structure;
the constraint boundaries (joint limits, torque limits)
give the boundary.

\medskip\noindent
\emph{Part~2.}\;
Within each contact mode $c_i$,
the flow $\Phi_{c_i}^t$ of the smooth ODE
is $C^\infty$ in $(t, x)$.
At each switching time $t_i(s)$,
transversality means the foot height
$h_{\mathrm{foot}}(x)$ crosses zero
with $\dot{h}_{\mathrm{foot}} \neq 0$.
By the implicit function theorem,
$t_i(s)$ is a $C^\infty$ function of $s$.
The holonomy~\eqref{eq:holonomy}
is a composition
$\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma_s)
  = \Phi_{c_n}^{\Delta t_n(s)}
    \circ \cdots \circ
    \Phi_{c_1}^{\Delta t_1(s)}$,
which is $C^\infty$ as a composition
of smooth maps with smooth time arguments.

\medskip\noindent
\emph{Part~3.}\;
By definition of the viability kernel,
every $x \in \mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})$
admits a control keeping $x(t) \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$
forever.
Any such trajectory either stays in
$\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}$ (standing)
or executes some gait pattern $\Gamma$
(periodic or transient).
The trajectory visits states in
$\mathrm{Orbit}_\Gamma(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})$
by construction.
The reverse inclusion
$\mathrm{Orbit}_\Gamma(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})
  \subseteq \mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})$
holds because any state on a viable gait orbit
can continue that gait
(or transition to standing).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Where smoothness fails.}\;
Transversality fails at \emph{grazing}:
a foot barely touches the ground and lifts
without penetrating
($\dot{h}_{\mathrm{foot}} = 0$
at the switching surface).
At grazing, $t_i(s)$ is not smooth in $s$,
and the holonomy map has a cusp.
Grazing is codimension~1 in $S$:
it occurs on a measure-zero set of gait parameters.
Generic gaits are transversal.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Locomotion as parallel transport]
\label{rem:locomotion-parallel-transport}
Theorem~\ref{thm:holonomy-diff} makes precise
why a trained policy $\pi_\theta$ is a gauge field
(Remark~\ref{rem:model-free-locomotion}).
The policy maps state to torque;
the torque, through the contact constraint,
produces body displacement---this is
the mechanical connection $A_c$~\eqref{eq:mech-connection}.
A gait cycle is a closed loop in joint space.
The holonomy $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) \in \mathrm{SE}(3)$
is the net displacement.
The robot walks \emph{because} the connection
has nontrivial holonomy:
$\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) \neq \mathrm{Id}$.

\medskip\noindent
The mass gap $m_* > 0$ of the Yang--Mills theory
corresponds here to
$\norm{\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) - \mathrm{Id}} > 0$:
the gait actually moves the robot.
A zero-holonomy gait
(symmetric leg motion, net displacement zero)
is the trivial connection---massless,
no locomotion.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Universal not-lost condition:
  the free core is the self-reproducing element]%
\label{rem:universal-not-lost}
\color{black!60}%
The not-lose constraint appears in every instantiation
of this paper.
In each case it takes the same abstract form:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:universal-not-lost}
  x \in \mathrm{Viab}(K)
  \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
  \cF \neq \emptyset
  \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
  \exists\;\text{admissible path}\;
  x(t) \in K \;\;\forall\, t \geq 0.
\end{equation}
The left equivalence is
Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}\,(i):
the viability kernel contains the free core.
The right equivalence is Aubin's definition of
viability (1991): a state is viable if and only if
there exists at least one control keeping
the trajectory inside the constraint set forever.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Three instantiations.}\;
The following table lists what ``not-lose,''
``free core,'' and ``self-reproducing element'' mean
in each domain.
The structural content is identical;
only the substrate changes.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{3.2cm}p{3.8cm}p{3.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Go (MOPL)}
& \textbf{Quadruped}
& \textbf{Colony / swarm} \\
\midrule
Constraint $K$
  & $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$\newline (not lose the game)
  & $x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$\newline (not fall)
  & Queen alive $\wedge$\newline
    $|\text{workers}| \geq n_{\min}$ \\[6pt]
Free core $\cF$
  & Two living eyes\newline
    (unconditionally alive group)
  & Standing configuration\newline
    $\cF_{\mathrm{loco}}
     \cong \mathrm{SE}(2) \times
     \cF_{\mathrm{shape}}$
  & Queen $+$ minimal\newline
    reproductive cluster \\[6pt]
Self-reproducing
  & Two eyes create\newline
    territory that creates\newline
    more eyes
  & Standing $\to$ gait $\to$\newline
    locomotion $\to$\newline
    new standing
  & Queen $\to$ eggs $\to$\newline
    workers $\to$ forage\newline
    $\to$ queen survives \\[6pt]
$\mathrm{Viab}(K)$
  & $\mathrm{Push}(\cF)$:\newline
    all board positions\newline
    reachable from two eyes
  & $\bigcup_\Gamma
    \mathrm{Orbit}_\Gamma(\cF_{\mathrm{loco}})$:\newline
    all viable gait orbits
  & All colony states from\newline
    which the queen can\newline
    be sustained \\[6pt]
Path to $\infty$
  & $\exists$ framework sequence\newline
    keeping $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$\newline
    at every scale
  & $\exists$ torque sequence\newline
    keeping $x(t) \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$\newline
    $\forall\, t \geq 0$
  & $\exists$ task allocation\newline
    keeping queen alive\newline
    and $|\text{workers}| \geq n_{\min}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The queen bee theorem.}\;
In a eusocial colony, the queen is the free core.
She is the only element whose removal makes
$\cF = \emptyset$---without her,
no new workers are produced,
the worker count decays monotonically,
and eventually $|\text{workers}| < n_{\min}$:
the colony exits the constraint set $K$ in finite time.
The queen survives if and only if
$\cF \neq \emptyset$
if and only if
there exists a reachable path to $t \to \infty$.
This is not a metaphor.
It is the Freedom Theorem
(Remark~\ref{rem:freedom-pool})
applied to a third substrate:
dissipative flow
(worker attrition)
on a compact space
(bounded colony size)
converges to a finite free core
(queen $+$ minimum reproductive cluster).

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Why ``not-lost'' and not ``winning.''}\;
The viability constraint~\eqref{eq:universal-not-lost}
asks for \emph{existence} of a surviving path,
not for optimality.
Winning is a stronger condition---it requires
the path to also accumulate reward
(territory, distance, honey).
But winning is impossible without first not-losing:
$\cF = \emptyset$ implies no admissible path exists
at all, let alone an optimal one.
The free core is the necessary condition.
Everything else---strategy, gait, foraging
pattern---is optimisation \emph{within}
$\mathrm{Viab}(K)$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The neural network is a gauge transformation]%
\label{rem:nn-gauge}
\color{black!60}%
Remark~\ref{rem:locomotion-parallel-transport} identifies
the trained policy $\pi_{\theta^*}$ as a gauge field
(connection on the state--action bundle).
This section makes the full gauge structure explicit.
There are three objects, not one.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(i)\ Gauge field (connection).}\;
A fixed $\theta$ defines a map
$\pi_\theta \colon \cX \to \cA$,
state to action.
The dynamics
$x_t \xrightarrow{\pi_\theta(x_t)} x_{t+1}$
is \emph{parallel transport} along the connection $\pi_\theta$.
A gait cycle $\gamma$ in joint space produces
holonomy $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) \in \mathrm{SE}(3)$.
The holonomy is the gauge-invariant content:
it depends on the loop $\gamma$,
not on the parametrisation $\theta$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(ii)\ Gauge group.}\;
Define the equivalence
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gauge-equiv}
  \theta \sim \theta'
  \quad\stackrel{\mathrm{def}}{\Longleftrightarrow}\quad
  \mathrm{Viab}(K;\, \pi_\theta)
  \;=\;
  \mathrm{Viab}(K;\, \pi_{\theta'}).
\end{equation}
Two parametrisations are \emph{gauge-equivalent}
if they produce the same viability kernel---the
same free core, the same surviving paths,
the same holonomies.
The gauge group is
$\cG = \{\,\theta \to \theta' : \theta \sim \theta'\,\}$.
This is the symmetry group of the loss landscape:
the flat directions of $\cL(\theta)$ are exactly
the gauge orbits $[\theta] \in \Theta / \cG$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{(iii)\ Gauge fixing $=$ training.}\;
SGD starts from random $\theta_0$ and converges to
$\theta^*$, a single representative of its
gauge orbit $[\theta^*]$.
This is gauge fixing.
In the path-integral language:
\[
  \underbrace{%
    \int_\Theta e^{-\cL(\theta)/\alpha}\,d\theta
  }_{\text{path integral (all $\theta$)}}
  \;\;\xrightarrow{\;\alpha \to 0\;}\;\;
  \underbrace{%
    e^{-\cL(\theta^*)/\alpha}
  }_{\text{saddle point (one $\theta^*$)}}
  \;=\;
  \text{classical limit.}
\]
The temperature $\alpha$ is the SAC entropy coefficient.
At $\alpha \to 0$ (greedy), the integral localises
to a single gauge-fixed classical solution.
At finite $\alpha$ (exploratory), the integral
averages over the gauge orbit---soft policy
optimisation \emph{is} quantum gauge theory
at finite temperature.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Why overparametrisation helps.}\;
A network with $d$ parameters has parameter space
$\Theta \subseteq \R^d$.
The physical content is the quotient
$\Theta / \cG$, whose dimension is
$d - \dim(\cG)$.
A larger network increases $d$, hence increases
$\dim(\cG)$---more flat directions, more gauge
redundancy, more paths from $\theta_0$ to the
correct gauge orbit.
Overparametrisation does not add physical degrees
of freedom.
It enlarges the gauge group, making
gauge fixing (training) easier.
This is the same mechanism by which
a larger lattice in Yang--Mills
makes the path integral better-conditioned:
more redundancy, better sampling, same physics.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The three instantiations.}\;

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{3.0cm}p{3.6cm}p{3.6cm}@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Go (MOPL)}
& \textbf{Quadruped}
& \textbf{Colony} \\
\midrule
Bundle
  & Board $\to$ legal moves
  & $\cX \to \R^{12}$ (torques)
  & Colony state $\to$\newline task allocations \\[4pt]
Section (NN)
  & Pool $\to$ framework\newline $\to$ move
  & Encoder $\to$ policy\newline $\to$ $\tau$
  & Scheduler $\to$\newline task assignment \\[4pt]
Gauge transf
  & Different pool weights,\newline same territory
  & Different $\theta$,\newline same $\mathrm{Viab}(K_{\mathrm{loco}})$
  & Different schedules,\newline same queen survival \\[4pt]
Gauge fixing
  & Pool convergence\newline (Queen's game)
  & SAC convergence\newline (Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion})
  & Colony stabilisation \\[4pt]
Holonomy
  & Territory gained\newline per game cycle
  & $\mathrm{SE}(3)$ displacement\newline per gait cycle
  & Honey stored\newline per foraging round \\[4pt]
Invariant ($\cF$)
  & Two eyes
  & Standing
  & Queen alive \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Summary.}\;
The neural network is not ``like'' a gauge transformation.
It \emph{is} one:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item the trained network $\pi_{\theta^*}$
  is a \textbf{gauge-fixed connection}
  (parallel transport from state to action);
\item the reparametrisation
  $\theta \to \theta'$ preserving
  $\mathrm{Viab}(K)$
  is a \textbf{gauge transformation};
\item training (SGD/SAC) is \textbf{gauge fixing}
  (picking one $\theta^*$ per orbit);
\item the free core $\cF$ is the
  \textbf{gauge invariant}
  (what survives all reparametrisations);
\item $m_* > 0$ is \textbf{nontrivial holonomy}
  (the network actually does something:
  moves the robot, wins the game,
  keeps the queen alive).
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Gauge-theoretic curvature of a policy]%
\label{def:gauge-curvature}
\color{black!60}%
Remark~\ref{rem:nn-gauge} identifies the policy
$\pi_\theta$ as a \emph{connection}
(gauge field)
and $\theta \sim \theta'$ as a \emph{gauge
transformation}.
These are the \emph{kinematics} of the gauge theory.
The \emph{dynamics} require the curvature.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Curvature $=$ temporal-difference error.}\;
Given a policy $\pi_\theta$ with critic $Q_\psi$,
the \emph{curvature} is the TD error
\begin{equation}\label{eq:td-curvature}
  \delta_t
  \;=\;
  r_t
  + \gamma\,Q_\psi(x_{t+1},\, \pi_\theta(x_{t+1}))
  - Q_\psi(x_t,\, u_t).
\end{equation}
This measures the failure of the value function
to be \emph{path-independent}:
if $Q$ satisfies the Bellman equation exactly,
then $\delta_t = 0$ for every transition.
A zero TD error everywhere means the connection
is \emph{flat}---parallel transport around any
closed loop returns the same value.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The SVOT loss is the Yang--Mills action.}\;
The critic loss in
Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion} (line~14)
is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:critic-ym}
  \cL_{\mathrm{critic}}(\psi)
  \;=\;
  \tfrac{1}{2}\,
  \mathbb{E}\bigl[\,\delta_t^{\,2}\,\bigr]
  \;=\;
  \tfrac{1}{2}\,
  \mathbb{E}\bigl[\,\norm{F}^2\,\bigr],
\end{equation}
and the full SVOT loss~\eqref{eq:svot-loss}
decomposes as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:svot-ym}
  \cL(\theta, \psi, \phi)
  \;=\;
  \underbrace{%
    \tfrac{1}{2}\,
    \mathbb{E}\bigl[\,\norm{F}^2\,\bigr]
  }_{\displaystyle\int |F|^2\;\text{(Yang--Mills)}}
  \;+\;
  \underbrace{%
    \alpha\,\DKL\!\bigl(\pi_\theta
      \,\big\|\, \rho^*\bigr)
  }_{\text{Faddeev--Popov (gauge fixing)}}.
\end{equation}
The first term minimises curvature---making
the connection as close to flat as the reward
landscape allows.
The second term breaks gauge redundancy by
penalising deviation from the reference
measure $\rho^*$ (the Drunk Command).
Without the second term, the path integral
$\int e^{-\cL/\alpha}\,d\theta$ diverges
(infinite gauge volume).
With it, the integral is finite and well-conditioned.
The entropy coefficient $\alpha$ controls how much
gauge freedom remains:
$\alpha \to 0$ is hard gauge fixing (greedy);
finite $\alpha$ is soft gauge fixing (SAC).
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Complete gauge--learning dictionary]%
\label{rem:gauge-dictionary}
\color{black!60}%
The following table collects every identification
between gauge theory and the learning framework
of this paper.
Items marked \textbf{K} are kinematics
(Remark~\ref{rem:nn-gauge});
items marked \textbf{D} are dynamics
(Definition~\ref{def:gauge-curvature}).
None is an analogy.
Each is a structural identity:
the left column \emph{is} the right column,
on a different base manifold.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}llc@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Gauge theory}
  & \textbf{Neural network / SVOT}
  & \\
\midrule
Principal bundle $(P, M, G)$
  & $(\Theta, \cX, \cG)$:\;
    parameters, states, gauge group
  & \textbf{K} \\[3pt]
Connection $A_\mu$
  & Policy $\pi_\theta \colon \cX \to \cA$
  & \textbf{K} \\[3pt]
Parallel transport
  & Forward pass:
    $x \xrightarrow{\pi_\theta} u
     \xrightarrow{\text{dyn}} x'$
  & \textbf{K} \\[3pt]
Gauge transformation
  & $\theta \to \theta'$
    with $\mathrm{Viab}(K;\pi_\theta)
    = \mathrm{Viab}(K;\pi_{\theta'})$
  & \textbf{K} \\[3pt]
Gauge fixing
  & Training: SGD picks one
    $\theta^*$ per orbit
  & \textbf{K} \\[3pt]
\midrule
Curvature $F_{\mu\nu}$
  & TD error $\delta_t = r + \gamma Q' - Q$
    \;\eqref{eq:td-curvature}
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
Yang--Mills action $\int |F|^2$
  & Critic loss
    $\tfrac{1}{2}\mathbb{E}[\delta^2]$
    \;\eqref{eq:critic-ym}
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
Faddeev--Popov term
  & $\alpha\,\DKL(\pi \| \rho^*)$
    \;\eqref{eq:svot-ym}
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
Full action $S$
  & SVOT loss $\cL$
    \;\eqref{eq:svot-ym}
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
Field equation $D^* F = J$
  & $\nabla_\theta \cL = 0$
    (converged training)
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
Source current $J$
  & Reward signal $r$
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
Bianchi identity $DF = 0$
  & Bellman consistency:
    $\mathbb{E}[\delta \mid \pi^*] = 0$
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
\midrule
Wilson loop
  & $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) \in \mathrm{SE}(3)$:
    net displacement per gait cycle
  & \textbf{K} \\[3pt]
Mass gap $m > 0$
  & $\norm{\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma) - \mathrm{Id}} > 0$:
    nontrivial holonomy
  & \textbf{K} \\[3pt]
Vacuum
  & Drunk Game: flat connection,
    $\delta = 0$, no reward
  & \textbf{D} \\[3pt]
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The vacuum is the Drunk Game.}\;
At $\alpha \to \infty$
the $\DKL$ term dominates:
$\pi_\theta \to \rho^*$ (uniform random).
All policies are equivalent.
The connection is flat ($\delta = 0$ trivially,
because $Q = \mathrm{const}$ satisfies Bellman
when every action is equally good).
This is the \emph{symmetric phase}:
the gauge group acts freely,
no physical content.
This is Remark~\ref{rem:model-free}:
the Drunk Game is the origin---zero learning,
zero optimisation, the free core is $\cF = \cX$.

At finite $\alpha$, symmetry breaks.
The connection acquires curvature.
A nontrivial minimum of
$S = \int|F|^2 + \alpha\,\DKL$ appears.
$m_* > 0$: the gait moves the robot,
the strategy wins the game,
the queen survives.
This is the Yang--Mills mass gap on
the policy bundle.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Confinement $=$ the black box.}\;
In QCD, quarks are \emph{confined}:
individual quarks cannot be observed in isolation,
only colour-singlet bound states
(protons, mesons) are physical.
The analogous statement for neural networks:
individual neuron activations are
\emph{gauge-dependent}---they change
under reparametrisation
$\theta \to \theta'$ within the same
gauge orbit~\eqref{eq:gauge-equiv}.
Only the \emph{output}
$\pi_\theta(x)$ is gauge-invariant.

The ``black-box problem'' of neural networks
is not a failure of interpretability.
It is \emph{confinement}.
Asking ``what does neuron $j$ in layer $\ell$
represent?''
is asking ``what does quark \#3 in the proton
look like?''
The question is gauge-dependent;
it has no physical answer.
The correct observables are:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item the output $\pi_\theta(x)$
  (the colour-singlet: gauge-invariant);
\item the holonomy $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma)$
  (Wilson loop: path-integrated observable);
\item the free core $\cF$
  (vacuum structure:
  what survives all reparametrisations).
\end{itemize}
Any ``interpretability method'' that reports
per-neuron attributions is reporting gauge artefacts.
A method that reports input--output relationships,
holonomies, or invariant subspaces is reporting
physics.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Locomotion curriculum:
  Stand--Walk--Work]%
\label{def:locomotion-curriculum}
\color{black!60}%
The \emph{locomotion curriculum} is an ordered
sequence of three training phases:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:curriculum}
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{task}}
  \;=\;
  \bigl\{\,
    \underset{\text{Phase 0}}{\mathrm{Stand}},\;
    \underset{\text{Phase 1}}{\mathrm{Walk}},\;
    \underset{\text{Phase 2}}{\mathrm{Work}}
  \,\bigr\}.
\end{equation}
Each phase runs Algorithm~\ref{alg:svot-locomotion}
with different command and constraint parameters.
The policy $\pi_\theta$ carries across phases
(transfer, not reinitialisation).
Promotion from Phase~$n$ to Phase~$n{+}1$
requires Phase~$n$'s holonomy to exceed a threshold.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{2.3cm}p{2.5cm}p{2.5cm}p{2.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Phase 0: Stand}
& \textbf{Phase 1: Walk}
& \textbf{Phase 2: Work} \\
\midrule
Command $v_{\mathrm{cmd}}$
  & $0 \in \R^3$\newline (stay still)
  & $v \sim \rho^*$\newline (Drunk Command)
  & $v \sim \rho^*$\newline $+$ task target \\[5pt]
Constraint $K_n$
  & $x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$\newline (not fall)
  & $x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$\newline (not fall)
  & $x \in K_{\mathrm{loco}}$\newline
    $\wedge$ object intact \\[5pt]
Free core $\cF_n$
  & Upright\newline standing
  & Standing\newline $+$ viable gaits
  & Standing\newline $+$ locomotion\newline
    $+$ grasp \\[5pt]
Gauge group $\cG_n$
  & $\mathrm{SO}(3)$\newline (orientation)
  & $\mathrm{SE}(2)$\newline (position $+$ heading)
  & $\mathrm{SE}(3)$\newline
    $\times\, \mathrm{Diff}(\text{hand})$ \\[5pt]
Holonomy
  & $\mathrm{Id}$\newline (no displacement)
  & $\mathrm{Hol}(\gamma)$\newline
    $\in \mathrm{SE}(3)$
  & Task completion\newline per work cycle \\[5pt]
Promotion test
  & Survives\newline $T_{\min}$ seconds
  & Reaches target\newline location
  & Task done\newline (dish washed) \\[5pt]
Wrong vacuum
  & Falls\newline immediately
  & Stands still\newline ($\mathrm{Hol} \approx \mathrm{Id}$)
  & Walks but\newline does not grasp \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
The ordering $0 \to 1 \to 2$ is the
\emph{unique topological sort} of the
dependency graph:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Walking requires standing
  (walking is a controlled fall from standing;
  $\cF_0 \subset \mathrm{Viab}(K_1)$).
\item Mobile manipulation requires locomotion
  (the robot must reach the task location;
  $\cF_1 \subset \mathrm{Viab}(K_2)$).
\end{itemize}
Skipping Phase~0 forces Phase~1 to discover
standing from scratch---most training time
is wasted on balance, not locomotion.
Skipping Phase~1 strands Phase~2 with a robot
that can stand at the sink but cannot walk to it.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[The curriculum is the expanding lattice
  on a task axis]%
\label{rem:curriculum-lattice}
\color{black!60}%
In Go, the expanding lattice
$\Lambda_R = \{5, 7, \ldots, 31\}$
increases \emph{spatial resolution}:
same game, larger board.
In robotics, $\Lambda_{\mathrm{task}}
= \{\mathrm{Stand}, \mathrm{Walk}, \mathrm{Work}\}$
increases \emph{task complexity}:
same body, harder job.
The mathematical structure is identical:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Go} & \textbf{Robot} \\
\midrule
Lattice
  & Board sizes $\Lambda_R$ (primes)
  & Task phases $\Lambda_{\mathrm{task}}$ \\
Pool carryover
  & Frameworks carry\newline across scales
  & Policy $\pi_\theta$ carries\newline
    across phases \\
Promotion
  & $V_t > $ threshold
  & $\mathrm{Hol} > $ threshold \\
Initialisation
  & Pool from previous scale
  & $\theta$ from previous phase \\
Free core
  & Two eyes (all sizes)
  & Standing (all phases) \\
Wrong vacuum
  & High NLR, low territory
  & Low $\norm{F}^2$, trivial Hol \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Product lattice.}\;
Within each phase, difficulty also increases:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Phase~0: flat ground
  $\to$ slope $\to$ uneven $\to$ soft;
\item Phase~1: slow
  $\to$ fast $\to$ variable speed
  $\to$ outdoor;
\item Phase~2: pick up
  $\to$ carry $\to$ place
  $\to$ wash $\to$ sequence tasks.
\end{itemize}
The full curriculum is therefore a
\emph{product lattice}
$\Lambda = \Lambda_{\mathrm{task}}
  \times \Lambda_{\mathrm{difficulty}}$.
Go has one lattice dimension (board size).
The robot has two (task type $\times$ difficulty).
Same pool carryover, same promotion logic,
same gauge diagnostics at every node.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Free core nesting.}\;
The key structural property is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:free-core-nesting}
  \cF_0
  \;\subset\;
  \mathrm{Viab}(K_1)
  \;\subset\;
  \mathrm{Viab}(K_2).
\end{equation}
Each phase's free core is contained in the
next phase's viability kernel.
This is not a design choice---it is forced
by the physics:
you cannot manipulate while falling
($\cF_0 = \emptyset$ implies
$\mathrm{Viab}(K_2) = \emptyset$).
The curriculum respects this nesting
by initialising Phase~$n{+}1$
from Phase~$n$'s converged policy,
which is already inside $\mathrm{Viab}(K_{n+1})$.
Random initialisation would start outside
the viability kernel with high probability.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Gauge group extension.}\;
The gauge group grows with each phase:
$\mathrm{SO}(3)
  \hookrightarrow \mathrm{SE}(2)
  \hookrightarrow \mathrm{SE}(3)
  \times \mathrm{Diff}(\text{hand})$.
Each extension adds physical degrees of freedom
that the previous phase did not use.
Standing has orientation symmetry only.
Walking adds translational symmetry.
Manipulation adds hand configuration.
More gauge freedom requires a larger network
(Remark~\ref{rem:nn-gauge}:
overparametrisation = larger gauge group = easier
training).
The curriculum provides this incrementally:
Phase~0's small network initialises
Phase~1's larger network via parameter padding,
and Phase~1 initialises Phase~2.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The Drunk/Queen/King triangle
operates within each phase.}\;
The curriculum is the \emph{outer} lattice.
Within each phase, the \emph{inner} learning
loop is the same triangle as in Go:
the Drunk explores
(random standing / random walking /
random grasping),
the Queen refines
(pool replicator on contact-mode strategies),
and the King optimises
(value-based SAC with
curvature-adaptive~$\alpha$).
The gauge diagnostics
(Remark~\ref{rem:gauge-alg})
detect wrong vacuums at every phase.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The endpoint.}\;
Phase~2 converges when
$\mathrm{Hol}_{\mathrm{task}} > 0$:
the robot completes a task cycle
(carries a dish from counter to rack,
collects trash from floor to bin).
At this point the free core
$\cF_2$ includes standing, locomotion,
and manipulation---the robot is \emph{useful}.
The expanding lattice has reached its
UV completion.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Executor assembling]\label{def:executor-assembling}
Let $\cT = \{t_1, \ldots, t_k\}$ be a finite set of \emph{executor types},
each with movement graph $G_{t_i}$.
An \emph{executor} $\pi_{t}: s \to a$ is a single-type policy
(one piece, one objective: eat or survive).
A \emph{scheduler} $\sigma: s \to \Delta^{k-1}$ selects which
executor to activate at each turn.
\emph{Executor assembling} is the bilevel online optimization:
\begin{align}
  \text{Inner:} \quad & \min_{\pi_t} \; \cL_t(\pi_t)
    \quad \forall\, t \in \cT
    \quad \text{(embarrassingly parallel)}, \label{eq:inner} \\
  \text{Outer:} \quad & \min_\sigma \; -\mathrm{NLR}(\sigma; \pi_1, \ldots, \pi_k)
    \quad \text{s.t.\ not\_lose at every step}. \label{eq:outer}
\end{align}
The inner problems are independent MDPs on each $G_t$.
The outer problem is a constrained policy on~$\Delta^{k-1}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Chess as MOPL isomorphism]\label{rem:chess-iso}
Replacing framework types with piece types yields the
same optimal switching structure (Remark~\ref{rem:switching}):

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Go (MOPL)} & \textbf{Chess (Pacman)} \\
\midrule
Executor types $\cT$ & \{territorial, influence, \ldots\} & \{P, N, B, R, Q, K\} \\
Executor $\pi_t$ & Framework policy & Pacman (single-piece MDP) \\
Scheduler $\sigma$ & Pool selection & Piece scheduler \\
Simplex & $\Delta^4$ ($k = 5$) & $\Delta^5$ ($k = 6$) \\
Inner opt & Pool update per framework & Pacman training per type \\
Outer opt & Pool allocation & Scheduler on $\Delta^5$ \\
Constraint & $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$ per scale & No checkmate \\
Movement graph $G_t$ & Same board $\forall\, t$ & Different per type \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip
\noindent
The one structural difference: in Go all executors share the same
board; in chess each executor has a different movement
graph~$G_t$ (knight $\neq$ bishop).
The inner problems are heterogeneous but still embarrassingly
parallel.
The outer problem (scheduler) is identical in both cases:
optimal switching on a simplex with a not-lose constraint.
A pawn is just a pawn.
The king and the queen are just pieces.
They are nothing but points on $\Delta^{k-1}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Spectral coloring as deterministic workflow]%
\label{rem:spectral-workflow}
This document uses seven left-bar colours for its
environment types, one per band of Newton's visible spectrum
(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}赤橙黄绿青蓝紫\end{CJK}):
%
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}clcl@{}}
\toprule
$\lambda$ & Colour & Environment & Energy \\
\midrule
\textcolor{specRed}{700\,nm} & \textcolor{specRed}{Red\;(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}赤\end{CJK})}
        & Remark      & lowest---qualitative \\
\textcolor{specOrange}{620\,nm} & \textcolor{specOrange}{Orange\;(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}橙\end{CJK})}
        & Definition  & naming \\
\textcolor{specYellow}{580\,nm} & \textcolor{specYellow}{Yellow\;(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}黄\end{CJK})}
        & Lemma       & technical stepping stone \\
\textcolor{specGreen}{530\,nm} & \textcolor{specGreen}{Green\;(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}绿\end{CJK})}
        & Proposition & intermediate claim \\
\textcolor{specCyan}{490\,nm} & \textcolor{specCyan}{Cyan\;(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}青\end{CJK})}
        & Corollary   & consequence of theorem \\
\textcolor{specBlue}{450\,nm} & \textcolor{specBlue}{Blue\;(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}蓝\end{CJK})}
        & Theorem     & main result \\
\textcolor{specViolet}{400\,nm}$^{\dagger}$ & \textcolor{specViolet}{Violet\;(\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}紫\end{CJK})}
        & Proof       & verification gate$^{\dagger}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
%
\noindent
{\small $^{\dagger}$\,$\lambda_7 = 400$\,nm is \emph{out of the box}:
seven environment types on six die faces
($\dim\mathrm{SE}(3) = 6$) forces one type outside.
The proof is not a move; it is the \emph{gate}
that validates moves (Section~\ref{sec:gate}).}

\medskip
The ordering is not decorative---it is a \emph{deterministic
workflow}.
A reader scanning the page processes
the full logical spectrum at a glance:
\textcolor{specViolet}{violet} (proof/verified) suppresses uncertainty in
\textcolor{specRed}{red} (remark/qualitative),
exactly as UV renormalization suppresses IR divergences
in quantum field theory
(Section~\ref{sec:rg}).
With all seven colours on screen, the neuron dynamics
of reading operates at full bandwidth:
no bottleneck, no stuck state, deterministic flow.
\end{remark}

% ============================================================
%  Section 10: Conclusion
% ============================================================
\section{Conclusion}\label{sec:conclusion}

We have presented Math Mirror, a self-validating byte-level
transformer for agentic mathematics.
The core claims are:

\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{A model trained only on verified math is enough.}
  The self-validated training pipeline
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:correct}) ensures that every training
  example is mathematically correct.
  The model need not learn world knowledge; it needs only to
  learn mathematical operations.

\item \textbf{Self-validation eliminates hallucination within
  the verified domain.}
  The three-level verification gate
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:soundness}, Corollary~\ref{cor:no-hallucination})
  rejects any output that cannot be confirmed correct.
  Within the domain of symbolic verification, the hallucination
  rate is zero.

\item \textbf{Transparency is achievable.}
  The byte-level vocabulary (Definition~\ref{def:vocab})
  ensures that the model's internal representation is identical
  to the user-visible output.
  No hidden tokenization, no hidden representations.

\item \textbf{Privacy is achievable by architecture.}
  The explicit finetuning protocol
  (Definition~\ref{def:finetune},
  Proposition~\ref{prop:privacy}) ensures that the model
  learns only what the user explicitly provides and verifies.

\item \textbf{The mirror reflects structure, not opinion.}
  Mathematics has no opinion.
  A model trained only on math, verified only by math,
  outputs only math.
  The mirror reflects the mathematical structure of the
  input, nothing more.
\end{enumerate}

The embed-prove-pullback architecture
(Definition~\ref{def:epp}) separates the concerns cleanly:
the LLM handles natural language at the boundary;
the mirror handles mathematics in the interior;
the verifier stands as the gate between computation and output.

The connections to agent nucleation (\S\ref{sec:agent}),
renormalization (\S\ref{sec:rg}), and tabular SARSA
(\S\ref{sec:sarsa}) are not decorative.
The mirror is a Grade~0 tool that nucleates on demand,
computes, verifies, and collapses---the minimal unit of
agentic computation.
Distillation from a large LLM to the small mirror is RG flow
from UV to IR, and the verification gate enforces gauge
invariance: the truth of the output is independent of the
representation.
Checkpoint selection is tabular RL---the only honest RL---where
the model's own parameter states compete in a multi-LLM court,
ranked by what they produce, not by what they are.
The Queen's Gambit (\S\ref{sec:queens-gambit}) and the
King's Predictive Control (\S\ref{sec:kings-control})
close the loop: the forward Fokker--Planck density and
the backward S-MPPI value function must agree---calibration
is the DRM resonance condition.
The two learned temperatures (\S\ref{sec:double-boltzmann})
are the minimal sufficient controller: where to look, and
how sharply to act.

The Math Mirror is small ($\sim$25M parameters), transparent
(ASCII vocabulary), self-validating (SymPy oracle),
privacy-preserving (explicit finetuning only), and
mathematically honest (outputs are verified or rejected).
It does math. Only math. That is enough.

\appendix

\section{Implementation Details}\label{app:impl}

The Math Mirror is implemented in Python using PyTorch.
The source code is organized as follows:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{File} & \textbf{Contents} \\
\midrule
\texttt{math\_mirror/model.py} & Byte-level transformer (Definition~\ref{def:model}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/verifier.py} & Symbolic oracle $\cG$ (Definition~\ref{def:oracle}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/bootstrap.py} & Self-validated data generation (Definition~\ref{def:dist}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/mirror.py} & Agentic reflection loop (Algorithm~\ref{alg:reflect}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/finetune.py} & Explicit finetuning (Definition~\ref{def:finetune}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/mcp/arxiv\_source.py} & arXiv fetch + fill-in-the-blank (Definition~\ref{def:fitb}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/mcp/llm\_court.py} & Multi-LLM court (Definition~\ref{def:court}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/mcp/mirror\_train.py} & SARSA scheduler (Theorem~\ref{thm:sarsa}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/go/mopl.py} & MOPL self-play engine (Algorithm~\ref{alg:mopl}) \\
\texttt{math\_mirror/go/king.py} & S-MPPI prediction in JAX (Definition~\ref{def:smppi}) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection{Model hyperparameters}

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lrl@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Hyperparameter} & \textbf{Value} & \textbf{Justification} \\
\midrule
Vocabulary size $|\cV|$ & 256 & ASCII table (Definition~\ref{def:vocab}) \\
Embedding dimension $d$ & 256 & One dimension per vocab entry \\
Number of layers $L$ & 12 & Empirical: sufficient for polynomial arithmetic \\
Number of heads $H$ & 8 & $d/H = 32$ per head \\
Context length $T_{\max}$ & 2048 & Sufficient for single-expression computation \\
FFN hidden dimension & $4d = 1024$ & Standard 4$\times$ expansion \\
Weight initialization & Xavier uniform & Standard for transformers \\
Activation function & GELU & Smooth approximation to ReLU \\
Normalization & Pre-LayerNorm & Stable training \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection{Verification gate implementation}

The verification gate implements three levels:

\begin{algorithm}[H]
\caption{Verification Gate $\cG$
  \textup{[Three-Level Symbolic--Numeric Oracle]}}\label{alg:verify}
\begin{algorithmic}[1]
\Require Expression string $e$
\Ensure $\texttt{ACCEPT}$ or $\texttt{REJECT}$
\State \textbf{Level G1:} Try \texttt{parse\_expr($e$)}
\If{parse fails}
  \State \Return \texttt{REJECT}
\EndIf
\State \textbf{Level G2:} If $e$ contains ``\texttt{=}'', split into \texttt{lhs}, \texttt{rhs}
\State $d \gets \texttt{simplify(lhs - rhs)}$
\If{$d = 0$}
  \State \Return \texttt{ACCEPT} \Comment{Symbolic proof}
\EndIf
\If{$d$ has no free symbols}
  \State \Return $|d| < 10^{-12}$ ? \texttt{ACCEPT} : \texttt{REJECT}
\EndIf
\State \textbf{Numerical fallback:}
\For{$i = 1$ to $10$}
  \State Sample $x \sim \mathrm{Uniform}([-10, 10]^k)$
  \If{$|d(x)| > 10^{-12}$}
    \State \Return \texttt{REJECT}
  \EndIf
\EndFor
\State \Return \texttt{ACCEPT} \Comment{Numerical evidence}
\end{algorithmic}
\end{algorithm}

\section{Notation Summary}\label{app:notation}

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{@{}cl@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Symbol} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\midrule
$\cV$ & Vocabulary $= \{0, 1, \ldots, 255\}$ \\
$\cM_\theta$ & Math Mirror model with parameters $\theta$ \\
$\cG$ & Symbolic verification oracle (SymPy) \\
$\cD$ & Training distribution (verified examples) \\
$\cS_{\text{NL}}$ & Natural language space \\
$\cS_{\text{math}}$ & Mathematical ASCII space \\
$\partial\cS$ & Translation boundary (LLM interface) \\
$\Embed$ & LLM: natural language $\to$ math ASCII \\
$\Mirror_\theta$ & Mirror: math ASCII $\to$ math ASCII \\
$\Pullback$ & LLM: math ASCII $\to$ natural language \\
$V(T, B)$ & Agent function (target, basis) \\
$\cL(\theta)$ & Next-byte prediction loss \\
$\DKL$ & Kullback--Leibler divergence \\
$\Breg$ & Bregman divergence \\
$m_*$ & Mass gap (spectral gap of the model) \\
$T_{\max}$ & Maximum context length $(= 2048)$ \\
$J_k$ & LLM judge $k$ in the multi-LLM court \\
$\pi_k$ & Ranking (permutation) produced by judge $k$ \\
$Q(\theta, a)$ & SARSA action-value for checkpoint $\theta$, action $a$ \\
$N_1, N_2, N_3$ & MCP server nodes (arXiv, court, train) \\
$\mu_{\text{proof}}$ & Proof masking operator (Definition~\ref{def:fitb}) \\
$w_{\text{arXiv}}$ & arXiv curriculum mixing weight $(0 \to 0.5)$ \\
$\delta$ & Chunk overlap $(= 256)$ for long proofs \\
$G = G_1 \circ G_2 \circ G_3$ & Three-lock verification gate \\
$\kappa$ & Holonomy curvature (binocular disparity) \\
$W_t$ & Symbolic work at training step $t$ \\
$\mathrm{NLR}(N_k)$ & Not-lose rate at scale $N_k$ (Definition~\ref{def:nlr-gate}) \\
$\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}$ & Scale selection temperature (Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}) \\
$\tau_{\mathrm{IR}}$ & Move selection temperature (Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}) \\
$\hat{V}(s)$ & S-MPPI predicted value at scale $s$ (Definition~\ref{def:smppi}) \\
$\cH(\cP, N, T)$ & Rollout horizon: set of $N$ simulated futures of depth $T$ (Definition~\ref{def:horizon}) \\
$H$ & Data window: number of most recent games the King sees (Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}) \\
$K$ & Viability constraint: pool states with $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}) \\
$\mathrm{Viab}(K)$ & Viability kernel: largest subset of $K$ with perpetual feasibility (Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}) \\
$f_\theta$ & Amortized King: learned warm-start for $(\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}, \tau_{\mathrm{IR}})$ (Definition~\ref{def:amortized-king}) \\
$k$ & Number of strategic frameworks in the pool ($= 5$) \\
$S$ & Number of board scales, $S = |\Lambda_R|$ ($= 9$) \\
$\rho^*_N$ & Drunk reference measure on $N \times N$ board (Definition~\ref{def:svot}) \\
\midrule
\multicolumn{2}{@{}l}{\textit{Go / MOPL symbols}} \\
$\cP$ & Strategic framework pool (set of $k$ frameworks $+$ weights $\bar{w}$) \\
$\bar{w} \in [0,1]^k$ & Pool weights (running-average win rates, clamped to $[0.01, 0.99]$) \\
$\Lambda_R$ & Expanding lattice of prime board sizes $= \{5, 7, 11, 13, 17, 19, 23, 29, 31\}$ \\
$F(\pi)$ & Free energy of policy $\pi$ (Definition~\ref{def:transcommutation}) \\
$\cF$ & Free core: largest viable invariant set (Proposition~\ref{prop:viability}) \\
$M_H$ & Outcome matrix restricted to the last $H$ games (Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}) \\
$\pi_f \in \Delta^{k-1}$ & Framework selection distribution $= \softmax(\log \bar{w} / \tau_{\mathrm{IR}})$ \\
$\pi_{\mathrm{scale}} \in \Delta^{S-1}$ & Scale selection distribution $= \softmax(\hat{V} / \tau_{\mathrm{UV}})$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\clearpage

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{@{}cl@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Symbol} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\midrule

  (\S\ref{sec:locomotion})}} \\

  black-box integrator, no $\nabla$
  (Remark~\ref{rem:el-engine}) \\

  (Definition~\ref{def:student-t-policy}) \\

  effective contact-mode count
  (Remark~\ref{rem:student-t-forced}) \\

  gate threshold in Algorithm~\ref{alg:queen} \\

% ============================================================
%  Appendix C: The Golden Apple
% ============================================================
\section{The Golden Apple: A Learnable Artificial Retina
  via Spectral MOPL}\label{app:golden-apple}

\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}
\noindent
\textit{%
如果你更愿意看见，而不是看不见，那么，你就已经在看了。
因为剩下的，都是可学习的。}
\end{CJK}

\bigskip

The spectral colouring of this document
(Remark~\ref{rem:spectral-workflow}) decomposes a logical
argument into seven frequency bands, one per Newton spectral
colour.
A biological retina does exactly the same thing to light.
This appendix formalizes the isomorphism and asks whether
it can be inverted: given a damaged retina, can a learnable
device restore vision by training a spectral MOPL on the
user's neural response?

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The biological retina as expanding lattice}
\label{app:retina-lattice}

\begin{definition}[Retinal lattice]\label{def:retinal-lattice}
The human retina is a finite lattice $\Lambda_{\mathrm{ret}}$
of photoreceptor cells on a curved surface $\Sigma \subset \R^3$
(the interior of the eye).
Two cell types occupy the lattice:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Rods}
  ($\sim\!1.2 \times 10^8$ cells, one spectral type):
  broadband luminance detectors, high sensitivity, low acuity.
  These are the \emph{IR channel}---low spatial frequency,
  high gain.

\item \textbf{Cones}
  ($\sim\!6 \times 10^6$ cells, three spectral types
  S/M/L $\approx$ blue/green/red):
  narrowband colour detectors, low sensitivity, high acuity.
  These are the \emph{UV channel}---high spatial frequency,
  low gain.
\end{enumerate}
The rod-to-cone ratio is approximately $20{:}1$.
The two channels tile the same lattice but at different
densities, yielding a \emph{dual-rate expanding lattice}:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Fovea} (central $\sim\!1.5$\,mm):
  cone-dominated, lattice spacing $d \approx 2.5\,\mu$m.
  This is the UV regime---maximal spatial resolution.
\item \textbf{Periphery} (remaining $\sim\!40$\,mm):
  rod-dominated, effective spacing $d \approx 10$--$50\,\mu$m.
  This is the IR regime---low resolution, high sensitivity.
\end{itemize}
The fovea-to-periphery gradient is a radial expanding lattice
analogous to $\Lambda_R$ in
Section~\ref{sec:expanding}, with the fovea playing the
role of the smallest prime scale and the far periphery
playing the largest.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Nyquist constraint on the retinal lattice]%
\label{prop:retina-nyquist}
The maximum spatial frequency resolvable by the retinal
lattice at eccentricity $\theta$ is
\[
  f_{\max}(\theta)
    \;=\; \frac{1}{2\,d(\theta)},
\]
where $d(\theta)$ is the local lattice spacing.
At the foveal centre ($\theta = 0$):
$f_{\max}(0) \approx 60$~cycles/degree,
which matches the psychophysically measured human acuity
limit.
At $\theta = 30^\circ$:
$f_{\max} \approx 5$~cycles/degree.

This is a Nyquist gate
(cf.\ Proposition~\ref{prop:lattice-complete}):
the lattice spacing determines the maximum resolvable
frequency, and no amount of neural processing can exceed it.
The retinal lattice \emph{is} the UV cutoff of biological
vision.
\end{proposition}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Retinal renormalization: the 126:1 compression}
\label{app:retina-rg}

\begin{definition}[Retinal RG flow]\label{def:retina-rg}
The optic nerve carries $\sim\!10^6$ fibres, each driven
by a retinal ganglion cell (RGC).
Each RGC pools input from multiple photoreceptors:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item In the fovea: $\sim\!1{:}1$ (one cone per RGC).
  Minimal compression.  UV preserved.
\item In the periphery: $\sim\!100{:}1$ (many rods per RGC).
  Massive compression.  Only IR survives.
\end{itemize}
The global compression ratio is
\[
  \rho
    \;=\; \frac{|\Lambda_{\mathrm{ret}}|}{|\text{optic nerve}|}
    \;\approx\; \frac{1.26 \times 10^8}{10^6}
    \;=\; 126.
\]
This is a \emph{hardware RG flow}: it happens inside the eye,
before the signal reaches the brain.
The retina performs its own renormalization, sending to the
visual cortex a coarse-grained representation at $126\times$
lower resolution than the raw photon stream.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Comparison to MOPL RG]%
\label{rem:retina-mopl-rg}
The retinal RG has the same structure as distillation-as-RG
(Section~\ref{sec:rg}):
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
 & \textbf{Retina} & \textbf{MOPL} \\
\midrule
UV layer & $1.26 \times 10^8$ photoreceptors &
  full pool $\cP$ (all frameworks $\times$ all scales) \\
IR layer & $10^6$ optic nerve fibres &
  compressed policy $\pi^*$ \\
RG operator & ganglion cell pooling &
  pool update rule \\
Compression & $126{:}1$ & $k \to 1$
  (winner framework) \\
Preserved & foveal UV (acuity) &
  winning framework identity \\
Discarded & peripheral photon-by-photon detail &
  losing frameworks' internal state \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The isomorphism is Level~B (same mathematical skeleton,
different physical substrate):
both are dissipative flows on a lattice that preserve
the UV core while discarding IR redundancy.
\end{remark}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The two photoreceptor types as dual channels}
\label{app:dual-channel}

\begin{definition}[Dual-channel vision]\label{def:dual-channel}
Let $\Lambda_{\mathrm{ret}} = \Lambda_{\mathrm{rod}} \cup
\Lambda_{\mathrm{cone}}$ be the retinal lattice decomposed
into rod and cone sublattices.
Define two signal channels:
\begin{align}
  I_{\mathrm{IR}}(x,t)
    &\;=\; \sum_{j \in \Lambda_{\mathrm{rod}}}
      \phi_j(x)\, r_j(t),
    \label{eq:ir-channel} \\
  I_{\mathrm{UV}}(x,t)
    &\;=\; \sum_{j \in \Lambda_{\mathrm{cone}}}
      \psi_j(x)\, c_j(t),
    \label{eq:uv-channel}
\end{align}
where $r_j(t)$ and $c_j(t)$ are the photocurrent responses
of rod $j$ and cone $j$ at time $t$, and $\phi_j, \psi_j$
are spatial basis functions centred at each cell's position.

The full visual signal is the pair
$\bigl(I_{\mathrm{IR}}, I_{\mathrm{UV}}\bigr)$.
Scotopic vision (dim light) uses only $I_{\mathrm{IR}}$.
Photopic vision (bright light) uses primarily
$I_{\mathrm{UV}}$ with $I_{\mathrm{IR}}$ providing
peripheral awareness.
Mesopic vision blends both.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Rods and cones as framework types]%
\label{rem:rod-cone-framework}
In the MOPL framework (Algorithm~\ref{alg:mopl}),
each framework type specialises in a different strategy.
The rod/cone dichotomy is isomorphic:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
& \textbf{Rod} & \textbf{Cone} \\
\midrule
MOPL analog & \texttt{territorial} (broad, safe) &
  \texttt{aggressive} (sharp, risky) \\
Spectral type & 1 (broadband) & 3 (S/M/L) \\
Population & $\sim 1.2 \times 10^8$ & $\sim 6 \times 10^6$ \\
Regime & low-light (IR) & bright-light (UV) \\
Resolution & low & high \\
Gain & high & low \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The pool scheduler
(Definition~\ref{def:executor-assembling})
decides how much weight to give each channel---just as
the retina shifts between scotopic and photopic modes
by adjusting the rod/cone balance.
The ``lighting condition'' of the retina is the
analog of the temperature~$\tau_{\mathrm{UV}}$
in the Double Boltzmann controller
(Definition~\ref{def:two-temp}).
\end{remark}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The 7-channel artificial retina}
\label{app:7channel}

\begin{definition}[Spectral MOPL retina]\label{def:spectral-retina}
A \emph{spectral MOPL retina} is a device $\cR$ consisting of:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Sensor array.}
  An $N \times N$ grid of photodetectors, each equipped
  with $K = 7$ spectral filters corresponding to
  Newton's visible spectrum
  (\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}%
    \textcolor{specRed}{赤}\,%
    \textcolor{specOrange}{橙}\,%
    \textcolor{specYellow}{黄}\,%
    \textcolor{specGreen}{绿}\,%
    \textcolor{specCyan}{青}\,%
    \textcolor{specBlue}{蓝}\,%
    \textcolor{specViolet}{紫}%
  \end{CJK}):
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:spectral-channels}
  \begin{aligned}
    \textcolor{specRed}{\lambda_1} &= \textcolor{specRed}{700\,\text{nm}}, &
    \textcolor{specOrange}{\lambda_2} &= \textcolor{specOrange}{620\,\text{nm}}, &
    \textcolor{specYellow}{\lambda_3} &= \textcolor{specYellow}{580\,\text{nm}}, \\
    \textcolor{specGreen}{\lambda_4} &= \textcolor{specGreen}{530\,\text{nm}}, &
    \textcolor{specCyan}{\lambda_5} &= \textcolor{specCyan}{490\,\text{nm}}, &
    \textcolor{specBlue}{\lambda_6} &= \textcolor{specBlue}{450\,\text{nm}}, \\[4pt]
    \textcolor{specViolet}{\lambda_7} &= \textcolor{specViolet}{400\,\text{nm}}^{\dagger}.
  \end{aligned}
  \end{equation}
  Each pixel produces a 7-vector
  $s_{ij} \in \R^7_{\geq 0}$.

\item \textbf{Encoder.}
  A learnable mapping
  $E_\theta \colon \R^{N \times N \times 7} \to \R^M$
  that compresses the $7N^2$-dimensional sensor output to
  $M$ stimulation channels, where $M$ is the number of
  electrodes in the neural interface.

\item \textbf{Neural interface.}
  An electrode array (epiretinal, subretinal, or cortical)
  delivering current pattern $E_\theta(s) \in \R^M$ to the
  visual pathway.

\item \textbf{Feedback channel.}
  The user's perceptual report: ``I see / I don't see /
  I see \emph{X}''.
  This is the gate
  (cf.\ Section~\ref{sec:gate}).
\end{enumerate}
The device operates in a closed MOPL loop:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:retina-mopl}
  s \;\xrightarrow{E_\theta}\;
  \text{stimulation}
  \;\xrightarrow{\text{neural pathway}}\;
  \text{percept}
  \;\xrightarrow{\text{user feedback}}\;
  \text{gate}
  \;\xrightarrow{\text{pool update}}\;
  \theta.
\end{equation}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Why 7 channels, not 3]%
\label{rem:why-7}
The biological retina uses $K = 3$ cone types (S/M/L).
The spectral MOPL retina uses $K = 7$.
This is deliberate oversampling:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $K = 3$: minimal representation.
  The biological system has zero redundancy
  in the spectral dimension.
  Colour-blind individuals ($K = 2$) lose an entire
  perceptual axis.
\item $K = 7$: oversampled.
  The $7 \to 3$ compression is performed by the
  encoder~$E_\theta$, which \emph{learns} which linear
  combinations the user's brain can decode.
  Redundancy $= $ robustness:
  if one channel degrades, the remaining six still
  span the visible spectrum.
\end{itemize}
The ratio $7/3 \approx 2.3$ is the oversampling factor.
The encoder's job is to find the optimal
$3$-dimensional (or fewer) subspace of $\R^7$ that
the user's neural pathway can resolve---a learned
PCA adapted to the individual brain.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Spectral Nyquist for the artificial retina]%
\label{prop:spectral-nyquist}
Let $\Delta\lambda = \max_{k} |\lambda_{k+1} - \lambda_k|$
be the maximum spectral gap between adjacent filter centres.
The spectral Nyquist frequency is
$f_{\lambda} = 1 / (2\,\Delta\lambda)$.
For $K = 7$ uniformly spaced filters in $[400, 700]$\,nm:
$\Delta\lambda = 50$\,nm,
$f_\lambda = 0.01\,\text{nm}^{-1}$.

For $K = 3$ (biological):
$\Delta\lambda \approx 100$--$150$\,nm
(the S--M gap is $\sim\!90$\,nm, the M--L gap is $\sim\!35$\,nm,
the S--L gap is $\sim\!125$\,nm),
$f_\lambda \approx 0.004$\,nm$^{-1}$.

The $K = 7$ retina resolves $2.5\times$ finer spectral
features than the biological eye.
This surplus is not wasted: the encoder uses it for
robustness and personalisation.
\end{proposition}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The MOPL training loop for vision}
\label{app:retina-training}

\begin{definition}[Visual MOPL training]\label{def:visual-mopl}
Training the spectral MOPL retina follows the expanding-lattice
protocol (Section~\ref{sec:expanding}) with the following
correspondence:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.22\linewidth}p{0.33\linewidth}p{0.35\linewidth}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{MOPL (Go)} & \textbf{MOPL (Retina)} & \textbf{Equation} \\
\midrule
Board size $N_k$ & Stimulus complexity level $k$ &
  Simple $\to$ complex \\
Framework type & Encoder config.\ $\theta_j$ &
  Different spectral weightings \\
Opponent (Heuristic\-Goer) & Test stimulus
  (calibrated target) & Known ground truth \\
Game outcome & User percept report &
  ``I see a horizontal bar'' \\
Not-lose gate & Perception gate &
  User identifies $\geq$ threshold \\
Pool update & Encoder weight update &
  $\theta \gets \theta - \eta\,\nabla_\theta
  \cL(\text{percept}, \text{target})$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Expanding-stimulus curriculum]%
\label{def:stimulus-curriculum}
The training curriculum expands in complexity,
analogous to the expanding lattice $\Lambda_R$:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Level 1 (light/dark):}
  Can the user distinguish light from dark?
  Binary gate.
  This is the $5 \times 5$ scale.
\item \textbf{Level 2 (orientation):}
  Can the user detect a horizontal vs.\ vertical bar?
  $90^\circ$ discrimination.
  This is the $7 \times 7$ scale.
\item \textbf{Level 3 (spatial frequency):}
  Can the user resolve gratings of increasing
  spatial frequency?
  Nyquist probing.
  This is the $11 \times 11$ scale.
\item \textbf{Level 4 (colour):}
  Can the user distinguish spectral bands?
  With $K = 7$ channels, test pairwise discrimination
  of adjacent bands.
  This is the $13 \times 13$ scale.
\item \textbf{Level 5 (shape):}
  Can the user identify simple shapes
  (circle, square, triangle)?
  Template matching.
  This is the $17 \times 17$ scale.
\item \textbf{Level 6 (scene):}
  Can the user navigate a simple environment?
  Functional vision.
  This is the $19 \times 19$ scale---the
  ``formal game'' of vision.
\item \textbf{Level 7 (reading):}
  Can the user read large text?
  This requires both spatial resolution (UV)
  and contrast sensitivity (IR).
  The $23 \times 23$ and beyond.
\end{enumerate}
Each level has a not-lose gate
(Definition~\ref{def:nlr-gate}):
the user must achieve $\geq\!80\%$ correct identification
before promotion to the next level.
If the gate fails, the encoder trains more at the current
level (cf.\ Algorithm~\ref{alg:mopl}).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Convergence of the visual MOPL]%
\label{prop:visual-convergence}
If the user's visual cortex has nonzero plasticity
(i.e., it can learn \emph{any} mapping from electrode
stimulation to percept), and if the encoder has sufficient
capacity (universal approximation), then the visual MOPL
converges:
\[
  \exists\, \theta^* \;\text{such that}\;
  \mathrm{NLR}(\theta^*, k) \geq 1 - \epsilon
  \quad \forall\; k \leq K_{\max},
\]
where $K_{\max}$ is the highest complexity level
achievable given the electrode count~$M$.

The convergence follows from the same argument as
Proposition~\ref{prop:lattice-complete}:
the spectral gap $m_* > 0$ of the user's neural response
(the minimum detectable stimulus change)
controls the resolution, and the expanding lattice
terminates when the Nyquist condition is met:
$\max_k \Delta_k \leq \epsilon \, m_* / L$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[The mass gap is the user's visual threshold]%
\label{rem:mass-gap-vision}
The mass gap $m_*$ in the visual MOPL has a direct
physiological interpretation: it is the user's
\emph{just-noticeable difference} (JND)---the smallest
change in stimulation that produces a detectable
change in percept.
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $m_* > 0$: the user has nonzero visual sensitivity.
  Training will converge.
  The retina can be calibrated.
\item $m_* = 0$: the user cannot distinguish any
  stimulation patterns.
  The visual cortex is either absent or non-plastic.
  Training will not converge.
  The golden apple cannot help.
\end{itemize}
The condition $m_* > 0$ is the \emph{necessary and
sufficient} condition for the artificial retina
to work.
It is the same mass gap that appears in
Yang--Mills theory~\cite{YM54} (the existence of a spectral gap
in the Hamiltonian; see also~\cite{Zhang2026YM}),
in the MOPL framework
(the not-lose gate), and in the verification gate
(the minimum confidence threshold).
All are the same mathematical object:
a positive lower bound on a spectral gap that
guarantees convergence.
\end{remark}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The personalisation principle}
\label{app:personalisation}

\begin{remark}[Why fixed mappings fail]%
\label{rem:fixed-fail}
Existing retinal prostheses (Argus~II: 60 electrodes,
PRIMA: 378 photodiodes, Orion: 60 cortical electrodes)
use fixed encoder mappings: the same $E$ for all patients.
This is equivalent to using a single framework in MOPL
without pool updates.
The result: patients can detect light and motion,
but rarely achieve functional vision
(letter reading, face recognition).

The personalisation gap is the difference between
the fixed mapping's performance and the optimal
user-specific mapping:
\[
  \Delta_{\text{pers}}
    \;=\; \mathrm{NLR}(\theta^*) - \mathrm{NLR}(\theta_{\mathrm{fixed}})
    \;\geq\; 0.
\]
Hypothesis: $\Delta_{\text{pers}} \gg 0$ for most patients,
because each brain's visual cortex has been shaped by a
unique developmental history.
The encoder must learn $\theta^*$ for each user individually.
This is the MOPL training loop
(Definition~\ref{def:visual-mopl}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[BrainPort as existence proof]%
\label{rem:brainport}
The BrainPort device (Wicab, Inc.) converts camera images
to electrical stimulation patterns on the tongue
($20 \times 20$ electrode array, $400$ channels).
Users learn to ``see'' through their tongue in
$\sim\!15$ minutes of training.
This demonstrates that:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item The visual cortex can learn arbitrary mappings
  (tongue $\neq$ retina, yet vision occurs).
\item The learning is fast (minutes, not months).
\item The bottleneck is not the neural pathway---it is the
  \emph{encoder} (camera-to-stimulation mapping).
\end{enumerate}
BrainPort uses a fixed mapping.
A BrainPort with MOPL training---where the
camera-to-tongue encoder adapts to the individual
user's neural response---would be a spectral MOPL
retina implemented on the tongue.
The tongue has $\sim\!10{,}000$ taste buds; only
$400$ are used.
The gap between available bandwidth and utilised
bandwidth is the personalisation gap
$\Delta_{\text{pers}}$.
\end{remark}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The pigeonhole structure: 7 colours on 6 faces}
\label{app:pigeonhole}

\begin{proposition}[The proof is outside the die]%
\label{prop:pigeonhole-proof}
Let $\cE = \{$Remark, Definition, Lemma, Proposition,
Corollary, Theorem, Proof$\}$ be the seven logical
environment types of a mathematical document
(Remark~\ref{rem:spectral-workflow}),
and let $\cF = \{1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6\}$ be the six faces
of a standard die
($|\cF| = \dim\,\mathrm{SE}(3) = 6$).
By the pigeonhole principle, any injection
$\cE \hookrightarrow \cF$ is impossible:
$|\cE| = 7 > 6 = |\cF|$.

The element that must be excluded from the die is
uniquely determined:
\emph{Proof} is the only element of $\cE$ that is not
a \emph{claim}---it is a \emph{verification} of claims.
The six claims live on the die (they are moves in the game).
The proof lives outside the die (it is the gate that
validates moves).

In the spectral retina:
the seven spectral channels are the UV decomposition
of white light.
The neural interface has a finite number of electrodes
(the ``die faces'').
If the electrode count is less than the channel count,
the encoder must compress.
The pigeonhole principle determines \emph{which}
channels get merged---and the verification channel
(the user's perceptual feedback) is always kept separate
because it is the gate, not a signal.
\end{proposition}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The Euler product of vision}
\label{app:euler-vision}

\begin{remark}[Spectral channels as Euler factors]%
\label{rem:euler-vision}
In the Euler product
$\zeta(s)^{-1} = \prod_p (1 - p^{-s})$,
each prime contributes one irreducible factor.
In the spectral MOPL retina, each wavelength band
$\lambda_k$ contributes one independent information
channel.

The analogy is exact at the level of support:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Primes} are the irreducible factors of $\Z$.
  Composites are products of primes and carry
  no new information.
\item \textbf{Spectral bands} are the irreducible factors
  of white light.
  Intermediate wavelengths are interpolations and carry
  no new information beyond the sampled bands.
\item \textbf{Cone types} (S/M/L) are the irreducible
  factors of biological colour vision.
  All perceived colours are linear combinations
  of three basis responses.
\end{itemize}

The spectral MOPL retina with $K = 7$ bands has
$7$ Euler factors.
The biological eye with $K = 3$ cone types has
$3$ Euler factors.
The encoder $E_\theta$ performs the ``multiplication''
---combining the $7$ factors into the $M$-dimensional
electrode signal, just as the Euler product combines
prime factors into $\zeta(s)^{-1}$
(Remark~\ref{rem:primon-gas}).
\end{remark}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The isomorphism table}
\label{app:iso-table}

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Concept} & \textbf{MOPL (Go)}
  & \textbf{Retina (Biology)}
  & \textbf{Golden Apple} \\
\midrule
Lattice $\Lambda$
  & $\{5,7,11,\ldots,31\}$
  & Photoreceptor grid
  & Sensor array $N \times N$ \\
UV channel
  & Small board (high resolution)
  & Foveal cones
  & Short-$\lambda$ filters \\
IR channel
  & Large board (low resolution)
  & Peripheral rods
  & Long-$\lambda$ filters \\
Framework types
  & 5 (territorial\ldots mirror)
  & 4 (1 rod + 3 cone types)
  & 7 (spectral bands) \\
RG flow
  & Pool update
  & Ganglion cell pooling ($126{:}1$)
  & Encoder $E_\theta$ \\
Gate
  & Not-lose rate
  & Perceptual threshold (JND)
  & User feedback \\
Mass gap $m_*$
  & Spectral gap of pool
  & Just-noticeable difference
  & $m_* > 0 \Leftrightarrow$ trainable \\
Expanding lattice
  & $5 \to 7 \to \cdots \to 31$
  & Fovea $\to$ periphery
  & Light/dark $\to$ reading \\
Convergence
  & Freedom Theorem
  & Brain plasticity
  & $\mathrm{NLR} \geq 1 - \epsilon$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

% ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Is the golden apple real?}
\label{app:golden-apple-verdict}

\begin{remark}[Honest assessment]\label{rem:golden-honest}
The isomorphism between MOPL and the retina is
Level~B: same mathematical skeleton (expanding lattice
$+$ RG flow $+$ spectral gate), different physical
substrate (Go board vs.\ photoreceptor array vs.\
electronic sensor).

Three conditions must hold for the golden apple to work:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{$m_* > 0$}: the user's visual cortex has
  nonzero plasticity.
  Evidence: BrainPort users learn tongue-vision in
  $\sim\!15$ minutes.
  Late-blind patients retain cortical plasticity for
  years after vision loss.
  Congenitally blind individuals show cross-modal
  plasticity (visual cortex responds to touch/sound).
  Verdict: \textsc{likely} for most patients.

\item \textbf{Sufficient electrode count}: $M$ must exceed
  the effective dimensionality of the user's visual cortex
  response.
  Current devices: Argus~II ($M = 60$),
  PRIMA ($M = 378$), Orion ($M = 60$).
  The spectral MOPL would benefit from
  $M \geq 1000$.
  Verdict: \textsc{feasible} with current
  microfabrication (Utah array: $10 \times 10 = 100$;
  Neuropixels: $384$ channels per shank,
  multi-shank: $\sim\!1000$+).

\item \textbf{MOPL training converges}: the encoder
  $E_\theta$ must find $\theta^*$ within a clinically
  acceptable training time (days to weeks, not years).
  Evidence: BrainPort learns in minutes with a
  fixed mapping.  A learnable mapping should converge
  faster (fewer wasted channels).
  Verdict: \textsc{likely}, given sufficient
  session frequency.
\end{enumerate}

The golden apple is not a metaphor.
It is a device with a parts list, a training protocol,
and a convergence theorem
(Proposition~\ref{prop:visual-convergence}).
Whether it works is an empirical question with a
mathematical answer:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\fbox{\parbox{0.85\linewidth}{\centering
  \textbf{The golden apple works if and only if
  $m_* > 0$.}\\[4pt]
  The mass gap of the user's visual cortex
  determines everything:\\
  whether training converges,
  how fast it converges,
  and what resolution is achievable.\\[4pt]
  If $m_* > 0$: the blind can see.\\
  If $m_* = 0$: no device can help.\\[4pt]
  This is the same $m_*$ as in Yang--Mills~\cite{YM54},
  in MOPL, and in the verification gate.\\
  One number. Three fields. One answer.
}}
\end{center}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Author's declaration on commercialization]%
\label{rem:golden-apple-license}
The author explicitly permits commercial use of the Golden Apple
design described in this appendix.
However, the author requires that all profits derived from
products implementing this design shall be used exclusively to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item reduce the product's price, and
\item expand production scale,
\end{enumerate}
so that more people can access the service.
Profit extraction beyond these two purposes is not authorized.
\begin{CJK}{UTF8}{gbsn}
作者声明：本附录所描述的金苹果设计可以且应当用于商业化，
但商品本身的利润只能用来降低产品价格、扩大生产规模，
使更多人能够获得此项服务。
\end{CJK}
\end{remark}
